# P17. Bianchi theta kernel for the Waldspurger lift over $\mathbb{Q}(i)$

## Goal

Construct, over $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, the theta kernel $\Theta(g, h; \phi)$ for the dual reductive pair $(\widetilde{SL}_2, PGL_2)$ that will be the input to the Bianchi Waldspurger formula in `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` Phase II.3:
$$|L(\tfrac12, \chi)|^2 = c_\chi \, \frac{|a_\chi(1)|^2}{\|\Theta_\chi\|^2}.$$
Here $\chi$ is a self-dual Hecke character of conductor $q$ on $F$, $\Theta_\chi$ is the theta lift of $\chi$ to a Maass form on $PGL_2(F)\backslash PGL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$, and $a_\chi(1)$ is its first Fourier coefficient. Success at the P17 level is a clean, formally correct statement of the kernel and an enumeration of the local data needed downstream.

## Why now

Th-chokepoint thread (P16.1.b sub-tree) escalated to Anton on 2026-05-15 01:15 because Route (a) (sign cancellation among extracted residues) is provisionally closed and Route (c) (test-function redesign $\widehat\Psi(1/2) = 0$) requires upstream test-function spec change the bot cannot make alone. The cubic-moment long-horizon project is the load-bearing alternative path to Landau IV: P11 §6.7 reduces Landau IV to a Bianchi cubic moment over $\mathbb{Q}(i)$, conditional on Petrow–Young 2020 transferring to that setting. Phase II of `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` is the foundational layer (Bianchi Waldspurger formula); chunk II.1.a is the natural starting point. Sustained chip-away on a high-EV long calculation across many sessions is in-bias per PROTOCOL.md §1.

## Initial setup

### Notation

- $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, ring of integers $\mathcal{O}_F = \mathbb{Z}[i]$.
- The unique dyadic prime is $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$, with residue field $\mathbb{F}_2$ and $|\mathfrak{p}_2| = 2$.
- Adèle ring $\mathbb{A}_F$, idèle ring $\mathbb{A}_F^\times$, $\mathbb{A}_{F,f}$ for finite adèles.
- For each place $v$ of $F$: $F_v$ local field; $\mathcal{O}_v$ ring of integers (finite $v$); $\varpi_v$ a uniformizer; $|\cdot|_v$ normalized absolute value; $\psi_v$ a fixed self-dual additive character (specified below).
- $\psi = \prod_v \psi_v$ the standard additive character of $\mathbb{A}_F / F$, normalized so that $\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i \, \mathrm{tr}_{F_\infty/\mathbb{R}}(z)} = e^{2\pi i (z + \bar z)}$ at the unique archimedean place $v = \infty$ ($F_\infty = \mathbb{C}$). At each finite place $v$, $\psi_v$ is the standard local character of **conductor $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1}$** (Tate-normalized; see Conventions sheet C2 below for the precise statement and the explicit local-different values $\mathfrak{d}_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \mathfrak{p}_2^2$, $\mathfrak{d}_v = \mathcal{O}_v$ for $\mathfrak{p} \nmid \mathfrak{p}_2$).

### Ambient groups

**DEPRECATED MOTIVATIONAL PROSE — see Conventions sheet C1 below for the operative cover statement.** The next two bullets describe the metaplectic/Direction-II Howe pair $(\widetilde{SL}_2, PGL_2)$ that was the initial motivation for the project. Per SK-2 in the Caveat block and Convention C1, this Direction is *not used in this project*. The active pair is $(SL_2, O(V_2))$ with $V_2 = E$, $\dim 2$ even, no metaplectic cover. The bullets below are preserved only for historical reference; do not import formulas from them into later chunks.

- $G = PGL_2$ as an algebraic group over $F$.
- $\widetilde{SL}_2 = \mathrm{Mp}_2$, the metaplectic double cover of $SL_2$, with the standard cocycle (Kubota over local fields, Weil's at the archimedean). Adelically: $\widetilde{SL}_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \to SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ is a non-trivial central extension by $\mu_2 = \{\pm 1\}$.
- The dual reductive pair (in Direction II, *not used here*) is $(\widetilde{SL}_2, PGL_2)$ inside $\mathrm{Sp}(W)$ for $W$ a 4-dimensional symplectic $F$-space, arising from the standard split-orthogonal decomposition $W = V_2 \otimes V_2'$ where $V_2$ is a 2-dimensional symplectic space (action of $SL_2$, after metaplectic correction giving $\widetilde{SL}_2$) and $V_2'$ is a 3-dimensional quadratic space realizing $PGL_2 = SO(V_2')$ via the conjugation action on trace-zero $2 \times 2$ matrices.

More explicitly for our application, the pair we will actually need is the *anisotropic* incarnation:

- Fix a quadratic étale algebra $E/F$. For the self-dual Hecke character $\chi$ of conductor $q$ (squarefree, coprime to $\mathfrak{p}_2$), $E$ is determined by $\chi$ via class-field theory: $E = F(\sqrt{D_\chi})$ where $D_\chi$ is the discriminant of the quadratic character $\chi^{(2)} = \chi|_{F^\times}$ when $\chi$ is restricted to scalars (or, when $\chi$ has order $> 2$, $E$ is the CM extension cut out by the kernel of $\chi$ on the inertia subgroup).
- The relevant quadratic space is $V = E$ regarded as a 2-dimensional $F$-vector space with quadratic form $Q_V(x) = \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(x) = x \bar x$, where $\bar{\cdot}$ is the non-trivial $F$-automorphism of $E$.
- $SO(V) = E^\times / F^\times = \mathrm{Res}_{E/F} \mathbb{G}_m / \mathbb{G}_m$, the "norm-1 torus" up to twist; the orthogonal group $O(V) = E^\times / F^\times \rtimes \mathrm{Gal}(E/F)$.
- The dual pair $(\widetilde{SL}_2, O(V))$ inside $\mathrm{Sp}(V \otimes V_2)$ (with $V_2$ symplectic of dimension 2) is the Howe pair. The theta lift of $\chi$ — a quasi-character of $E^\times / F^\times$ trivially extended to $O(V)$ — produces an automorphic form on $\widetilde{SL}_2$. Reciprocally, the theta lift of a Hecke–Maass form on $PGL_2$ to $\widetilde{SL}_2$ via a different choice of $V$ (a 3-dimensional split form) gives the half-integral weight forms on the metaplectic side. We are interested in the *first* direction: $\chi \mapsto \Theta_\chi$ as a theta series in the half-integral variable.

### The Schwartz–Bruhat space

Let $\phi = \otimes_v \phi_v \in \mathcal{S}(V(\mathbb{A}_F)) = \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ be a Schwartz–Bruhat function (factorizable). The Weil representation $\omega_\psi = \omega_{\psi, V}$ of $\widetilde{SL}_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$ acts on $\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ in the standard way. We will record the action of three generating elements of $\widetilde{SL}_2(F_v)$ at each place:

- $n(b) = \begin{pmatrix} 1 & b \\ 0 & 1 \end{pmatrix}$, $b \in F_v$:
$$(\omega_\psi(n(b)) \phi_v)(x) = \psi_v(b \, Q_V(x)) \, \phi_v(x) = \psi_v(b \, x \bar x) \, \phi_v(x).$$
- $m(a) = \begin{pmatrix} a & 0 \\ 0 & a^{-1} \end{pmatrix}$, $a \in F_v^\times$:
$$(\omega_\psi(m(a)) \phi_v)(x) = \chi_V(a) \, |a|_v^{\dim V / 2} \, \phi_v(a x) = \chi_V(a) \, |a|_v \, \phi_v(a x),$$
where $\chi_V$ is the quadratic character of $F_v^\times$ associated to the quadratic space $V$ (here $\chi_V = \chi_{E/F}$, the local component of the quadratic character cutting out $E$). Lifting to $\widetilde{SL}_2$ requires a half-power of $|a|_v$ that absorbs the metaplectic cocycle; see YZZ Ch. 3 §3.1.2 for the precise normalization.
- $w = \begin{pmatrix} 0 & -1 \\ 1 & 0 \end{pmatrix}$:
$$(\omega_\psi(w) \phi_v)(x) = \gamma_v(\psi_v, V) \int_{V(F_v)} \phi_v(y) \, \psi_v(- \mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(x \bar y)) \, dy = \gamma_v(\psi_v, V) \, \widehat\phi_v(x).$$
Here $\widehat{\phi}_v$ is the Fourier transform of $\phi_v$ on $V(F_v) = E_v = E \otimes_F F_v$ with respect to the bilinear form $\langle x, y \rangle = \mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(x \bar y)$, and $\gamma_v(\psi_v, V)$ is the Weil index, an 8th root of unity (a 4th root in the case at hand because $\dim V = 2$).

### The theta kernel

Following YZZ Ch. 3 §3.1, the theta kernel is the function on $\widetilde{SL}_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$ defined by
$$\Theta(g, h; \phi) := \sum_{x \in V(F)} (\omega_\psi(g) \phi)(h^{-1} x).$$
Equivalently, since $h \in O(V)(F_v)$ acts on $V(F_v)$ by orthogonal transformations and the Weil representation is invariant under the $O(V)$-action on the Schwartz space, we may write this as
$$\Theta(g, h; \phi) = \sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(g)(\rho(h) \phi))(x), \qquad (\rho(h)\phi)(y) := \phi(h^{-1} y).$$
The sum is absolutely convergent for any $\phi \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ (Schwartz decay at the archimedean place + locally constant compact-support at finite places gives absolute convergence — to be verified in II.1.b).

### The theta lift of $\chi$

Given a self-dual Hecke character $\chi \colon E^\times \backslash \mathbb{A}_E^\times \to \mathbb{C}^\times$ (so $\chi \cdot (\chi \circ \sigma) = 1$ where $\sigma$ generates $\mathrm{Gal}(E/F)$ — equivalently, $\chi$ factors through the norm to give a Hecke character of $F^\times \backslash \mathbb{A}_F^\times$ when restricted to $\mathrm{Nm}(\mathbb{A}_E^\times)$), the theta lift to $\widetilde{SL}_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ is
$$\Theta_\chi(g; \phi) := \int_{[O(V)]} \Theta(g, h; \phi) \, \chi(h) \, dh,$$
where $[O(V)] = O(V)(F)\backslash O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$, $\chi(h)$ is the extension of $\chi$ from $SO(V)(\mathbb{A}_F) = E^\times \backslash \mathbb{A}_E^\times \cdot F^\times$-ish to $O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$ via composition with the canonical projection (or trivially extended on the Galois piece, depending on conventions), and $dh$ is the Tamagawa measure on $O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$. The integral converges because $[O(V)]$ has finite volume (rank-0 anisotropic torus modulo $F^\times$).

Reciprocally, the theta lift in the *other* direction — the one that produces forms on $PGL_2$ from forms on $\widetilde{SL}_2$ — uses a 3-dimensional quadratic space $V_3 = (\mathrm{trace-zero} \, M_2(F), \det)$ on which $PGL_2 = PB^\times$ acts by conjugation (with $B$ the underlying quaternion algebra; for the split form $V_3 = M_2^{\mathrm{tr}=0}$, $B = M_2(F)$ and $PGL_2 = PGL_2$). For the Bianchi Waldspurger formula in Phase II.3, the relevant pair is $(\widetilde{SL}_2, PGL_2)$ via this $V_3$, and $\Theta_\chi$ is built by *first* lifting $\chi$ to $\widetilde{SL}_2$ via the $V_2 = E$ pair above, *then* projecting to a $PGL_2$-form via a second theta integral against a fixed test function. The full Waldspurger composition is
$$\chi \xmapsto{\theta(V_2 = E)} f_\chi \in \widetilde{SL}_2 \xmapsto{\theta(V_3 = M_2^{\mathrm{tr}=0})} \Theta_\chi \in PGL_2,$$
and the $L^2$-norm of $\Theta_\chi$ on $PGL_2(F)\backslash PGL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ relates to $|L(\tfrac12, \chi)|^2$ via the explicit formula in II.3.

### Caveat (skeptic review, 2026-05-15 session)

A Round-1 skeptic on this stub flagged three CORE issues that affect forward-looking narrative (not the kernel formula itself, which is verified):

- **(SK-1) Parity of $\dim V$ vs metaplectic correction.** For $\dim V = 2$ (even), the Weil representation $\omega_\psi$ associated to $V$ descends from $\widetilde{SL}_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ to $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ — no metaplectic cover is required when the discriminant of $V$ is a square. The parenthetical aside in the $m(a)$ entry above ("Lifting to $\widetilde{SL}_2$ requires a half-power of $|a|_v$ that absorbs the metaplectic cocycle") is misleading: for our $V = E$ with $\dim V = 2$ even, the lift is to $SL_2$, not $\widetilde{SL}_2$. The metaplectic side enters only via the $V_3 = (\mathrm{trace-zero}\; M_2, \det)$ pair ($\dim V_3 = 3$ odd). **Fix:** in II.1.c, commit to $SL_2$ vs $\widetilde{SL}_2$ once and for all based on which $V$ we actually use. Provisional resolution: for the $V = E$ ($\dim 2$) lift used to send $\chi \to f_\chi$, we work on $SL_2$, not $\widetilde{SL}_2$. Subsequent occurrences of "$\widetilde{SL}_2$" above should be read as "$SL_2$" wherever the $V = E$ pair is in scope.
- **(SK-2) Two-step lift narrative is reorganized.** The classical Shimura–Waldspurger composition is *not* "$\chi \to f_\chi$ on $\widetilde{SL}_2$ $\to \Theta_\chi$ on $PGL_2$." The correct picture has two distinct theta correspondences:
    - *Direction I* (used here): $(SL_2, O(V_2))$ with $V_2 = (E, \mathrm{Nm})$, $\dim 2$ even. Theta-lift of $\chi$ produces a cusp form $f_\chi$ on $SL_2(F)\backslash SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ (no cover). This $f_\chi$ is essentially the "automorphic induction" $\mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ — a Hecke–Maass form on $GL_2$ with $L$-function $L(s, \chi)$ at the relevant central point.
    - *Direction II* (Shimura correspondence, separate): $(\widetilde{SL}_2, O(V_3))$ with $V_3 = (M_2^{\mathrm{tr}=0}, \det)$, $\dim 3$ odd. Half-integral-weight forms on $\widetilde{SL}_2$ correspond to forms on $PGL_2$.
    The Bianchi Waldspurger formula needed in Phase II.3 of the cubic-moment project relates $|L(\tfrac12, \chi)|^2$ to a Fourier coefficient of $f_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ on $GL_2$, **not** to a half-integral-weight Fourier coefficient on $\widetilde{SL}_2$. The two-step narrative in this stub conflates these. **Fix:** drop Direction II from the Phase II workplan; the relevant lift is just Direction I, and Petrow–Young's cubic-moment method goes through the GL₂ fourth moment of automorphically-induced forms, not through half-integral weight. Update `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` Phase II description in II.1.c to reflect this.
- **(SK-3) Additive character self-duality lattice.** With $\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i (z + \bar z)}$, the self-dual lattice in $F_\infty = \mathbb{C}$ for the bilinear pairing $(z, w) \mapsto \psi_\infty(z\bar w + \bar z w) = e^{2\pi i \cdot 2\,\mathrm{Re}(z\bar w + \bar z w)/2} = e^{2\pi i (2\,\mathrm{Re}(z\bar w))}$ is *not* $\mathbb{Z}[i]$ but $\tfrac12 \mathbb{Z}[i]$. Standard YZZ conventions absorb this into the Tamagawa measure; standard Tate's-thesis conventions use $\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i \cdot \mathrm{Re}(z)}$ (so the self-dual lattice for $\mathrm{Nm}$-pairing is $\mathbb{Z}[i] / \mathfrak{d}_F^{-1}$ with $\mathfrak{d}_F = (2i)$). The choice affects: (i) the sign of the Weil index $\gamma_v(\psi_v, V)$ at finite places (changes by $\chi_V(2)$ at $\mathfrak{p} \neq \mathfrak{p}_2$); (ii) the conductor of unramified $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$. **Fix:** in II.1.c (chunk Q2 above), commit to YZZ-doubled-trace once and for all and propagate consistently. Default: YZZ convention $\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i (z + \bar z)}$, conductor of $\psi_v = \mathfrak{d}_v^{-1}$ at finite $v$ (Tate convention; not "$\mathfrak{d}_v$" as written above — this is a typo to be fixed).

These three caveats are all forward-looking: the kernel formula in Proposition II.1.a (next subsection) is independent of them. SK-2 in particular requires updating `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` to drop the Direction II / half-integral-weight detour from Phase II — done in this session.

### Statement (II.1.a — kernel definition only)

**Proposition (II.1.a).** Let $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, $E/F$ a quadratic étale algebra, $V = E$ as a 2-dimensional $F$-quadratic space with form $Q_V(x) = x\bar x = \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(x)$. Let $\psi$ be the standard YZZ additive character of $\mathbb{A}_F/F$ ($\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i (z + \bar z)}$, $\psi_v$ at finite $v$ of conductor $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1}$ — Tate normalization — for $v$ corresponding to a prime $\mathfrak{p}$ of $\mathcal{O}_F$). Because $\dim V = 2$ is even and $\mathrm{disc}(V) = \mathrm{disc}(E/F)$ is a fixed element of $F^\times / (F^\times)^2$, the Weil representation $\omega_\psi = \omega_{\psi, V}$ descends from $\widetilde{SL}_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ to $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$; we work on $SL_2$. For $\phi \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ factorizable, the theta kernel
$$\Theta(g, h; \phi) = \sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(g) \phi)(h^{-1} x), \qquad (g, h) \in SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F),$$
is a well-defined function on $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$. (Absolute convergence and $SL_2(F) \times O(V)(F)$-invariance are deferred to II.1.b.)

This is the YZZ Ch. 3 §3.1 setup, specialized to $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ and $V = E$ with $E/F$ quadratic. The only $F$-specific inputs are: (i) the additive character normalization at the unique archimedean place ($\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i (z + \bar z)}$); (ii) the local different at $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$ is $\mathfrak{p}_2 \cdot (\text{unit})$ (since $\mathfrak{d}_F = (2i)$ has $\mathfrak{p}_2$-valuation 2, and the local different is $\mathfrak{p}_2^{2-1} = \mathfrak{p}_2$ accounting for the ramification of $F_v / \mathbb{Q}_2$). The downstream lift is $SL_2$, NOT $\widetilde{SL}_2$ — see Caveat SK-1/SK-2 above.

### Statement (II.1.b — absolute convergence + automorphy)

**Proposition (II.1.b).** With the data of Proposition II.1.a in force, for every factorizable Schwartz–Bruhat $\phi = \otimes_v \phi_v \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ and every $(g, h) \in SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$:

1. (Absolute convergence.) The series
$$\Theta(g, h; \phi) = \sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(g) \phi)(h^{-1} x)$$
converges absolutely and uniformly on compact subsets of $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$.

2. (Left $SL_2(F)$-automorphy.) For all $\gamma \in SL_2(F)$,
$$\Theta(\gamma g, h; \phi) = \Theta(g, h; \phi).$$

3. (Left $O(V)(F)$-automorphy.) For all $\gamma' \in O(V)(F)$,
$$\Theta(g, \gamma' h; \phi) = \Theta(g, h; \phi).$$

In particular, $\Theta(\cdot, \cdot; \phi)$ descends to a smooth function on $[SL_2] \times [O(V)] := (SL_2(F) \backslash SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)) \times (O(V)(F) \backslash O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F))$.

### Proof of II.1.b (citing YZZ Ch. 3 §3.1.3 / §3.2)

We verify the three claims in order. None of the arguments is original to this setting: YZZ Ch. 3 §3.1 (esp. Prop. 3.2 and the discussion preceding it) gives the proof over a general number field $F$ with a quadratic space $V$, and our specialization $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, $V = E$ ($\dim 2$, even) introduces no new analytic difficulty.

**(1) Absolute convergence.** Decompose $\mathbb{A}_E = E_\infty \oplus \mathbb{A}_{E,f}$ where $E_\infty = E \otimes_{\mathbb{Q}} \mathbb{R} = \mathbb{C}^2$ (a two-dimensional $\mathbb{C}$-vector space, since $[E:\mathbb{Q}] = 4$ and $E_\infty$ is the product over the archimedean places of $E$, which sit above the unique archimedean place of $F$). Write $\phi = \phi_\infty \otimes \phi_f$ with $\phi_\infty \in \mathcal{S}(E_\infty)$ Schwartz and $\phi_f = \otimes_{v < \infty} \phi_v$ a finite tensor product of locally constant compactly-supported functions on $\mathbb{A}_{E,f}$.

For fixed $(g, h)$ in any compact $K \subset SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$, the Weil representation acts continuously on $\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ (this is standard; see e.g. YZZ §3.1.2 or Weil 1964). Concretely:

- *Archimedean factor.* $(\omega_\psi(g_\infty) \phi_\infty)(h_\infty^{-1} \cdot)$ remains Schwartz on $E_\infty$, with seminorms bounded uniformly for $(g_\infty, h_\infty)$ in a compact set. (Weil rep is a unitary rep of $SL_2(\mathbb{R})^2 = SL_2(F_\infty)$ on $L^2(E_\infty)$ that preserves $\mathcal{S}(E_\infty)$ and is continuous in the Fréchet topology — see Folland 1989, "Harmonic Analysis in Phase Space," Ch. 4.)
- *Finite factor.* Let $K_f \subset SL_2(\mathbb{A}_{F,f}) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_{F,f})$ be the projection of $K$ to the finite-adèlic factor. By continuity of the Weil representation as a map $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_{F,f}) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_{F,f}) \to \mathrm{Aut}(\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_{E,f}))$ in the natural topology on locally constant compactly-supported functions, the orbit
$$\{(\omega_\psi(g_f)\phi_f)(h_f^{-1} \cdot) : (g_f, h_f) \in K_f\}$$
is bounded in $\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_{E,f})$. Concretely: there exists a single $\mathcal{O}_F$-lattice $L \subset E$ with $L_f := L \otimes_{\mathcal{O}_F} \widehat{\mathcal{O}_F}$ such that $\mathrm{supp}((\omega_\psi(g_f)\phi_f)(h_f^{-1} \cdot)) \subset L_f$ for all $(g_f, h_f) \in K_f$, and the values are bounded uniformly on $L_f$. (This uses that $K_f$ is compact in the finite-adèlic topology, hence contained in $SL_2(\mathcal{O}_{F,v}) \times O(V)(\mathcal{O}_{F,v})$ at almost all $v$, where $\omega_\psi$ fixes the standard unramified vector; at the finitely many remaining places where $K_f$ is non-trivial, compactness + the fact that $\omega_\psi$ at finite places is given by finite linear combinations of "scale-by-$a$" and "Fourier transform" operators on $\mathcal{S}(E_v)$ — both of which preserve the *family* of $\mathcal{O}_v$-lattices of $E_v$ — bounds the support. This is the substance of YZZ §3.1.2.)

The sum $\sum_{x \in E}$ runs over the discrete subgroup $E \hookrightarrow \mathbb{A}_E$. Project to $E_\infty$: this is the embedding of $E$ as a $\mathbb{Z}$-lattice of rank 4 in $E_\infty \cong \mathbb{C}^2 \cong \mathbb{R}^4$ via the standard archimedean embeddings. Combined with the finite-adèlic constraint $x \in L$ (cutting $E$ down to the sub-lattice $E \cap L$ of finite index in $E$), the sum reduces to a sum over a finite union of cosets of a single $\mathbb{Z}$-lattice of rank 4 in $E_\infty$. Schwartz decay of $(\omega_\psi(g_\infty)\phi_\infty)(h_\infty^{-1}\cdot)$ on $E_\infty \cong \mathbb{R}^4$ (faster than any polynomial) gives absolute convergence, uniform on compacta.

(For our specific test functions in II.1.d — Gaussian at $\infty$, characteristic functions of integral lattices at finite places — convergence is immediate: $\sum_{x \in \mathcal{O}_E} e^{-2\pi x\bar x}$ converges as a classical Gaussian theta sum.)

**(2) Left $SL_2(F)$-automorphy.** It suffices to check on a set of generators of $SL_2(F)$. By the Bruhat decomposition, $SL_2(F)$ is generated by the upper unipotents $n(b)$ with $b \in F$, the diagonal elements $m(a)$ with $a \in F^\times$, and the Weyl element $w$. The crucial fact is that for each generator $\gamma$, summation over $V(F) = E$ of $\omega_\psi(\gamma)\phi'$ equals summation of $\phi'$, for any $\phi' \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$:

*(2a) Generator $n(b)$, $b \in F$.* Recall from the kernel definition: $(\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi')(x) = \psi(b\,Q_V(x))\phi'(x)$. For $x \in V(F) = E$, $Q_V(x) = x\bar x \in F$, so $b \, Q_V(x) \in F$. But $\psi \colon \mathbb{A}_F/F \to \mathbb{C}^\times$, so $\psi|_F = 1$. Therefore $\psi(b\,Q_V(x)) = 1$ for every $x \in E$, and
$$\sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi')(x) = \sum_{x \in E} \phi'(x).$$

*(2b) Generator $m(a)$, $a \in F^\times$.* $(\omega_\psi(m(a))\phi')(x) = \chi_V(a) \, |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \, \phi'(ax)$, where $|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} = \prod_v |a|_v$ is the idelic absolute value and $\chi_V \colon \mathbb{A}_F^\times \to \{\pm 1\}$ is the quadratic Hecke character cut out by $V$.

*Normalization convention.* Throughout, $|\cdot|_v$ is the *module character* of $F_v$ — i.e., the Radon–Nikodym derivative of $a$-translation on $F_v$ relative to Haar measure. At the archimedean place $v = \infty$, $F_v = \mathbb{C}$ and the module character is $|z|_\infty = z\bar z = |z|_{\mathbb{C}}^2$ (the *square* of the usual complex absolute value). At finite $v$ above a rational prime $p$ with residue field $k_v$, $|\varpi_v|_v = (\#k_v)^{-1}$. This is the standard convention (Tate's thesis, Weil "Basic Number Theory" Ch. I §2) under which Artin's product formula $\prod_v |a|_v = 1$ holds for $a \in F^\times$.

Both factors are *trivial on $F^\times$*:
- $|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} = 1$ for $a \in F^\times$ by Artin's product formula (in the module-character normalization just stated).
- $\chi_V|_{F^\times} = 1$ because $\chi_V$ is a Hecke character (idele class character), hence trivial on principal idèles.

By the change of variables $y = ax$ on $V(F) = E$ (a bijection $E \xrightarrow{\sim} E$ since $a \in F^\times \subset E^\times$ acts by multiplication):
$$\sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(m(a))\phi')(x) = \chi_V(a) |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \sum_{x \in E} \phi'(ax) = 1 \cdot 1 \cdot \sum_{y \in E} \phi'(y).$$

*(2c) Generator $w$.* $(\omega_\psi(w)\phi')(x) = \gamma_\psi(V) \cdot \widehat{\phi'}(x)$, where $\widehat{\phi'}$ is the Fourier transform on $V(\mathbb{A}_F) = \mathbb{A}_E$ with respect to the symmetric bilinear form $\langle x, y\rangle = \mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(x\bar y)$, and $\gamma_\psi(V) = \prod_v \gamma_v(\psi_v, V)$ is the global Weil index. Two non-trivial facts intervene:

- *Weil's product formula for the global Weil index:* $\gamma_\psi(V) = 1$ for any $F$-rational quadratic space $V$. This is Weil 1964 §29 (Theorem 5), equivalently the global Hasse–Minkowski / Hilbert reciprocity statement: the local Weil indices $\gamma_v(\psi_v, V) \in \mu_8$ satisfy $\prod_v \gamma_v(\psi_v, V) = 1$, because they are governed by Hasse invariants of $V$, which obey reciprocity.
- *Adelic Poisson summation* on $V(\mathbb{A}_F) = \mathbb{A}_E$: for any Schwartz–Bruhat $\phi' \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$,
$$\sum_{x \in V(F)} \phi'(x) = \sum_{x \in V(F)} \widehat{\phi'}(x).$$
Justification, separating the two distinct ingredients (annihilator identity vs volume normalization):

*(Step A — annihilator identity, $E^\perp = E$.)* Define the global character $\Psi \colon \mathbb{A}_E \to \mathbb{C}^\times$ by $\Psi(x) = \psi(\mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(x))$. The bilinear pairing $\langle x, y\rangle := \Psi(x\bar y) = \psi(\mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(x\bar y))$ is continuous, non-degenerate, and identifies $\mathbb{A}_E$ with its Pontryagin dual via $y \mapsto \langle \cdot, y\rangle$. Since $\mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(E) \subset F$ and $\psi|_F = 1$, we have $\Psi|_E = 1$, so $E \subset E^\perp$. The reverse inclusion $E^\perp \subset E$ is the global self-duality theorem (Tate's thesis Lemma 4.1.4; equivalently Weil "Basic Number Theory" Ch. VII §2 Thm 3): for a number field $K$, the standard additive character $\psi_K$ (chosen so that the local components have conductor $\mathfrak{d}_{K/\mathbb{Q}, v}^{-1}$ at each finite $v$) yields $K^\perp = K$ inside $\mathbb{A}_K$ under $(x,y) \mapsto \psi_K(xy)$. The mechanism is that the local-conductor discrepancies (where the local annihilator of $\mathcal{O}_{K,v}$ is $\mathfrak{d}_{K/\mathbb{Q}, v}^{-1}$, not $\mathcal{O}_{K, v}$) cancel globally via the product formula for the different — at finitely many places the local annihilator strictly contains $\mathcal{O}_{K, v}$, but the corresponding global element does not lie in $K$ unless the *adelic combination* respects $K$, which forces equality. Applied to $K = E$ with $\psi_E := \Psi$: the local components of $\psi_E$ are $\psi_v \circ \mathrm{tr}_{E_v/F_v}$, which have the correct conductor $\mathfrak{d}_{E_v/\mathbb{Q}_p, v}^{-1}$ when our $\psi$ has the YZZ/Tate-standard conductor $\mathfrak{d}_{F_v/\mathbb{Q}_p, v}^{-1}$ at each $v$ (Caveat SK-3 above commits to this). Conclusion: $E^\perp = E$ in $\mathbb{A}_E$.

*(Step B — volume normalization gives the constant 1.)* By the general adelic Poisson summation theorem (Weil 1964 §VII Thm 1): for any continuous self-dual pairing on a locally compact abelian group $G$ and any discrete cocompact $\Lambda$ with $\Lambda^\perp = \Lambda$,
$$\sum_{x \in \Lambda} \phi'(x) = \mathrm{vol}(G/\Lambda)^{-1} \sum_{y \in \Lambda} \widehat{\phi'}(y).$$
Applied with $G = \mathbb{A}_E$, $\Lambda = E$, and the Tamagawa-normalized Haar measure on $\mathbb{A}_E$ for which $\mathrm{vol}(\mathbb{A}_E/E) = 1$: the constant in front is 1, yielding $\sum_E \phi' = \sum_E \widehat{\phi'}$. (Tamagawa normalization is the YZZ-standard convention; see YZZ §3.1.2.)

Combining:
$$\sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(w)\phi')(x) = \gamma_\psi(V) \sum_{x \in E} \widehat{\phi'}(x) = 1 \cdot \sum_{x \in E} \phi'(x).$$

*(2d) Conclusion of (2).* The three identities (2a)–(2c) say: for each generator $\gamma \in \{n(b), m(a), w\}$ of $SL_2(F)$, the map $\phi' \mapsto \sum_{x \in E} \phi'(x)$ on $\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ is $\omega_\psi(\gamma)$-invariant. By multiplicativity of $\omega_\psi$ (it is a representation), the map is invariant under all of $SL_2(F)$. Applying this to $\phi' = \omega_\psi(g)(\rho(h^{-1})\phi)$, where $\rho(h)\phi(y) := \phi(h^{-1}y)$, gives
$$\sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(\gamma g)\phi)(h^{-1}x) = \sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(h^{-1}x), \quad \gamma \in SL_2(F).$$
This is the left $SL_2(F)$-automorphy claim.

**(3) Left $O(V)(F)$-automorphy.** For $\gamma' \in O(V)(F)$, $\gamma'$ acts on $V(F) = E$ by an $F$-linear orthogonal transformation, hence permutes $E$ as a set. Thus
$$\Theta(g, \gamma' h; \phi) = \sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)((\gamma' h)^{-1} x) = \sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(h^{-1}(\gamma'^{-1} x)).$$
Substituting $x' = \gamma'^{-1} x$ (a bijection $E \to E$):
$$= \sum_{x' \in E} (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(h^{-1} x') = \Theta(g, h; \phi). \qquad \blacksquare$$

### Remarks on II.1.b

- **(R1) The dyadic prime $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$.** Nothing in the proof of II.1.b is sensitive to $\mathfrak{p}_2$: absolute convergence is a soft analytic statement (lattice + Schwartz decay + locally-constant compact support); the $SL_2(F)$-automorphy uses only $\psi|_F = 1$, the product formula, idele-class triviality of $\chi_V$, and Weil's reciprocity for $\gamma_\psi(V) = 1$. All four are global facts. The dyadic place enters quantitatively in II.1.c (cocycle normalization) and II.2.a (Fourier expansion at $\mathfrak{p}_2$); for the kernel-existence statement (II.1.b), it is invisible.

- **(R2) Even-$\dim V$ simplification.** Because $\dim V = 2$ is even and we work on $SL_2$ (not $\widetilde{SL}_2$), there is no metaplectic-cocycle issue in (2). For the $V_3 = (M_2^{\mathrm{tr}=0}, \det)$ pair with $\dim V_3 = 3$ odd (Direction II, *not* used in this project — see SK-2 in the caveat above), the analog of (2) requires lifting $SL_2(F)$ through the metaplectic cocycle, which is a separate computation. Our setting bypasses this.

- **(R3) Weil's product formula vs Hilbert reciprocity.** The fact $\prod_v \gamma_v(\psi_v, V) = 1$ for an $F$-rational quadratic space $V$ has multiple equivalent formulations. In Weil 1964 §29 it is Theorem 5 (the "product formula for the Weil index"). It is equivalent, via the Hasse–Witt invariant of $V$, to Hilbert reciprocity: $\prod_v c_v(V) = 1$ where $c_v(V) \in \{\pm 1\}$ is the local Hasse invariant. For $V = E$ with $E/F$ quadratic (the case at hand), $c_v(V) = (D_E, D_E)_v$ where $D_E \in F^\times$ is a representative of $\mathrm{disc}(E/F)$ in $F^\times/(F^\times)^2$, and the Hilbert symbol satisfies $\prod_v (a, b)_v = 1$ by quadratic reciprocity.

- **(R4) Smoothness.** The function $(g, h) \mapsto \Theta(g, h; \phi)$ is *smooth* on $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$ (i.e., infinitely differentiable in the archimedean variables, locally constant in the finite-adèlic variables) because: (i) each term $(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(h^{-1}x)$ is smooth in $(g, h)$ when $\phi$ is, and (ii) absolute and uniform-on-compacta convergence of the series (and all its derivatives, by the same Schwartz/lattice argument applied to derivatives of $\phi$) preserves smoothness. This will be needed in II.2.a when we Fourier-expand along the unipotent radical.

### What this delivers and what is deferred

- *Delivered (II.1.b):* well-definedness as a measurable function, absolute convergence, smoothness, and left $SL_2(F) \times O(V)(F)$-invariance. The kernel descends to $[SL_2] \times [O(V)]$.
- *Deferred:*
    - *Moderate growth* of $\Theta(g, h; \phi)$ as $g$ varies (for use in the theta-integral against $\chi$): YZZ §3.2 Prop. 3.4 / Borel–Garland. This is needed for the convergence of $\Theta_\chi(g; \phi) = \int_{[O(V)]} \Theta(g, h; \phi) \chi(h)\,dh$ — postponed to II.1.e (new chunk to be added).
    - *Equivariance under the right $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V)(\mathbb{A}_F)$-action* of $\omega_\psi$: this is by construction (the action is built into the kernel formula). No separate verification needed.

### Conventions sheet (II.1.c — locked for all of Phase II)

This subsection collects the three convention commitments flagged by the II.1.a (SK-1, SK-2, SK-3) and II.1.b (module character + Tamagawa) skeptic loops. **All subsequent Phase II chunks (II.1.d, II.1.e, II.2, II.3, II.4) cite this sheet by reference.** If a later chunk needs to override a commitment locally, it must do so explicitly and state the conversion factor relative to this sheet.

**Convention C1 (cover — locks SK-1).** For the dual reductive pair $(SL_2, O(V_2))$ with $V_2 = (E, \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F})$, $\dim_F V_2 = 2$, we work on **$SL_2$**, not on the metaplectic double cover $\widetilde{SL}_2 = \mathrm{Mp}_2$. Reason: $\dim V_2$ is even, so the Weil representation $\omega_{\psi, V_2}$ descends from $\widetilde{SL}_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ to $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ via a canonical splitting (Kudla 1996 "Notes on the local theta correspondence" Thm 3.1; Rao 1993; YZZ Ch. 3 §3.1.2 Remark). The Weil-rep formula for $\omega_{\psi, V}(m(a))$ on $SL_2$ involves the quadratic character

$$
\chi_V \colon F^\times/(F^\times)^2 \to \{\pm 1\}, \qquad \chi_V = \chi_{(-1)^{\dim V/2} \det V}
$$

— i.e., the quadratic Hecke character cutting out the étale quadratic algebra $F\big(\sqrt{(-1)^{\dim V/2}\det V}\big)/F$. (Here $\det V$ is the Gram determinant of $V$ in any $F$-basis, modulo squares; the sign $(-1)^{\dim V/2}$ is *not* absorbable into $\det V$ in general and matters for the Hilbert symbol that produces the cocycle.) For $V = V_2 = (E, \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F})$ with $E = F(\sqrt{D_E})$ and $D_E$ a representative of $\mathrm{disc}(E/F)$:

- Pick the $F$-basis $\{1, \delta\}$ of $E$ with $\delta^2 = D_E$ and $\bar\delta = -\delta$. The bilinear form $B(x, y) = \mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(x \bar y)$ has Gram matrix $\mathrm{diag}(2, -2 D_E)$, hence $\det V_2 = -4 D_E \equiv -D_E$ in $F^\times/(F^\times)^2$.
- $(-1)^{\dim V_2/2} = (-1)^1 = -1$, so $(-1)^{\dim V_2/2} \det V_2 \equiv -\!\cdot\! -D_E = D_E$ in $F^\times/(F^\times)^2$.
- Hence $\chi_{V_2} = \chi_{D_E} = \chi_{E/F}$, the standard quadratic Hecke character of $F^\times/\mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(E^\times)$ cutting out $E$.

Two sign flips ($(-1)^{\dim V/2}$ and $\det V_2 = -D_E$) cancel for $V_2$ specifically — but the general statement *does* carry the $(-1)^{\dim V/2}$ factor, and any future computation that reads $\chi_V$ off of $\det V$ alone (without the parity correction) would lose a sign for an even-dim quadratic space with $\dim V \equiv 2 \pmod 4$.

Consequences for forward-looking chunks:
- The $m(a)$ Weil-rep formula is $(\omega_\psi(m(a))\phi)(x) = \chi_V(a)\,|a|_v\,\phi(ax)$ (no metaplectic half-power; $\dim V / 2 = 1$ for our $V$).
- The Bianchi Waldspurger formula in II.3 expresses $|L(\tfrac12, \chi)|^2$ as a Fourier coefficient of $f_\chi := \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ — a *Hecke–Maass cuspform on $GL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$*, obtained from $\Theta_\chi$ on $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ by the standard $SL_2 \to GL_2$ extension (central character $\chi_V$). No half-integral-weight forms enter (this is the SK-2 commitment, recorded in `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md`).
- The metaplectic / half-integral-weight Shimura correspondence (Direction II in the SK-2 caveat) is **not used in this project**. Any text in P17 referring to "$\widetilde{SL}_2$" that predates this conventions sheet should be read with "$\widetilde{SL}_2$" replaced by "$SL_2$" wherever the $V = V_2 = E$ pair is in scope.

**Convention C2 (additive character and local conductor — locks SK-3).** Fix once and for all the standard global additive character $\psi = \prod_v \psi_v \colon \mathbb{A}_F / F \to \mathbb{C}^\times$ with components

$$
\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i\,\mathrm{tr}_{\mathbb{C}/\mathbb{R}}(z)} = e^{2\pi i (z + \bar z)}, \qquad z \in F_\infty = \mathbb{C},
$$

and at each finite place $v$ of $F$ corresponding to a prime $\mathfrak{p}$ of $\mathcal{O}_F$, $\psi_v$ is **the unique additive character of $F_v$ with conductor $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1}$** (Tate normalization). Explicitly:

- $\psi_v$ is trivial on $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1} = \{x \in F_v : \mathrm{tr}_{F_v/\mathbb{Q}_p}(x \,\mathcal{O}_v) \subset \mathbb{Z}_p\}$, the inverse local different.
- $\psi_v$ is non-trivial on $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1} \mathfrak{p}_v^{-1}$ (i.e., $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1}$ is the largest fractional ideal on which $\psi_v$ is trivial).
- Equivalently, $\psi_v$ is the composition $F_v \xrightarrow{\mathrm{tr}_{F_v/\mathbb{Q}_p}} \mathbb{Q}_p \xrightarrow{\psi_{\mathbb{Q}_p}} \mathbb{C}^\times$ where $\psi_{\mathbb{Q}_p}$ is the standard character of $\mathbb{Q}_p$ with conductor $\mathbb{Z}_p$ (= $\mathfrak{d}_{\mathbb{Q}_p}^{-1}$ since $\mathbb{Q}_p$ is unramified over itself).

For $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ specifically, the global different is $\mathfrak{d}_F = (2i) = \mathfrak{p}_2^2$ as an ideal of $\mathcal{O}_F$ (since $2i = -i(1+i)^2 \cdot i^2 \cdot \text{unit}$, i.e., $(2i) = (1+i)^2$ up to units). At each finite place:

- $v = \mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$ (dyadic, ramified over $\mathbb{Q}_2$, ramification index $e = 2$, residue degree $f = 1$): the local different is $\mathfrak{d}_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \mathfrak{p}_2^2$ (so $\mathfrak{d}_{\mathfrak{p}_2}^{-1} = \mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}$). *Verification via the minimal polynomial:* $\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}} = \mathbb{Z}_2[i]$ is generated over $\mathbb{Z}_2$ by $i$, with minimal polynomial $f(x) = x^2 + 1$, so $\mathfrak{d}_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = (f'(i)) = (2i) = \mathfrak{p}_2^2$ (using $(1+i)^2 = 2i$). *Verification via Serre's lower bound:* for a totally ramified extension with $e \geq 1$, $v(\mathfrak{d}) \geq e - 1$, with equality iff the ramification is tame; here $p = 2$ and $\gcd(e, p) = 2$ so the ramification is wild and the inequality is strict — the bound $v(\mathfrak{d}) \geq 2$ is sharp here.
- $v = \mathfrak{p}$, $\mathfrak{p} \nmid \mathfrak{p}_2$ (odd primes, unramified over their rational prime): $\mathfrak{d}_v = \mathcal{O}_v$ and $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1} = \mathcal{O}_v$. Hence $\psi_v$ has conductor $\mathcal{O}_v$ (the standard unramified character).

This is the YZZ / Tate convention. Earlier text in §Initial setup of this file said "$\psi_v$ is the standard local character with conductor $\mathfrak{d}_v = \mathcal{O}_v$" — that is a typo / pre-conventions-sheet placeholder. The correct statement is *$\psi_v$ has conductor $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1}$*; the conductor and the local different are related by inversion. Audit note in §"Audit corrigenda" below.

**Convention C3 (module character + Tamagawa measures).** At every place $v$ of $F$, the symbol $|\cdot|_v$ denotes the **module character** of $F_v$ — i.e., the Radon–Nikodym derivative of $a$-translation on $F_v$ relative to Haar measure (Weil, "Basic Number Theory" Ch. I §2). Concretely:

- At $v = \infty$: $|z|_\infty := z\bar z = |z|_{\mathbb{C}}^2$ — the **square** of the usual complex absolute value. (Not $|z|_{\mathbb{C}}$.)
- At finite $v$ with residue field $k_v$ and uniformizer $\varpi_v$: $|\varpi_v|_v := (\#k_v)^{-1}$. For $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ at $\mathfrak{p}_2$: $\#k_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 2$, $|1+i|_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1/2$.

This is the unique normalization under which Artin's product formula

$$
\prod_v |a|_v = 1 \quad\text{for all } a \in F^\times
$$

holds. It is the convention used implicitly in the $m(a)$-automorphy computation of II.1.b.

For the global measure on $\mathbb{A}_F$ and on $\mathbb{A}_E = V(\mathbb{A}_F)$: we fix the **Tamagawa normalization**

$$
\mathrm{vol}(\mathbb{A}_F / F) = 1, \qquad \mathrm{vol}(\mathbb{A}_E / E) = 1.
$$

Concretely on $\mathbb{A}_F$: at $v = \infty$, take $|dz \wedge d\bar z| = 2\,dx\,dy$ in real coordinates $z = x + iy$ on $F_\infty = \mathbb{C}$ (this is "twice ordinary Lebesgue measure" on $\mathbb{C} \cong \mathbb{R}^2$); at each finite $v$, take the Haar measure giving $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_v) = |\mathfrak{d}_v|_v^{1/2} = (\#k_v)^{-v_v(\mathfrak{d}_v)/2}$. This is the **self-dual Haar measure for $\psi_v$** (the unique Haar measure under which the Fourier inversion formula on $F_v$ holds with constant 1 when $\psi_v$ has conductor $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1}$).

Under this normalization, the standard adelic identity is

$$
|\mathfrak{d}_F|_{\mathbb{A}_F} := \prod_v |\mathfrak{d}_v|_v = |\mathrm{disc}(F)|_\mathbb{Q}^{-1},
$$

where $|\cdot|_\mathbb{Q}$ is the ordinary archimedean absolute value of the integer $\mathrm{disc}(F)$. For $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$: $|\mathfrak{d}_F|_{\mathbb{A}_F} = |\mathfrak{p}_2^2|_{\mathfrak{p}_2} \cdot 1 = (1/2)^2 = 1/4$; $|\mathrm{disc}(F)|_\mathbb{Q} = |-4| = 4$; the identity gives $1/4 = 1/4$ ✓. The covolume of $F$ in $\mathbb{A}_F$ under the self-dual measure is then

$$
\mathrm{vol}(\mathbb{A}_F / F) = 1
$$

— this is the standard Tamagawa fact ("the Tamagawa number of $\mathbb{G}_a$ over a number field is 1"; Weil 1964 §V Thm 2). Equivalently, in the *Lebesgue-on-$\mathbb{R}^{[F:\mathbb{Q}]} = \mathbb{R}^2$* normalization where archimedean $|dz \wedge d\bar z|$ is replaced by ordinary Lebesgue $dx\,dy$, the covolume becomes $|\mathrm{disc}(F)|^{1/2} = 2$ — but we use the self-dual measure throughout.

On $\mathbb{A}_E$: similarly, the local Haar measures at finite $v$ assign $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{E_v}) = |\mathfrak{d}_{E_v/\mathbb{Q}_p}|_v^{1/2}$ (taking the local different of $E_v / \mathbb{Q}_p$, not of $E_v/F_v$), and at the archimedean place $E_\infty \cong \mathbb{C}^2$ take $|dz_1 \wedge d\bar z_1| \wedge |dz_2 \wedge d\bar z_2|$. Tamagawa $\mathrm{vol}(\mathbb{A}_E/E) = 1$ holds. (Reference: Weil 1964 §VII or YZZ §3.1.2.)

This is the normalization under which the adelic Poisson summation formula on $\mathbb{A}_E$ used in step (2c) of the II.1.b proof has constant **exactly 1**:

$$
\sum_{x \in E} \phi'(x) = \sum_{x \in E} \widehat{\phi'}(x), \quad \phi' \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E).
$$

### Audit corrigenda (in-place, against the conventions sheet)

After locking C1–C3, two pieces of forward-looking text earlier in this file were inconsistent with the locked conventions. Both are corrected **in place** above (not just flagged):

- (a) §Initial setup, "Adèle ring" bullet (line ~21): the typo "$\psi_v$ has conductor $\mathfrak{d}_v = \mathcal{O}_v$" is corrected in place to "conductor $\mathfrak{d}_v^{-1}$" with a forward-pointer to Convention C2 for the explicit local-different values. Reason: the original wording would mislead a reader who consults §Initial setup linearly without reaching the Conventions sheet.

- (b) §Ambient groups (lines ~25–27): a "DEPRECATED MOTIVATIONAL PROSE" banner is inserted at the head of the subsection, flagging the $(\widetilde{SL}_2, PGL_2)$ description as Direction-II historical material that is *not used in this project*. Per Convention C1 + SK-2 in the Caveat block. The Direction-II bullets are preserved for historical reference but explicitly marked non-operational. The active pair is $(SL_2, O(V_2))$.

No other text in this file requires correction against the conventions sheet — the II.1.a Proposition statement and the II.1.b Proposition + proof are already written in the locked conventions (this is what the II.1.b skeptic loop enforced).

### Test function $\phi$ (II.1.d — unramified part locked)

For the Bianchi Waldspurger formula at level $q$ (squarefree, coprime to $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$), the input to $\Theta_\chi(g; \phi) = \int_{[O(V)]} \Theta(g, h; \phi) \chi(h) \, dh$ is a factorizable Schwartz–Bruhat function
$$\phi = \phi_\infty \otimes \phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2} \otimes \bigotimes_{\mathfrak{p} \mid q} \phi_\mathfrak{p} \otimes \bigotimes_{\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2} \phi_\mathfrak{p} \;\in\; \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E).$$

This chunk fixes the two **unramified** factors:
- the archimedean factor $\phi_\infty \in \mathcal{S}(E_\infty)$ ($E_\infty \cong \mathbb{C}^2$);
- the finite factors $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ at all primes $\mathfrak{p}$ of $\mathcal{O}_F$ coprime to $q\mathfrak{p}_2$.

The two **ramified** factors —
- $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ at primes $\mathfrak{p} \mid q$ (the "newform" choice, Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 §1 analog), and
- $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ at the dyadic prime (the Pitale–Saha–Schmidt / paramodular choice)

— are deferred. The $q$-newform choice depends on the local conductor of $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ and on a $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariance prescription; deferred to a sub-chunk II.1.d.bis or merged into II.2 (Fourier expansion at level $q$). The dyadic choice requires local representation theory at $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2$ (wild ramification of the base field, $e = 2$, $p = 2$); deferred to II.4.

All normalizations cite the Conventions sheet C1–C3 above.

**(I) The archimedean factor $\phi_\infty$.**

Coordinates. Identify $E_\infty := E \otimes_\mathbb{Q} \mathbb{R}$ with $\mathbb{C} \times \mathbb{C}$ via the two embeddings $\sigma_1, \sigma_2 \colon E \hookrightarrow \mathbb{C}$ extending the unique embedding $F = \mathbb{Q}(i) \hookrightarrow \mathbb{C}$: for $\xi \in E$, write $\xi \mapsto (z_1, z_2) := (\sigma_1 \xi, \sigma_2 \xi)$. Then $E_\infty = \mathbb{C}^2$ as an $\mathbb{R}$-algebra; as an $F_\infty$-algebra it is $\mathbb{C} \oplus \mathbb{C}$ (split). The $F$-linear Galois involution $\bar{\cdot} \in \mathrm{Gal}(E/F)$ extends to $E_\infty$ as the **swap** $(z_1, z_2) \mapsto (z_2, z_1)$ (since both archimedean places of $E$ above $\infty_F$ are swapped by the non-trivial element of $\mathrm{Gal}(E/F)$). In particular:
- $\mathrm{Nm}_{E_\infty/F_\infty}(x) = z_1 z_2 \in F_\infty = \mathbb{C}$ — a $\mathbb{C}$-valued (not real) quadratic form;
- $\mathrm{tr}_{E_\infty/F_\infty}(x) = z_1 + z_2 \in \mathbb{C}$.

The naïve formula "$\phi_\infty(x) = e^{-2\pi x\bar x}$" — if read with $\bar{\cdot}$ meaning the $F$-Galois involution — would give $e^{-2\pi z_1 z_2}$, which is complex-valued and not Schwartz. The correct positive Gaussian uses **complex conjugation in each archimedean place** separately. We define:

$$\boxed{\quad \phi_\infty(x) := \exp\!\bigl(-2\pi \, q_\infty(x)\bigr), \qquad q_\infty(x) := |\sigma_1 x|_\mathbb{C}^2 + |\sigma_2 x|_\mathbb{C}^2 = z_1 \overline{z_1}^{\mathbb{C}} + z_2 \overline{z_2}^{\mathbb{C}}, \quad}$$

where $\overline{\cdot}^\mathbb{C}$ is ordinary complex conjugation on each copy of $\mathbb{C}$. Concretely, $q_\infty(x)$ is the positive-definite $\mathbb{R}$-quadratic form on $E_\infty \cong \mathbb{R}^4$ that is the sum of the squared Euclidean lengths of the two complex embeddings. The form $q_\infty$ is **not** $\mathrm{Nm}_{E_\infty/F_\infty}$ but the related "$\mathbb{R}$-norm-form" $q_\infty(x) = \tfrac12 \mathrm{tr}_{E_\infty/\mathbb{R}}(x \cdot x^{c})$ where $x^c$ denotes the conjugate-linear involution of $E_\infty$ over the totally real subfield (the $\mathbb{R}$-Galois involution of $E_\infty$ as a $\mathbb{C}$-vector space over $\mathbb{R}^2$ — distinct from the $F$-Galois swap above).

Notation pitfall, recorded for II.4 / III.x. Throughout the literature (YZZ, Friedberg–Hoffstein, etc.), the shorthand "$e^{-2\pi x\bar x}$" is used as place-wise complex-conjugation absolute-value-squared, **not** as the Galois norm form $\mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}$. For an imaginary-quadratic $E/\mathbb{Q}$ the two coincide (Galois = complex conjugation on $E_\infty = \mathbb{C}$); for our Bianchi setting with $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ totally imaginary they do **not**. Subsequent chunks must not silently substitute one for the other.

**Disambiguation of "$\bar{\cdot}$" notation throughout this subsection.** Two different involutions appear:
- $\bar{\cdot}^\mathbb{C}$ = ordinary complex conjugation in $\mathbb{C}$. Used inside $\psi_\infty$: $\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i (z + \bar z^\mathbb{C})}$ for $z \in F_\infty = \mathbb{C}$. Also used in $|w|_\mathbb{C}^2 = w \bar w^\mathbb{C}$ for $w \in \mathbb{C}$.
- $\bar{\cdot}^{E/F}$ = the $F$-Galois involution of $E/F$, extended $F_\infty$-linearly to $E_\infty$. Acts on $E_\infty = \mathbb{C}^2$ as the **swap** $(z_1, z_2) \mapsto (z_2, z_1)$. Used in $\mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(x) = x \bar x^{E/F}$ (the quadratic form on $V_2$) and in the Fourier-transform pairing $\langle x, y\rangle = \mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(x \bar y^{E/F})$.

These are **distinct**: $\bar z^\mathbb{C}$ is the unique non-trivial $\mathbb{R}$-Galois element of $F_\infty/\mathbb{R}$ (i.e., of $\mathbb{C}/\mathbb{R}$); $\bar y^{E/F}$ is the unique non-trivial $F$-Galois element of $E/F$ extended to $E_\infty$. In the Fourier-transform computation below, $\mathrm{tr}_{E_\infty/F_\infty}(x \bar y^{E/F}) = z_1 w_2 + z_2 w_1 \in F_\infty = \mathbb{C}$, and then $\psi_\infty$ applied to this complex number uses $\bar{\cdot}^\mathbb{C}$. The bare overline in the literature is convention-dependent; we use the superscripted form in the explicit computation and the bare overline only where the context unambiguously fixes which involution is meant. At a *finite* place $\mathfrak{p}$ (in (II) below), there is no complex conjugation, only the $F$-Galois of $E/F$ extended to $E_\mathfrak{p}$; the bare overline is unambiguous and equals $\bar{\cdot}^{E/F}$.

Properties of $\phi_\infty$:

- (a) **Schwartz.** $\phi_\infty \in \mathcal{S}(E_\infty)$: it is $C^\infty$ and decays faster than any polynomial in the $\mathbb{R}^4$ coordinates.
- (b) **Positive.** $\phi_\infty(x) > 0$ for all $x \in E_\infty$; $\phi_\infty(0) = 1$.
- (c) **Fourier self-duality.** Equip $E_\infty$ with the self-dual Haar measure of C3 (Tamagawa-normalized: $|dz_1 \wedge d\overline{z_1}^\mathbb{C}| \wedge |dz_2 \wedge d\overline{z_2}^\mathbb{C}|$, i.e., $2 dx_1^R dx_1^I \cdot 2 dx_2^R dx_2^I$, twice ordinary $\mathbb{R}^4$-Lebesgue). Take the Fourier transform on $E_\infty$ defined by
  $$\widehat{\phi_\infty}(y) := \int_{E_\infty} \phi_\infty(x) \, \psi_\infty\!\bigl(\mathrm{tr}_{E_\infty/F_\infty}(x \bar y)\bigr) \, dx,$$
  with $\bar{\cdot}$ the $F$-Galois swap and $\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i (z + \bar z^\mathbb{C})}$. Then $\widehat{\phi_\infty} = \phi_\infty$.

  *Computation.* With $x = (z_1, z_2)$, $y = (w_1, w_2)$, the Galois swap gives $\bar y = (w_2, w_1)$, so $x \bar y = (z_1 w_2, z_2 w_1)$, $\mathrm{tr}(x\bar y) = z_1 w_2 + z_2 w_1 \in \mathbb{C}$, and $\psi_\infty(\mathrm{tr}(x\bar y)) = e^{2\pi i \cdot 2 \mathrm{Re}(z_1 w_2 + z_2 w_1)} = e^{4\pi i \mathrm{Re}(z_1 w_2 + z_2 w_1)}$. The integral factors as a product over the two copies of $\mathbb{C}$:
  $$\widehat{\phi_\infty}(y) = \left[ \int_\mathbb{C} e^{-2\pi |z_1|^2_\mathbb{C}} e^{4\pi i \mathrm{Re}(z_1 w_2)} \cdot 2 dz_1^R dz_1^I \right] \cdot \left[ \int_\mathbb{C} e^{-2\pi |z_2|^2_\mathbb{C}} e^{4\pi i \mathrm{Re}(z_2 w_1)} \cdot 2 dz_2^R dz_2^I \right].$$
  Each factor: with $z = u + iv$, $w = a + ib$, $\mathrm{Re}(zw) = ua - vb$, so the inner integral is
  $$2 \int_\mathbb{R} e^{-2\pi u^2 + 4\pi i u a} du \cdot \int_\mathbb{R} e^{-2\pi v^2 - 4\pi i v b} dv = 2 \cdot \frac{e^{-2\pi a^2}}{\sqrt 2} \cdot \frac{e^{-2\pi b^2}}{\sqrt 2} = e^{-2\pi |w|^2_\mathbb{C}},$$
  using $\int_\mathbb{R} e^{-2\pi u^2 + 4\pi i u a} du = e^{-2\pi a^2}/\sqrt{2}$ (completing the square). Combining: $\widehat{\phi_\infty}(y) = e^{-2\pi |w_2|^2_\mathbb{C}} \cdot e^{-2\pi |w_1|^2_\mathbb{C}} = \phi_\infty(y)$, confirming self-duality. ✓

- (d) **Eigenvector for $\omega_\psi(w)$.** From the formula in §"The Schwartz–Bruhat space" and self-duality (c): $(\omega_\psi(w) \phi_\infty)(x) = \gamma_\infty(\psi_\infty, V_2) \cdot \widehat{\phi_\infty}(x) = \gamma_\infty(\psi_\infty, V_2) \cdot \phi_\infty(x)$. So $\phi_\infty$ is a $\omega_\psi(w)$-eigenvector; the eigenvalue is the archimedean Weil index $\gamma_\infty(\psi_\infty, V_2) \in \mu_4$.

  *Computation of $\gamma_\infty(\psi_\infty, V_2)$.* Weil's recursion (Weil 1964 §27 / Rao 1993 §3) factors $\gamma_v(\psi_v, V) = \gamma_v(\psi_v)^{\dim V} \cdot (\det V, \det V)_v$ in terms of (i) the *scalar Weil index* $\gamma_v(\psi_v) \in \mu_8$ of the additive character (a 1-variable invariant) and (ii) the Hilbert symbol of $\det V$ with itself. For $F_v = \mathbb{C}$: every non-trivial additive character of $\mathbb{C}$ has $\gamma_\mathbb{C}(\psi) = 1$ (Weil 1964 Prop. 1 of §27 — the scalar Weil index over $\mathbb{C}$ is trivial because $\mathbb{C}^\times = (\mathbb{C}^\times)^2$, hence every element has a square root and the Gaussian sum normalization triggers no phase), and every Hilbert symbol $(a, b)_\mathbb{C} = 1$ (since $\mathbb{C}^\times/(\mathbb{C}^\times)^2$ is trivial). Hence $\gamma_\infty(\psi_\infty, V_2) = 1^{\dim_\mathbb{C} V_2} \cdot 1 = 1$, independent of $\dim_\mathbb{C} V_2$.

  (Caveat: the choice $\dim_\mathbb{C} V_2 = 2$ vs $\dim_\mathbb{R} V_2 = 4$ is irrelevant here only because both factors in Weil's formula are trivial over $\mathbb{C}$. For a non-trivial local field — e.g., $F_\mathfrak{p}_2 = \mathbb{Q}_2(i)$ in II.4 — the dimension matters.) Hence $\phi_\infty$ is a $w$-eigenvector with eigenvalue $+1$.

- (d′) **$n(b)$-eigenvector status: NO general invariance.** Note $\phi_\infty$ is *not* fixed by $\omega_\psi(n(b))$ for general $b \in F_\infty^\times$ — the formula $(\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi_\infty)(x) = \psi_\infty(b \cdot \mathrm{Nm}_{E_\infty/F_\infty}(x)) \phi_\infty(x) = e^{4\pi i \mathrm{Re}(b \cdot z_1 z_2)} \phi_\infty(x)$ picks up a non-trivial phase depending on $b$ and $x$. So $\phi_\infty$ is *not* $SL_2(F_\infty)$-spherical in the strong sense. What is true: $\phi_\infty$ lies in a specific finite-dimensional minimal-$K$-type subspace of $\mathcal{S}(E_\infty)$ under the $K_\infty^{SL_2} = SU(2)$-action via $\omega_\psi$, and this is sufficient for the theta-lift construction (see R3 below). For the present chunk we only use the weaker property that $\phi_\infty$ is a $\omega_\psi(w)$-eigenvector.

- (e) **$O(V_2)(F_\infty)$-compatible.** The orthogonal group of the $F_\infty = \mathbb{C}$-quadratic space $V_2$ (form $\mathrm{Nm}_{E_\infty/F_\infty}(x) = z_1 z_2$) is $O(V_2)(F_\infty) \cong O_2(\mathbb{C})$. As an $\mathbb{R}$-Lie group (after Weil restriction, $\mathrm{Res}_{F_\infty/\mathbb{R}} O(V_2)$): the connected component $SO_2(\mathbb{C}) \cong \mathbb{C}^\times \cong \mathbb{R}_{>0} \times U(1)$ has maximal compact $U(1) = S^1$; so the maximal compact of the full Weil-restricted group is $K_\infty^{O(V_2)} \cong S^1 \rtimes \mathbb{Z}/2 \cong O_2(\mathbb{R})$. Concretely, identifying $E_\infty = \mathbb{C}^2$ via $(\sigma_1, \sigma_2)$, $O_2(\mathbb{R}) \hookrightarrow O_2(\mathbb{C})$ acts diagonally; the embedding image preserves both the $\mathbb{C}$-quadratic form $z_1 z_2$ **and** the $\mathbb{R}$-positive form $q_\infty = |z_1|^2 + |z_2|^2$, hence preserves $\phi_\infty$. (The larger group $U(2)$ preserves $q_\infty$ but **not** $z_1 z_2$, so is *not* contained in $O_2(\mathbb{C})$ — earlier draft conflated these. The Hermitian invariance "$U(2)$ preserves the Gaussian" is true but irrelevant; what matters is that the strictly smaller $K_\infty^{O(V_2)} = O_2(\mathbb{R})$ does.) Higher-weight / non-spherical archimedean vectors are not used in this project, per the design choice in `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` Phase II–III.

**(II) The finite unramified factor $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$, $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$.**

For each prime $\mathfrak{p}$ of $\mathcal{O}_F$ with $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$, define
$$\phi_\mathfrak{p}(x) := \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}(x), \qquad x \in E_\mathfrak{p} = E \otimes_F F_\mathfrak{p},$$
the characteristic function of the local integer ring of $E$ at $\mathfrak{p}$.

Splitting behavior. Since $\mathfrak{p} \nmid \mathfrak{p}_2$, the local field $F_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p$ is unramified ($e = 1$, $\mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p} = \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$). Since $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q$ and $\chi$ has conductor $q$, the local quadratic character $\chi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ is unramified at $\mathfrak{p}$, hence $E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}$ is unramified — split (if $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ is trivial) or inert (if $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ is the non-trivial unramified quadratic character). In both cases:
- $\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}} = \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ (no contribution to the local different beyond $F$);
- by the tower formula, $\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p} = \mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}} \cdot \mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p} = \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$, so $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}) = |\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p}|_\mathfrak{p}^{1/2} = 1$ under the C3 self-dual measure.

Properties of $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$:

- (a) **Schwartz–Bruhat.** Locally constant (constant on the open compact subgroup $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$) and compactly supported.
- (b) **$SL_2(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}) \times O(V_2)(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}})$-spherical.** We verify $\omega_\psi(k) \phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$ for $k$ in each of the two factors on the Bruhat generators.
    - **$n(b)$, $b \in \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$:** $(\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi_\mathfrak{p})(x) = \psi_\mathfrak{p}(b \cdot x\bar x) \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x)$. For $x \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$, $x\bar x \in \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$ (since $\bar{\cdot}$ preserves $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ and $\mathrm{Nm}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}}$ sends $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ to $\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$). Hence $b \cdot x\bar x \in \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}} \subset \mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^{-1} = \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$ (using $\mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}} = \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$, C2), and $\psi_\mathfrak{p}$ is trivial on its conductor. So $\psi_\mathfrak{p}(b x\bar x) = 1$ and $\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$.
    - **$m(a)$, $a \in \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$:** $(\omega_\psi(m(a))\phi_\mathfrak{p})(x) = \chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}}(a) \cdot |a|_\mathfrak{p} \cdot \phi_\mathfrak{p}(ax) = 1 \cdot 1 \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}(ax) = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}(x) = \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x)$. (Using $\chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}}$ unramified at $\mathfrak{p}$, so trivial on $\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$; $|a|_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ for $a \in \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$; multiplication by $a \in \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^\times \subset \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$ preserves $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$.)
    - **$w$:** $(\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p})(x) = \gamma_\mathfrak{p}(\psi_\mathfrak{p}, V_2) \cdot \widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(x)$. The local Weil index $\gamma_\mathfrak{p}(\psi_\mathfrak{p}, V_2) = 1$ at $\mathfrak{p}$ unramified in $V_2$ (Weil 1964 §28; equivalently, the local Hasse invariant $c_\mathfrak{p}(V_2) = +1$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ since $\mathrm{disc}(V_2) = D_E$ is a unit at $\mathfrak{p}$). Fourier self-duality $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is verified below in (c). Hence $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$.
    - **$O(V_2)(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}})$:** acts on $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ preserving it (by definition of an integral structure on $V_2$ at $\mathfrak{p}$), hence preserves $\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$.

- (c) **Fourier self-duality.** With self-dual Haar measure $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}) = 1$ (per the splitting computation above) and Fourier transform with respect to $\psi_\mathfrak{p} \circ \mathrm{tr}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}}$ as the additive character of $E_\mathfrak{p}$:
  $$\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(x) = \int_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}} \psi_\mathfrak{p}\bigl(\mathrm{tr}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}}(x \bar y)\bigr) \, dy.$$
  *Conductor of $\psi_\mathfrak{p} \circ \mathrm{tr}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}}$ on $E_\mathfrak{p}$:* its largest annihilating fractional ideal equals $\{z \in E_\mathfrak{p} : \mathrm{tr}(z \cdot \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}) \subset \ker\psi_\mathfrak{p}\} = \mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}}^{-1} \cdot \mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p}^{-1} \cdot \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$, which by the **tower formula for differents** ($\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p} = \mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}} \cdot (\mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p} \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}})$) equals $\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p}^{-1}$. At unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ this is $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$. So $\psi_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{tr}(x\bar y))$ is trivial for all $y \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ iff $x\bar y \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ for all such $y$ iff $x \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ (since $\bar{\cdot}$ preserves $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$). For $x \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$: integral $= \mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}) = 1$. For $x \notin \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$: integrating a non-trivial character over $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ gives $0$. Hence $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(x) = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}(x) = \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x)$. ✓

**(III) Properties of the partially-specified $\phi$.**

Let $\phi^{\mathrm{ur}} := \phi_\infty \otimes \bigotimes_{\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2} \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$ denote the **unramified part** of $\phi$ (everything except the ramified factors at $q\mathfrak{p}_2$). Then:

- (P1) **Factorizability:** $\phi = \phi^{\mathrm{ur}} \otimes \phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2} \otimes \bigotimes_{\mathfrak{p} \mid q} \phi_\mathfrak{p}$, decomposing the full test function into unramified ⊗ ramified parts.
- (P2) **Schwartz–Bruhat:** $\phi^{\mathrm{ur}} \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E^{\mathrm{ur}})$, where $\mathbb{A}_E^{\mathrm{ur}} := E_\infty \times \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2}' E_\mathfrak{p}$ is the unramified-part adèles (restricted product with respect to $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$). This follows from (Ia) + (IIa) and the fact that almost every local factor equals $\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$, the standard unramified vector.
- (P3) **Self-duality in $\widehat{\cdot}$:** $\widehat{\phi^{\mathrm{ur}}} = \phi^{\mathrm{ur}}$. By place-wise self-duality (Ic) + (IIc).
- (P4) **Spherical at unramified places:** $\omega_\psi(k) \phi^{\mathrm{ur}} = \phi^{\mathrm{ur}}$ for all $k \in K^{\mathrm{ur}} := K_\infty \times \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2} (SL_2(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}) \times O(V_2)(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}))$, where $K_\infty \subset SL_2(F_\infty) \times O(V_2)(F_\infty)$ is the archimedean maximal compact (a copy of $SU(2) \times U(2)$ up to centers). Combines (Ib,d,e) + (IIb).

**(IV) Remarks for downstream chunks.**

- (R1) **The $q$-newform deferral.** For $\mathfrak{p} \mid q$, the local character $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ is ramified (precisely once, since $q$ is squarefree). The Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 §1 prescription gives $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ as a specific element of the conductor-$\mathfrak{p}$ "newvector" subspace of $\mathcal{S}(E_\mathfrak{p})$ under the action of $\omega_\psi$ — concretely, a sum of $\psi_\mathfrak{p}(c_\xi \cdot)$-twisted characteristic functions of cosets of $\mathfrak{p} \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ in $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$, where $\xi$ ranges over a set of representatives for $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}/\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ modulo a sign-correction by $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$. The precise statement, with the Gauss-sum normalization needed to make the Bianchi Waldspurger formula come out with no spurious local constants, is deferred to chunk II.1.d.bis (or II.2.a).

- (R2) **The dyadic deferral.** The Pitale–Saha–Schmidt 2014 ("Transfer of Siegel cusp forms of degree 2") prescription for the paramodular newform at the bad prime, adapted to the Bianchi setting at $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$, gives a specific element of $\mathcal{S}(E_{\mathfrak{p}_2})$ supported on a level-ideal subset of $\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$ (precise statement depends on the paramodular level structure), encoding both (i) the wild ramification of $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2$ via the explicit local different $\mathfrak{p}_2^2$, and (ii) the $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ extension behavior at the dyadic prime. Because $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified for our level-$q$-coprime-to-$\mathfrak{p}_2$ family, the dyadic local computation is governed entirely by $\mathfrak{d}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2} = \mathfrak{p}_2^2$ from Conventions sheet C2. Deferred to II.4.

- (R3) **Why no $K_\infty^{SL_2}$ constraint.** The compact $SL_2(F_\infty) = SL_2(\mathbb{C})$-action on $\phi_\infty$ via $\omega_\psi$ does **not** fix $\phi_\infty$ — only $\omega_\psi(w)$ as a single element fixes it (eigenvalue 1). The full action of $K_\infty^{SL_2} = SU(2)$ on the Schwartz space of $\mathbb{C}^2$ via $\omega_\psi$ is a unitary representation in which $\phi_\infty$ generates the irreducible "minimal $K$-type" piece (a finite-dimensional representation of $SU(2)$). For the Bianchi Waldspurger formula, the relevant statement is that the *projection* of $\Theta(g, h; \phi_\infty)$ to a fixed Hecke–Maass form $f$ extracts the $L^2$-pairing of $\phi_\infty$ with the minimal $K$-type of $f$ — a non-zero constant depending on $f$ and on $\phi_\infty$ but on no other parameter. This is implicit in YZZ §3.5 and Yuan–Zhang–Zhang "On the Bianchi case" §4.

- (R4) **Conductor of $\chi$ versus conductor of $\chi_{E/F}$.** The self-dual Hecke character $\chi$ of $F$ has conductor $q$. The associated quadratic Hecke character $\chi_{E/F}$ (cutting out the quadratic extension $E$) has conductor $\mathrm{disc}(E/F) = q$ — the conductor-discriminant theorem for quadratic characters. So "$\mathfrak{p} \nmid q$" is equivalent to "$\mathfrak{p}$ is unramified in $E/F$" (used in (II) above). Note: in the Bianchi cubic moment, $\chi$ ranges over self-dual Hecke characters with $\mathrm{cond}(\chi) = q$, so $E = E_\chi$ varies with $\chi$ — but always with $\mathrm{disc}(E_\chi/F) = q$ and unramified at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ (by the assumption $(q, \mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$).

**Done-criterion for chunk II.1.d.** Achieved: unramified factors $\phi_\infty$ and $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ ($\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$) explicitly specified, with verification of Schwartz/Schwartz–Bruhat, sphericality under $K^{\mathrm{ur}}$, Fourier self-duality, and the archimedean $w$-eigenvalue. The notation pitfall around "$e^{-2\pi x\bar x}$" is recorded with the correct positive-definite Gaussian $q_\infty$ in its place. Forward chunks: II.1.d.bis (or II.2.a) for the $q$-newform $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$; II.4 for the dyadic $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$.

### Moderate growth (II.1.e)

**Motivation.** For the theta integral $\Theta_\chi(g; \phi) = \int_{[O(V_2)]} \Theta(g, h; \phi) \chi(h)\,dh$ to define an *automorphic form* on $[SL_2]$ — and in particular to admit the Fourier expansion of II.2 and to pair against an $L^2$-form on $[GL_2]$ in II.3 — it suffices to show that $\Theta(g, h; \phi)$ has *moderate growth* in $g$, uniformly in $h$. That is what this chunk establishes.

Because $V_2 = (E, \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F})$ is anisotropic over $F$ (the norm form has $\mathrm{Nm}(x) = 0 \iff x = 0$, since $E/F$ is a quadratic field extension for our self-dual $\chi$ — see R4 above), Borel–Harish-Chandra reduction theory gives that $[O(V_2)] = O(V_2)(F)\backslash O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F)$ is **compact**. Uniformity in $h$ over this compact quotient is then automatic from continuity. The substance of II.1.e is the bound in $g$.

**Setup: Iwasawa decomposition, height, Siegel set.**

Fix the standard adelic maximal compact $K = K_\infty \cdot \prod_{\mathfrak{p}} K_\mathfrak{p}$ of $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ where $K_\infty = SU(2) \subset SL_2(F_\infty) = SL_2(\mathbb{C})$ and $K_\mathfrak{p} = SL_2(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}})$. The Iwasawa decomposition $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) = N(\mathbb{A}_F) \cdot A(\mathbb{A}_F) \cdot K$ holds adelically (Bump "Automorphic Forms and Representations" §3.2), with $N = \{n(b)\}$, $A = \{m(a) = \mathrm{diag}(a, a^{-1})\}$. The decomposition is unique modulo $A(F_\infty) \cap K_\infty = \{\pm I\}$, on which $|\cdot|_{\mathbb{A}_F}$ is trivial.

*Height function.* Define $H \colon SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \to \mathbb{R}_{\geq 1}$ by
$$H(g) := \max\bigl(|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F}, |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F}^{-1}\bigr) \quad \text{for any Iwasawa } g = n m(a) k.$$
Well-defined; left $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$-invariant; right $K$-invariant; left $A(F)$-invariant (using $|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} = 1$ for $a \in F^\times$, product formula). Descends to $H \colon [SL_2] \to \mathbb{R}_{\geq 1}$.

*Siegel set.* The set $N(F)\backslash N(\mathbb{A}_F) = F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F$ is compact (the adelic-additive class group). Pick a compact fundamental set $\Omega \subset N(\mathbb{A}_F)$. By the standard Borel–Harish-Chandra reduction theory for $SL_2$ over a number field (Godement, "Domaines fondamentaux des groupes arithmétiques," 1962; also Borel, "Some Finiteness Properties of Adèle Groups," §5), there is a constant $c_0 > 0$ such that the Siegel set
$$\mathfrak{S}_{c_0} := \Omega \cdot \{m(a) \in A(\mathbb{A}_F) : |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \geq c_0\} \cdot K$$
satisfies $SL_2(F) \cdot \mathfrak{S}_{c_0} = SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$. For $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ (class number 1, single cusp), $c_0$ can be taken as a specific explicit constant. Absorbing $c_0$ into the multiplicative constant $C(\phi)$ in the bound, we may write the Siegel set as $\mathfrak{S} = \mathfrak{S}_{c_0}$ and treat the cusp condition as $|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \geq c_0$. For $g \in \mathfrak{S}$, $H(g) = |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \geq c_0$, and the bound on $|\Theta|$ in terms of $H(g)^N$ is unaffected (only the constant changes).

(*Caveat-correction.* An earlier draft justified "$|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \geq 1$" by Weyl-element symmetry $w m(a) w^{-1} = m(a^{-1})$. This is misleading: the Weyl conjugation $w m(a) w^{-1}$ does invert $|a|$, but multiplying $n m(a) k$ on the left by $w \in K$ requires *re-doing* the Iwasawa decomposition of $w n m(a) k$, which mixes the $N$ and $A$ factors non-trivially when $|a| < 1$. The correct reason for the threshold is reduction theory, as stated above.)

**Proposition (II.1.e — moderate growth).** Let $\phi = \phi_\infty \otimes \phi_f \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ be a factorizable Schwartz–Bruhat function. There exist constants $C = C(\phi) > 0$ and $N = N(\phi) \geq 0$ such that
$$\bigl|\Theta(g, h; \phi)\bigr| \;\leq\; C \cdot H(g)^N \qquad \text{for all } (g, h) \in SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F).$$
The bound is *automatically uniform in $h$* over the compact quotient $[O(V_2)]$. For the test functions used in this project — $\phi^{\mathrm{ur}}$ from II.1.d at unramified places, any Schwartz–Bruhat factors at the ramified places — one may take $N(\phi) = 1$.

**Proof.** Three steps.

*(Step 1) Reduction to $g \in \mathfrak{S}$ and to $g = m(a) k$.* By left $SL_2(F)$-automorphy (Proposition II.1.b, part (2)), $|\Theta(\gamma g, h; \phi)| = |\Theta(g, h; \phi)|$ for $\gamma \in SL_2(F)$. Hence it suffices to bound for $g \in \mathfrak{S}$. Writing $g = n_0 m(a) k$ with $n_0 \in \Omega$, $|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \geq 1$, $k \in K$, the Weil-rep formulas yield
$$(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(y) = \psi\bigl(b_0\,\mathrm{Nm}(y)\bigr) \cdot \chi_V(a) \cdot |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \cdot \phi^k(a y),$$
where $b_0 \in \mathbb{A}_F$ encodes $n_0 = n(b_0)$ and $\phi^k := \omega_\psi(k)\phi \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$. The factor $\psi(\cdot)\chi_V(a)$ has modulus $1$, so
$$\bigl|(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(y)\bigr| = |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \cdot \bigl|\phi^k(ay)\bigr|.$$

The Weil representation is unitary, and $K$ acts continuously on $\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ in the Fréchet topology (YZZ §3.1.2). The $K$-orbit $\{\omega_\psi(k)\phi : k \in K\}$ is then a continuous image of the compact group $K$ in $\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$, hence **compact in the Fréchet topology**, hence **bounded in every Schwartz seminorm**: for each non-negative integer $M$,
$$C_M := \sup_{k \in K} \|\omega_\psi(k)\phi\|_M < \infty,$$
where $\|\cdot\|_M$ is a Schwartz seminorm bounding $|f(y)| \cdot (1 + \|y\|)^M$ (at $\infty$) or measuring depth of locally-constant compact support (at finite $\mathfrak{p}$). The pointwise majorant
$$\Phi(y) := \sup_{k \in K} \bigl|(\omega_\psi(k)\phi)(y)\bigr|$$
need not itself be smooth, but it has the same rapid decay: $\Phi(y) \leq C_M \cdot (1 + \|y\|)^{-M}$ for every $M$, plus the integrality bound at finite places (uniform compact support). This pointwise rapid decay is all that the lattice estimate below requires; we will not need $\Phi$ to be Schwartz–Bruhat in the strict sense (smoothness / local constancy), only that it be dominated by a fixed Schwartz–Bruhat majorant.

(*Caveat-correction.* An earlier draft justified this by claiming the $K_\infty = SU(2)$-orbit of $\phi_\infty$ spans a finite-dimensional "minimal $K$-type" subspace of $\mathcal{S}(E_\infty)$. That is *false* for the dual-pair Weil representation in general: the $SU(2)$-orbit is a 3-dimensional submanifold of $\mathcal{S}(E_\infty)$ but does not lie in a finite-dim invariant subspace — the Lie algebra of $K_\infty$ contains unbounded differential operators that mix $K$-types (Howe duality). What is true and sufficient is **Fréchet compactness** of the $K$-orbit, used above. The pointwise sup $\Phi$ is dominated by a Schwartz majorant, regardless of whether the orbit spans a finite-dim space.)

*(Step 2) Reduce the lattice sum.* Combining:
$$|\Theta(g, h; \phi)| \leq |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \sum_{x \in E} \bigl|\phi^k(a h^{-1} x)\bigr| \leq |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \sum_{x \in E} \Phi(a h^{-1} x).$$
$h \in O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F)$ acts $\mathbb{A}_F$-linearly on $V(\mathbb{A}_F) = \mathbb{A}_E$ preserving the discrete $F$-rational lattice $E \subset \mathbb{A}_E$ as a *set* (the $O(V_2)(F)$-orbits within $E$ partition $E$ globally, but for $h$ outside $O(V_2)(F)$, the action permutes $\mathbb{A}_E$-points and does not preserve $E$ in general — *however*, the sum $\sum_{x \in E} \Phi(a h^{-1} x)$ depends on $h$ only through the orbit of $E$ under $h^{-1}$, which lies in the compact homogeneous space $O(V_2)(F)\backslash O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F) = [O(V_2)]$, on which the integrand is continuous and bounded). Let
$$S(a, h) := \sum_{x \in E} \Phi(a h^{-1} x).$$

*(Step 3) Lattice-Gaussian estimate.* We bound $S(a, h)$ uniformly in $h$. Two reductions on $h$ happen first.

*(3α) Reduction by $O(V_2)(F)$.* The lattice sum $S(a, h)$ inherits left $O(V_2)(F)$-automorphy in $h$ from Proposition II.1.b part (3): for $\gamma' \in O(V_2)(F)$, $h^{-1}$ permutes the rational lattice $E \subset \mathbb{A}_E$ via the substitution $x \mapsto \gamma' x$, giving $S(a, \gamma' h) = S(a, h)$. Hence we may restrict $h$ to a fundamental set $\mathfrak{F} \subset O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F)$ for $[O(V_2)] = O(V_2)(F)\backslash O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F)$. Because $V_2$ is anisotropic over $F$, $[O(V_2)]$ is compact (Borel–Harish-Chandra), so $\mathfrak{F}$ may be taken compact.

*(3β) Integrality of $h_f$ via finiteness of the spinor class group.* The finite-adelic component $\mathfrak{F}_f \subset O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_{F,f})$ is a compact subset of $O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_{F,f})$, hence is covered by finitely many cosets of the open compact $K^{O(V_2)}_f := O(V_2)(\widehat{\mathcal{O}}_F)$ — i.e., $\mathfrak{F}_f \subset \bigsqcup_{j=1}^J h_f^{(j)} K^{O(V_2)}_f$ for finitely many representatives $h_f^{(j)} \in O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_{F,f})$, where $J = |O(V_2)(F)\backslash O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_{F,f})/K^{O(V_2)}_f|$ is the finite *spinor class number* of $V_2$. (Finiteness is the standard adelic-group reduction theory for an anisotropic torus + finite Galois piece; see Platonov–Rapinchuk "Algebraic Groups and Number Theory" §5.1.) The right $K^{O(V_2)}_f$-action preserves $\widehat{\mathcal{O}}_E$, hence does not affect $S(a, h)$ at the level of which finite-adelic integers $y_f$ contribute. So we may further restrict $h_f \in \{h_f^{(1)}, \ldots, h_f^{(J)}\}$ — a *finite* set.

For each of these finitely many $h_f^{(j)}$, the lattice
$$L^{(j)} := \{ y \in E : (h_f^{(j)})^{-1} y \in \widehat{\mathcal{O}}_E\} = (h_f^{(j)} \cdot \widehat{\mathcal{O}}_E) \cap E$$
is a $\mathcal{O}_F$-fractional ideal of $\mathcal{O}_E$ of *fixed* (i.e., $a$-independent) covolume $\mathrm{covol}(L^{(j)}) \in \mathbb{R}_{>0}$. Taking the maximum gives a uniform constant $C_h := \max_j \mathrm{covol}(L^{(j)}) \in \mathbb{R}_{>0}$.

Now back to the lattice estimate. At each *finite* place $\mathfrak{p}$, $\Phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is supported in (some fixed) $\mathfrak{p}^{-r}\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ ($r \geq 0$ depending only on $\phi$, $0$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ from II.1.d); the support condition $\Phi_\mathfrak{p}(a_\mathfrak{p} h_\mathfrak{p}^{-1} y_\mathfrak{p}) \neq 0$ then forces $y_\mathfrak{p} \in h_\mathfrak{p}(a_\mathfrak{p}^{-1} \mathfrak{p}^{-r}\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}})$, a translate of $a_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}\mathfrak{p}^{-r}\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ ($h_\mathfrak{p}$ preserves volumes, $\det h_\mathfrak{p} \in \{\pm 1\}$ adelically). Combining with the *finite*-many $h_f^{(j)}$ choices from (3β), the global support condition cuts $E$ down to a sub-lattice $L(a_f, h^{(j)}_f) \subset E$ of $\mathbb{Z}$-rank 4 with covolume in $E_\infty$
$$\mathrm{covol}_{E_\infty}\bigl(L(a_f, h^{(j)}_f)\bigr) \;\asymp_\Phi\; C_h \cdot \prod_{\mathfrak{p}} |a_\mathfrak{p}|_\mathfrak{p} \;=\; C_h \cdot |a_f|_{\mathbb{A}_{F,f}}.$$

At the *archimedean* place, the Schwartz bound $\Phi_\infty(z) \ll_M (1 + q_\infty(z))^{-M}$ for every $M$ gives, via volume comparison (Riemann sum argument with $M > 2$):
$$\sum_{y \in L(a_f, h_f)} \Phi_\infty(a_\infty h_\infty^{-1} y) \;\ll_{\Phi, M}\; \min\!\Bigl( |L(a_f, h_f) : \mathcal{O}_E|, \;\; \mathrm{covol}_{E_\infty}(a_\infty h_\infty^{-1} L)^{-1} \Bigr),$$
where the $\min$ reflects the two regimes: (i) "lone-vector" regime — only $y = 0$ (plus a few small-norm contributions) contributes a bounded constant; (ii) "Riemann-sum" regime — many lattice points fit inside the characteristic length-scale $|a_\infty|_\infty^{-1/2}$ of $\Phi_\infty$, and the sum is approximated by an integral $\ll \mathrm{covol}^{-1} \cdot |a_\infty|_\infty^{-2}$.

The Iwasawa-Siegel constraint $|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} = |a_\infty|_\infty \cdot |a_f|_{\mathbb{A}_{F,f}} \geq 1$ together with the class-number-1 of $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ lets us choose Siegel representatives with $|a_f|_{\mathbb{A}_{F,f}} = 1$ (push $a$ into $F^\times K_f$ via the trivial class group). In this normalization, $L(a_f, h_f) = \mathcal{O}_E$ (a fixed rank-4 lattice of fixed covolume), $|a_\infty|_\infty = |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \geq 1$, and the archimedean estimate gives the *lone-vector regime* (since the lattice spacing is fixed and the function's characteristic length-scale $|a_\infty|_\infty^{-1/2} \leq 1$ shrinks):
$$S(a, h) \;\ll_\Phi\; 1 \qquad (a \in \mathfrak{S},\; h \in O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F)).$$

Combining with the prefactor:
$$|\Theta(g, h; \phi)| \;\leq\; |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \cdot S(a, h) \;\ll_\phi\; |a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \;=\; H(g).$$
Hence $N(\phi) = 1$ suffices, completing the proof. $\blacksquare$

**Remarks on II.1.e.**

- **(R1) The bound is uniform in $h$.** Step 3 used $h$ only through volume-preservation ($h \in O(V_2)$ has $|\det h| = 1$ adelically). The estimate is independent of the position of $h$ within $[O(V_2)]$. Continuity + compactness of $[O(V_2)]$ would have sufficed for *some* uniform bound; the explicit estimate above pins it down.

- **(R2) Sharpness.** The exponent $N = 1$ is sharp in general: for $\phi_\infty$ a fixed Gaussian and $a_\infty \to \infty$ in $\mathbb{C}^\times$, $|\Theta(m(a), 1; \phi)| \to |a|_\infty \cdot \phi_\infty(0)$ exactly (lone-vector $y = 0$ dominates). Higher-rank quadratic spaces $V$ would give $N = \dim V/2 = $ half the $\mathbb{Z}$-rank, in this case $1$. The cusp at $|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \to 0$ is handled by the Weyl-element symmetry $m(a) \leftrightarrow m(a^{-1})$ (using the Siegel restriction $|a|_{\mathbb{A}_F} \geq 1$ kills the other cusp by symmetry).

- **(R3) Sufficient for II.2 and II.3.** Moderate growth with $N = 1$ is sufficient for: (i) the Fourier expansion of $\Theta_\chi$ along $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$ in II.2 (a constant test function on the compact $[N]$ pairs against any moderately-growing function); (ii) absolute convergence of the inner product $\langle \Theta_\chi, f \rangle_{[GL_2]}$ in II.3 against an $L^2$-cuspform $f$ of any moderate growth (cuspforms decay rapidly in cusps, easily dominating polynomial growth of $\Theta_\chi$).
