- **(R4) Why $\phi^{\mathrm{ur}}$ suffices.** The bound $N(\phi) = 1$ depends on $\phi$ only through (a) the archimedean Schwartz seminorms of $\phi^k_\infty$ (uniformly in $k \in K_\infty$) and (b) the covolume of the finite-adelic support lattice $L(a_f, h_f^{(j)})$. Both are bounded uniformly by the data already specified in II.1.d: at $\infty$, the $SU(2)$-orbit $\{\omega_\psi(k)\phi_\infty : k \in K_\infty\}$ is a continuous image of the compact $K_\infty = SU(2)$ in the Fréchet space $\mathcal{S}(E_\infty)$, hence Fréchet-compact, hence uniformly bounded in every Schwartz seminorm (per the corrected Step 1 argument; note this does *not* claim the orbit lies in a finite-dim invariant subspace — that was the disowned earlier draft); at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$, $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$ is $K_\mathfrak{p}$-fixed, contributing $\mathrm{covol}|_\mathfrak{p} = 1$. The deferred ramified factors at $\mathfrak{p} \mid q$ and $\mathfrak{p}_2$ are Schwartz–Bruhat at compact support of fixed depth (bounded by the conductor $q\mathfrak{p}_2$), contributing only a $\phi$-dependent constant to $C(\phi)$ — *not* to the exponent $N(\phi)$.

**Done-criterion for chunk II.1.e.** Achieved: $|\Theta(g, h; \phi)| \ll_\phi H(g)$ on $SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F) \times O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F)$, uniformly in $h$. Forward chunks: II.2 can now Fourier-expand $\Theta_\chi(g) = \int_{[O(V_2)]} \Theta(g, h; \phi) \chi(h) dh$ along the unipotent radical $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$, with convergence guaranteed by the moderate-growth bound combined with compactness of $[O(V_2)]$.

### Fourier expansion (II.2.a — orbit-unfolded form)

**Motivation.** With Phase II.1 closed (kernel definition + automorphy + conventions + test function at unramified places + moderate growth), we begin Phase II.2: the Fourier expansion of the theta lift $\Theta_\chi$ along the unipotent radical $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$ of the standard Borel $B \subset SL_2$. The output of II.2.a is an *abstract* identification of the $n$-th Fourier coefficient $a_\chi(n; g)$ as an adelic integral against $\chi$ of a single Weil-rep matrix coefficient evaluated at a norm representative $\xi_n \in E$. Explicit local factorization + Gauss-sum computation (the Friedberg–Hoffstein closed form $a_\chi(n; g) = c \cdot \chi(\xi_n) |\xi_n|_E^{-1/2} G_n$) is deferred to II.2.b.

**Setup.** Let
$$\Theta_\chi(g; \phi) := \int_{[E^1]} \Theta(g, \eta; \phi) \, \chi(\eta) \, d\eta,$$
where:

- $\chi : E^\times \backslash \mathbb{A}_E^\times \to \mathbb{C}^\times$ is a unitary Hecke character of $E$, regarded as a character of $E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)$ via the inclusion $E^1 \hookrightarrow \mathbb{A}_E^\times$. We work with the "type-I self-dual" case $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = 1$ (Bianchi cubic-moment family); the general self-dual $\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$ with $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ is recorded in R5.
- $[E^1] = E^1(F) \backslash E^1(\mathbb{A}_F) = [SO(V_2)]$ is the *compact* adelic quotient of the norm-1 torus ($V_2$ anisotropic + Borel–Harish-Chandra). The Tamagawa measure gives $\mathrm{vol}([E^1])$ a fixed positive constant; explicit value irrelevant at this chunk.
- The integrand $\Theta(g, \eta; \phi)$ is automorphic in $\eta \in [E^1]$ — this follows from Prop II.1.b (3) restricted from $O(V_2)(F)$ to its connected component $E^1(F)$ — so the integral makes sense.

**Why $[E^1]$ rather than $[O(V_2)]$.** The original P17 §Theta lift definition used $[O(V_2)] = O(V_2)(F)\backslash O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F)$. The key identity is
$$[O(V_2)] = (E^1(F) \rtimes \langle\sigma\rangle)\backslash (E^1(\mathbb{A}_F) \rtimes \langle\sigma\rangle) = E^1(F)\backslash E^1(\mathbb{A}_F) = [E^1],$$
because the Galois generator $\sigma$ lies in $O(V_2)(F)$ globally, so the $\sigma$-factor cancels on both sides of the quotient. Hence $\int_{[O(V_2)]}\Theta(g,h;\phi)\chi(h)dh$ and $\int_{[E^1]}\Theta(g,\eta;\phi)\chi(\eta)d\eta$ are the *same* integral over the *same* quotient space; using $E^1$-coordinates avoids the artificial "extension $\chi(\sigma) \in \{\pm 1\}$" step (which would require $\chi^2|_{E^1} = 1$ for the extension to be a *homomorphism* on the semi-direct product — a constraint *not* automatic for self-dual $\chi$). Subsequent local factorization in II.2.b will split the adelic integral $\int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)}$ into a product $\prod_v \int_{E^1(F_v)}$, and the Galois action on each $E^1(F_v)$ is handled per-place via $\bar\xi_n$ — no global $\sigma$-extension is required.

By moderate growth II.1.e + compactness of $[E^1]$, the integrand is continuous and bounded on compacts of $g$; hence $\Theta_\chi(\cdot; \phi)$ is a well-defined continuous function on $SL_2(F)\backslash SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ inheriting moderate growth from $\Theta$. (The character $\chi$ has $|\chi(\eta)| = 1$.)

**Fourier expansion along $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$.** Because $\Theta_\chi$ is automorphic on $SL_2(F)\backslash SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$, it descends to a function on $N(F)\backslash N(\mathbb{A}_F) = F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F$ when evaluated at $n(u)g$ for fixed $g$ — i.e., $u \mapsto \Theta_\chi(n(u)g)$ is a function on the compact abelian group $F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F$. Its Pontryagin dual is $F$ (additive). The Fourier expansion is
$$\Theta_\chi(n(u) g; \phi) = \sum_{n \in F} a_\chi(n; g) \, \psi(n u), \qquad a_\chi(n; g) := \int_{F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F} \Theta_\chi(n(u) g; \phi) \, \psi(-n u) \, du,$$
where $du$ is the self-dual Tamagawa measure on $\mathbb{A}_F$ giving $\mathrm{vol}(F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F) = 1$ (Convention C3). Convergence of the series in $L^2(F\backslash\mathbb{A}_F)$ is Plancherel; pointwise convergence will follow from rapid decay of $a_\chi(n; g)$ in $|n|_{\mathbb{A}_F}$ (deferred to II.3).

**Proposition (II.2.a — orbit-unfolded $n$-th Fourier coefficient).** Let $\phi \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}_E)$ be factorizable Schwartz–Bruhat, and let $\chi$ be a unitary Hecke character of $E^1(F)\backslash E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)$ as above. For $n \in F$:

**(i) $n = 0$:** $a_\chi(0; g) = (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(0) \cdot \int_{[E^1]} \chi(\eta) \, d\eta$. This equals $\mathrm{vol}([E^1]) \cdot (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(0)$ if $\chi|_{[E^1]} = 1$, and $0$ otherwise.

**(ii) $n \in F^\times$, $n \notin \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(E^\times)$:** $a_\chi(n; g) = 0.$

**(iii) $n \in F^\times \cap \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(E^\times)$:** Pick any $\xi_n \in E^\times$ with $\mathrm{Nm}(\xi_n) = n$. The norm-1 torus $E^1(F)$ acts on $E^\times$ by multiplication, *simply transitively* on $\mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n) \cap E^\times$: for $x_1, x_2$ in the fiber, $x_2/x_1 \in E^1(F)$, and the stabilizer of any element of $E^\times$ in $E^1$ under multiplication is trivial. Hence $\mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n) \cap E^\times = E^1(F)\cdot \xi_n$ as a single free $E^1(F)$-orbit, and the orbit-unfolding gives the clean form
$$\boxed{\, a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) \, (\omega_\psi(g) \phi)(\eta^{-1} \xi_n) \, d\eta \,}$$
with *no* stabilizer factor. The integral is independent of the choice of $\xi_n$ (different choices differ by $E^1(F)$-multiplication, absorbed by change of variable $\eta \to \gamma\eta$, $\gamma \in E^1(F)$, plus automorphy $\chi(\gamma\eta) = \chi(\eta)$).

**(iv) Special role of squares.** When $n \in (F^\times)^2$, one may take $\xi_n = m \in F^\times \subset E$ (so $\bar\xi_n = \xi_n$, equivalently $\eta_0 = \xi_n/\bar\xi_n = 1$). The orbital integral (iii) is unchanged in value but acquires the *symbolic relation*: change of variable $\eta \to \eta^{-1}$ in $E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)$ (measure-preserving since $E^1$ is abelian) sends $\chi(\eta) \to \chi(\eta^{-1}) = \chi(\eta)^{-1}$ and $(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) \to (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta\,m)$, giving the alternative expression
$$a_\chi(m^2; g) = \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta)^{-1} (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta \, m) \, d\eta.$$
This equals $a_\chi(m^2; g)$ as written in (iii), but only *trivially*: the two integrals are the same integral viewed under the involution $\eta \leftrightarrow \eta^{-1}$, and identifying them with each other yields no new constraint unless additional symmetry of $\phi$ enforces $(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta\, m) = (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\, m)$. The classical type-II sign-of-functional-equation vanishing on squares — sometimes stated as "$a_\chi(m^2) = 0$ when $\chi$ has odd root number" — is in fact a *downstream* property requiring either (a) paramodular Atkin–Lehner symmetry on $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ at ramified primes, or (b) $\chi^2 = 1$ on $E^1$ (genus-character case). The present Proposition (II.2.a) does *not* derive type-II vanishing; it is recorded as a downstream sanity-check, not a chunk-level claim.

**Skeptic-flagged correction (2026-05-15 session 6 Round 1).** An earlier draft of this Proposition split (iii) and (iv) along the dichotomy "$\xi_n \notin F$ ⇒ stabilizer trivial" vs "$\xi_n \in F$ ⇒ stabilizer $\langle\sigma\rangle$" using $O(V_2)(F) = E^1(F)\rtimes\langle\sigma\rangle$ acting on $\mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n)$. The error: for $\xi_n \notin F$, the element $\eta_0\sigma \in O(V_2)(F)$ with $\eta_0 := \xi_n/\bar\xi_n \in E^1(F)$ also fixes $\xi_n$ (since $\eta_0\sigma\cdot \xi_n = \eta_0\bar\xi_n = (\xi_n/\bar\xi_n)\bar\xi_n = \xi_n$), so the $O(V_2)(F)$-stabilizer is *never* trivial — always order 2. The factor-of-2 discrepancy is resolved cleanly above by using $[E^1]$-coordinates from the start: in $E^1$-coordinates, the orbit is free (simply transitive), no stabilizer factor, and the equivalence with the $[O(V_2)]$-integration is the global identity $[O(V_2)] = [E^1]$ noted in Setup. The "$[O(V_2)]$-orbital with factor $\tfrac12$" form is also correct (consistent under $\int_{O(V_2)(\mathbb{A}_F)} = 2\int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)}$ when $\chi$ extends $\sigma$-trivially), but is more delicate due to the $\chi$-extension constraint; the $[E^1]$ form is the operative one going forward.

**Proof.** Three steps.

*(Step 1) Fubini setup.* By definition (using $[E^1]$-coordinates from Setup),
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F} \!\!\int_{[E^1]} \!\Theta(n(u) g, \eta; \phi) \, \chi(\eta) \, d\eta \, \psi(-n u) \, du.$$
The function $\Theta(n(u) g, \eta; \phi)$ is jointly continuous in $(u, \eta) \in (F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F) \times [E^1]$ — both compact (the former by Tamagawa, the latter by $V_2$-anisotropic + Borel–HC). Continuity + compactness gives joint boundedness; absolute integrability is automatic. Fubini permits the interchange:
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{[E^1]} \chi(\eta) \left[ \int_{F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F} \Theta(n(u) g, \eta; \phi) \, \psi(-n u) \, du \right] d\eta.$$
Within the inner $u$-integral we further interchange $\int_{F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F}$ with $\sum_{x \in E}$ inside $\Theta$. *Justification:* by Prop II.1.b (1), $\sum_{x \in E}|(\omega_\psi(n(u) g)\phi)(\eta^{-1} x)|$ converges absolutely and *uniformly* on $(u, \eta) \in \Omega_u \times [E^1]$ for $\Omega_u \subset \mathbb{A}_F$ any fundamental compact for $F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F$ (a stronger statement than mere pointwise convergence; it is the uniform-on-compacta version of absolute convergence, which Prop II.1.b actually gives). Hence the integration-summation swap is dominated-convergence-justified.

*(Step 2) Inner $u$-integral cuts to $\mathrm{Nm}(x) = n$.* The Weil-rep formula at $n(u)$ gives
$(\omega_\psi(n(u) g) \phi)(y) = \psi(u \cdot Q_V(y)) \cdot (\omega_\psi(g) \phi)(y).$
Substituting $y = \eta^{-1} x$ and using $\eta \in E^1 = SO(V_2)$ preserves $Q_V$ (so $Q_V(\eta^{-1} x) = Q_V(x) = \mathrm{Nm}(x)$):
$$\Theta(n(u) g, \eta; \phi) = \sum_{x \in E} \psi\!\bigl(u \cdot \mathrm{Nm}(x)\bigr) \cdot (\omega_\psi(g) \phi)(\eta^{-1} x).$$
Plug into the $u$-integral:
$$\int_{F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F} \sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(g) \phi)(\eta^{-1} x) \cdot \psi\!\bigl((\mathrm{Nm}(x) - n) u\bigr) \, du = \sum_{x \in E} (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1} x) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\mathrm{Nm}(x) = n},$$
using $\int_{F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F} \psi(\alpha u) du = \mathrm{vol}(F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\alpha = 0} = \mathbf{1}_{\alpha = 0}$ (orthogonality of characters on the compact group $F\backslash \mathbb{A}_F$; Tamagawa $\mathrm{vol} = 1$ by C3). The conclusion is
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{[E^1]} \chi(\eta) \sum_{x \in E,\, \mathrm{Nm}(x) = n} (\omega_\psi(g) \phi)(\eta^{-1} x) \, d\eta. \tag{$\star$}$$

*(Step 3) $E^1(F)$-orbit unfolding.* The fiber $\mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n) \cap E$:

- **$n = 0$:** $\mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(0) \cap E = \{0\}$ ($\mathrm{Nm}$ is anisotropic on $E/F$). Plugging $x = 0$ into ($\star$): $(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1} \cdot 0) = (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(0)$, independent of $\eta$. So $a_\chi(0; g) = (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(0) \cdot \int_{[E^1]} \chi(\eta) \, d\eta$, proving (i).
- **$n \in F^\times \setminus \mathrm{Nm}(E^\times)$:** $\mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n) \cap E = \emptyset$, so $a_\chi(n; g) = 0$, proving (ii).
- **$n \in F^\times \cap \mathrm{Nm}(E^\times)$:** Pick $\xi_n \in E^\times$ with $\mathrm{Nm}(\xi_n) = n$. Then $\mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n) \cap E = \mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n)\cap E^\times = E^1(F)\cdot \xi_n$ as a *free* $E^1(F)$-orbit (the action of $E^1(F)$ on $E^\times$ by multiplication has trivial point stabilizer). Hence
$$\sum_{x \in E^1(F)\cdot \xi_n} F(x) = \sum_{\gamma \in E^1(F)} F(\gamma\xi_n),$$
with no stabilizer factor. Plugging into ($\star$):
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{[E^1]} \chi(\eta) \sum_{\gamma \in E^1(F)} (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\gamma\xi_n) \, d\eta.$$
Now apply the standard $\Gamma$-unfolding for $\Gamma = E^1(F)$ discrete in $E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)$: for any function $\Phi$ on $E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)$ with $\sum_{\gamma \in \Gamma}|\Phi(\gamma\eta)|$ converging uniformly on $[E^1]$,
$$\int_{[E^1]} \chi(\eta) \sum_{\gamma \in \Gamma} \Phi(\gamma\eta) \, d\eta = \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) \Phi(\eta) \, d\eta$$
(provided $\chi$ is $\Gamma$-invariant: $\chi(\gamma\eta) = \chi(\eta)$ for $\gamma \in E^1(F)$, automatic from automorphy of $\chi$). Apply with $\Phi(\eta) := (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\xi_n)$; the inner sum's uniform convergence on $[E^1]$ inherits from the absolute convergence of $\Theta$ in Prop II.1.b (1) by extracting the $\mathrm{Nm}(x) = n$ subset of $E$ as a discrete subset of the lattice $E \subset \mathbb{A}_E$. Note: the substitution
$$\sum_{\gamma\in\Gamma}(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\gamma\xi_n) = \sum_{\gamma\in\Gamma}\Phi(\gamma^{-1}\eta)$$
followed by the relabeling $\gamma \to \gamma^{-1}$ (a bijection on $\Gamma$ that preserves the sum) gives $\sum_\gamma\Phi(\gamma\eta)$, and yields the $\Gamma$-unfolding identity. Result:
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) \, (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1} \xi_n) \, d\eta,$$
proving (iii). The "special role of squares" (iv) is a corollary observation: for $\xi_n = m \in F$, the change of variable $\eta \to \eta^{-1}$ relates $a_\chi(m^2; g)$ to itself with $\chi$ replaced by $\chi^{-1}$ and $\xi_n$ unchanged (because $E^1$ is abelian and $\bar\eta = \eta^{-1}$ on $E^1$), giving the asymmetric identity in the proposition statement. $\blacksquare$

**Remarks on II.2.a.**

- **(R1) Galois partner and Friedberg–Hoffstein form.** The chunk-level formula uses *one* representative $\xi_n$ of the $E^1(F)$-orbit $\mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n)\cap E^\times$. Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 §1 (over $\mathbb{Q}$) and subsequent Bianchi references typically symmetrize over $\{\xi_n, \bar\xi_n\}$ — the two natural $F$-conjugate choices — yielding the equivalent form
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \tfrac12 \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) \bigl[(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) + (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\bar\xi_n)\bigr] d\eta.$$
This is the same orbital integral (since $\bar\xi_n = \eta_0\xi_n$ with $\eta_0 = \bar\xi_n/\xi_n \in E^1(F)$, the substitution $\eta \to \eta_0^{-1}\eta$ converts the second integrand into the first, with $\chi(\eta_0^{-1}\eta) = \chi(\eta)$ by automorphy); the symmetrization is a *notational* preference for II.2.b downstream factorization.

- **(R2) Local factorization picture.** Choosing $\phi = \otimes_v \phi_v$ factorizable and using $E^1(\mathbb{A}_F) = \prod_v' E^1(F_v)$, the adelic integral factors as a product of local orbital integrals at each place $v$:
$$W_v(g_v; \xi_n) := \int_{E^1(F_v)} \chi_v(\eta_v) (\omega_{\psi_v}(g_v)\phi_v)(\eta_v^{-1} \xi_n) \, d\eta_v.$$
At unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ with $\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$, $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$ gives $W_\mathfrak{p} = \mathrm{vol}(E^1(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}))$ — a constant. At $\mathfrak{p}$ with $v_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n) > 0$, $W_\mathfrak{p}$ is a *Gauss-sum-like* integral: integrate $\chi_v$ over a $\mathcal{O}_v$-orbit of $\xi_n$, giving the Hecke-eigenvalue-like factor $\chi_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n) \cdot |\xi_n|_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^{1/2}$-or-$-1/2$ depending on conductor convention. Computing $W_v$ explicitly at all places is the substance of chunk II.2.b.

- **(R3) Central character compatibility.** A *coarser* vanishing occurs from the central character: $\Theta_\chi(z g) = \chi_V(z) \Theta_\chi(g)$ for $z \in Z(SL_2)(\mathbb{A}_F) = \mu_2$ (the Weil-rep formula at $m(-1)$ — using $\dim V_2 = 2$ even, $\chi_V = \chi_{E/F}$ — gives the central transformation). Combined with $\psi(nu)$-equivariance of $a_\chi(n; \cdot)$, this forces $\chi_V$-compatibility on $n$. For our type-I family ($\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = 1$), this is automatic.

- **(R4) Connection to $L(\tfrac12, \chi)$.** The downstream identity (II.3) — Bianchi Waldspurger formula — relates $|a_\chi(1; g)|^2 / \|\Theta_\chi\|^2_{[GL_2]}$ to $|L(\tfrac12, \chi)|^2$. The $\xi_n = 1$ case (with $n = 1 \in (F^\times)^2$) gives the clean form
$$a_\chi(1; g) = \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}) \, d\eta,$$
the orbital integral whose local factors (in II.2.b) produce the Gauss sums in the Friedberg–Hoffstein closed form. *No spurious $\tfrac12$-factor* (cf. the disowned earlier draft); this comes from using $[E^1]$ rather than $[O(V_2)]$-with-double-cover.

- **(R5) The "$\delta = 1$" case ($\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$).** For self-dual $\chi$ with $\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$ and $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$, the theta-lift target is GL₂-of-$F$ twisted by $\chi_{E/F}$ rather than GL₂ itself; the orbital integral changes by an appropriate twist. The Bianchi cubic-moment family (P11 §6.7) uses the $\delta = 0$ type-I family above, so $\delta = 1$ is not load-bearing for the present project; recorded here only for completeness.

**Done-criterion for chunk II.2.a.** Achieved: the $n$-th Fourier coefficient $a_\chi(n; g)$ of the theta lift $\Theta_\chi$ along $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$ is identified as a single adelic orbital integral $\int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1} \xi_n) d\eta$ over a norm-representative $\xi_n \in \mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n) \cap E$, with vanishing dichotomy on $\mathrm{Nm}(E^\times)$ (no spurious stabilizer factor; this resolves the skeptic-flagged factor-of-2 error in the disowned earlier draft via $[O(V_2)] = [E^1]$). Forward chunks: II.2.b factorizes this orbital integral into local pieces $W_v(g_v; \xi_n)$ and computes each one explicitly using the II.1.d test-function choices, producing the Friedberg–Hoffstein closed form $a_\chi(n) = c \cdot \chi(\xi_n) \cdot |\xi_n|_E^{-1/2} \cdot G_n$ with explicit Gauss-sum factor $G_n$.

### Local factorization (II.2.b — orbital integral $W_v$ at unramified places)

**Motivation.** II.2.a identified the $n$-th Fourier coefficient (for $n \in F^\times \cap \mathrm{Nm}(E^\times)$) as the single adelic orbital integral
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) \, (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) \, d\eta.$$
This chunk factorizes that integral into a product of local pieces $W_v$ at each place $v$ and computes $W_v$ explicitly at every *unramified* place: the archimedean $v = \infty$ (where the answer is a Bessel-K transform of $|\xi_n|$), and the finite $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ (where the answer splits into an *inert* case = constant and a *split* case = geometric-sum Hecke-like factor). The ramified factors at $\mathfrak{p} \mid q$ and at the dyadic $\mathfrak{p}_2$ are deferred (II.1.d.bis and II.4).

**Local Haar measure normalization.** Fix a factorization $d\eta = \prod_v d\eta_v$ of the global Haar measure on $E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)$ as a restricted product of local Haar measures, normalized so that:
- at every finite $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ with $\mathfrak{p}$ inert in $E/F$: $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})$ is compact, $\mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}), d\eta_\mathfrak{p}) = 1$;
- at every finite $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ with $\mathfrak{p}$ split in $E/F$: $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}) \cong F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$ via the split-coordinate parametrization $(t, t^{-1}) \leftrightarrow t$ (see Setup paragraph below), with $d\eta_\mathfrak{p}$ corresponding to the multiplicative Haar measure $d^\times t$ giving $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_\mathfrak{p}^\times, d^\times t) = 1$;
- at $v = \infty$: $E^1(F_\infty) \cong \mathbb{C}^\times$ via the same split-coordinate parametrization (since $\infty$ is split in $E/F$ when $E$ is totally imaginary over $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ — there are two archimedean places of $E$ above the unique $\infty$ of $F$), with $d\eta_\infty = \frac{dr}{r} \cdot \frac{d\theta}{2\pi}$ in polar coordinates $t = r e^{i\theta}$ on $\mathbb{C}^\times$ (the standard $S^1$-normalized multiplicative measure).

These local normalizations differ from the standard Tamagawa measure on $E^1$ by a finite product of correction factors (essentially $L(1, \chi_{E/F})$-type convergence factors at split primes); the discrepancy is a global constant absorbed into the eventual $c_\chi$ in the Bianchi Waldspurger formula and is irrelevant for the *form* of the closed expression.

**Setup at a finite unramified $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ — splitting of $E/F$ at $\mathfrak{p}$.** Recall $\chi$ has conductor $q$ and $E = E_\chi$ has $\mathrm{disc}(E/F) = q$ (R4 of II.1.d). For $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q$ the extension $E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}$ is unramified, hence:

- **Inert case** ($\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ non-trivial): $E_\mathfrak{p}$ is the unramified quadratic extension of $F_\mathfrak{p}$, $\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}/\varpi_\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}} = \mathbb{F}_{q_\mathfrak{p}^2}$, $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}) = \ker(\mathrm{Nm} \colon \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times \to \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^\times)$ is *compact* (since $\mathrm{Nm}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}^k) = \varpi_\mathfrak{p}^{2k}$ on $\varpi_\mathfrak{p}^\mathbb{Z}$ has trivial kernel, $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}) \subset \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$).
- **Split case** ($\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ trivial): $E_\mathfrak{p} = F_\mathfrak{p} \oplus F_\mathfrak{p}$ as $F_\mathfrak{p}$-algebra, $\mathrm{Nm}(a, b) = ab$, $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}) = \{(t, t^{-1}) : t \in F_\mathfrak{p}^\times\} \cong F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$ (non-compact).

In both cases the Galois generator $\sigma$ acts by $\sigma(a, b) = (b, a)$ (split) or by the non-trivial Frobenius (inert).

**Setup of the character $\chi$ at split unramified $\mathfrak{p}$.** Write $\chi_\mathfrak{p}(a, b) = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(a) \cdot \chi^-_\mathfrak{p}(b)$ for the two components of $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ on $E_\mathfrak{p}^\times = F_\mathfrak{p}^\times \times F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$. The two structural hypotheses on $\chi$ — self-dual ($\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$, where here "self-dual" means *conjugate-self-dual* per the auto-induction normalization) and type-I ($\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = 1$) — are globally distinct conditions, but *at a split unramified $\mathfrak{p}$* each separately reduces to the *same local* relation $\chi^-_\mathfrak{p} = (\chi^+_\mathfrak{p})^{-1}$: self-duality at $\mathfrak{p}$ ($\chi^\sigma_\mathfrak{p}(a,b) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}(b,a) = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(b)\chi^-_\mathfrak{p}(a)$ matched against $\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(a,b) = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(a)^{-1}\chi^-_\mathfrak{p}(b)^{-1}$ gives $\chi^-_\mathfrak{p} = (\chi^+_\mathfrak{p})^{-1}$), and type-I at $\mathfrak{p}$ ($\chi^+_\mathfrak{p}\chi^-_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ on the diagonal $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$, also $\chi^-_\mathfrak{p} = (\chi^+_\mathfrak{p})^{-1}$). The global δ-distinction (type-I vs type-II self-dual) is invisible at split $\mathfrak{p}$ and re-enters only at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$. Restricting to $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}) = \{(t, t^{-1})\}$:
$$\chi_\mathfrak{p}\bigl((t, t^{-1})\bigr) = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(t) \cdot \chi^-_\mathfrak{p}(t^{-1}) = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(t) \cdot \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(t) = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(t)^2.$$
With $\chi$ unramified at $\mathfrak{p}$, $\chi^+_\mathfrak{p}$ is determined by its value at $\varpi_\mathfrak{p}$: set
$$\alpha_\mathfrak{p} := \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) \in \mathbb{C}^\times \text{ (unitary).}$$
Then $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{E^1}$ is the unramified character of $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times \cong E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})$ with Satake parameter $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2$.

**Setup of the character $\chi$ at the archimedean place.** At $\infty$ split in $E/F$, write $\chi_\infty(z_1, z_2) = \chi^+_\infty(z_1)\chi^-_\infty(z_2)$ with $\chi^\pm_\infty \colon \mathbb{C}^\times \to S^1$. Every unitary character of $\mathbb{C}^\times$ has the form $z \mapsto (z/|z|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})^k \cdot |z|_\mathbb{C}^{i\tau/2}$ for some $k \in \mathbb{Z}$ and $\tau \in \mathbb{R}$ (here $|z|_\mathbb{C} = z\bar z^\mathbb{C}$, the C3 module character at $\infty$). The same self-dual + type-I argument gives $\chi^-_\infty = (\chi^+_\infty)^{-1}$, hence
$$\chi_\infty\bigl((t, t^{-1})\bigr) = \chi^+_\infty(t)^2.$$
Write $\chi^+_\infty(z) = (z/|z|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})^k |z|_\mathbb{C}^{i\tau/2}$ with $(k, \tau)$ the *spectral parameter* of $\chi$ at infinity.

**Factorization Lemma.** For a factorizable $\phi = \otimes_v \phi_v$ and a global representative $\xi_n \in E^\times$ with $\mathrm{Nm}(\xi_n) = n$, the orbital integral factors:
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \prod_v W_v(g_v; \xi_n), \qquad W_v(g_v; \xi_n) := \int_{E^1(F_v)} \chi_v(\eta) \, (\omega_{\psi_v}(g_v)\phi_v)(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) \, d\eta_v,$$
with the product convergent in the restricted-product sense: at almost all $\mathfrak{p}$ (every $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$), $W_\mathfrak{p}(g_\mathfrak{p}; \xi_n)$ is a constant (1, for $g_\mathfrak{p} \in K_\mathfrak{p}$ and $\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$) and contributes trivially.

*Proof of factorization.* The integrand $\chi(\eta)(\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) = \prod_v \chi_v(\eta_v)(\omega_{\psi_v}(g_v)\phi_v)(\eta_v^{-1}\xi_n)$ factors place-by-place, and $E^1(\mathbb{A}_F) = \prod_v' E^1(F_v)$ is a restricted product with respect to the compact open subgroups $E^1(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}})$. The restricted-product factorization of integrals of factorizable functions is standard (Bump §3.1; Weil "Basic Number Theory" Ch. IV §4). Absolute integrability of each $W_v$ follows from rapid decay of $\phi_v$ at every place (archimedean Schwartz; finite locally constant compact support) combined with compactness or rapid-decay of the integration domain. $\blacksquare$

**Proposition (II.2.b).** With the test function $\phi$ of II.1.d, and for $g_\mathfrak{p} \in K_\mathfrak{p}$ at every unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ (sphericality of $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ gives $\omega_{\psi_\mathfrak{p}}(g_\mathfrak{p})\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$), and for $g_\infty = 1$ at the archimedean place (the general $g_\infty \in K_\infty^{SL_2} = SU(2)$ case requires the minimal-$K$-type matrix coefficient and is deferred — see (R5) and II.1.d (R3)):

**(a) Inert unramified $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$, $\xi_n \in E_\mathfrak{p}$ arbitrary.** $W_\mathfrak{p}(g_\mathfrak{p}; \xi_n) = \mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{v_{\mathfrak{P}}(\xi_n) \geq 0} = \mathbf{1}_{\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$ (using the inert normalization $\mathrm{vol} = 1$). The value depends on $\xi_n$ only through the indicator $\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$, which is automatic when $n = \mathrm{Nm}(\xi_n)$ has $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) \geq 0$ (since at inert $\mathfrak{p}$, $v_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{Nm}(\xi_n)) = 2 v_{\mathfrak{P}}(\xi_n) \geq 0$ iff $\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$).

**(b) Split unramified $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$, $\xi_n = (\alpha, \beta) \in F_\mathfrak{p}^\times \times F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$ with $\alpha\beta = n$.** Let $a := v_\mathfrak{p}(\alpha)$, $b := v_\mathfrak{p}(\beta)$, $c := a + b = v_\mathfrak{p}(n)$. With $\alpha_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p})$:
$$W_\mathfrak{p}(g_\mathfrak{p}; \xi_n) = \sum_{k=-b}^{a} \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2k} = \begin{cases} \dfrac{\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2(a+1)} - \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-2b}}{\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2 - 1}, & \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2 \neq 1, \\[6pt] c + 1, & \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2 = 1. \end{cases}$$
The integration range $-b \leq v_\mathfrak{p}(t) \leq a$ is non-empty iff $a + b \geq 0$, i.e., $c = v_\mathfrak{p}(n) \geq 0$ — automatic under the running assumption $n \in \mathcal{O}_F$ (mixed-sign $(a, b)$ with $a + b \geq 0$ is allowed, e.g., $(a, b) = (-1, c+1)$). The per-place value $W_\mathfrak{p}$ depends on the global choice of $\xi_n$ through the pair $(a, b)$, *not* on $n$ alone; different orbit representatives $\xi_n' = \eta_0 \xi_n$ (with $\eta_0 \in E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})$) shift $(a, b) \to (a + j, b - j)$ for some $j \in \mathbb{Z}$ and multiply $W_\mathfrak{p}$ by $\chi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta_0) = \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2j}$ — see (R3) for the place-by-place cancellation in the global product.

**(c) Archimedean $v = \infty$, $\xi_n \in E_\infty^\times$, $g_\infty = 1$.** Write $\xi_n = (z_1, z_2) \in \mathbb{C}^\times \times \mathbb{C}^\times$ with $z_1 z_2 = n$. Then $W_\infty(1; \xi_n) = 0$ unless $k = 0$ (where $k$ is the $S^1$-weight of $\chi^+_\infty$); when $k = 0$:
$$W_\infty(1; \xi_n) = \int_0^\infty r^{2i\tau} \, e^{-2\pi(r^{-2}|z_1|_\mathbb{C} + r^2|z_2|_\mathbb{C})} \, \frac{dr}{r} = \bigl(|z_1|_\mathbb{C}/|z_2|_\mathbb{C}\bigr)^{i\tau/2} \cdot K_{i\tau}\!\bigl(4\pi |n|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2}\bigr),$$
where $K_{i\tau}$ is the modified Bessel function of the second kind (using $|z_1|_\mathbb{C} \cdot |z_2|_\mathbb{C} = |z_1 z_2|_\mathbb{C} = |n|_\mathbb{C}$; recall $|\cdot|_\mathbb{C} = z\bar z^\mathbb{C}$ per C3, the squared ordinary Euclidean modulus). The phase factor $(|z_1|_\mathbb{C}/|z_2|_\mathbb{C})^{i\tau/2}$ uses the principal real branch of $\log(|z_1|/|z_2|)$ on the positive ray. General $g_\infty \in K_\infty^{SL_2} = SU(2)$: see (R5).

*Note* on $(|z_1|/|z_2|)^{i\tau/2}$: this is a pure phase (unit modulus) that records the ratio of the two archimedean components of $\xi_n$. Substituting $\xi_n \to \bar\xi_n = (z_2, z_1)$ inverts the ratio and conjugates the phase factor; consistent with the global $\chi(\eta_0) = 1$ symmetry of II.2.a (R1).

**Proof of Proposition (II.2.b).**

*Proof of (a) — inert.* For $g_\mathfrak{p} \in K_\mathfrak{p}$, sphericality (II.1.d (IIb)) gives $\omega_{\psi_\mathfrak{p}}(g_\mathfrak{p})\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p} = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$. At an inert prime, $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}) \subset \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$ (the norm-1 condition forces unit valuation), so for $\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$: $\eta^{-1}\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ for all $\eta \in E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})$, and $\phi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) = 1$. For $\xi_n \notin \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$: $\eta^{-1}\xi_n \notin \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ (multiplication by a unit preserves valuation), and $\phi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) = 0$. Hence
$$W_\mathfrak{p}(g_\mathfrak{p}; \xi_n) = \mathbf{1}_{\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}} \cdot \int_{E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})} \chi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta) \, d\eta_\mathfrak{p}.$$
Since $\chi$ is unramified at $\mathfrak{p}$, $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times}$ is trivial, hence trivial on $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}) \subset \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$. Integral $= \mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})) = 1$ by the inert normalization. ✓

*Proof of (b) — split.* For $g_\mathfrak{p} \in K_\mathfrak{p}$: $\omega_{\psi_\mathfrak{p}}(g_\mathfrak{p})\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$ by sphericality. With $\eta = (t, t^{-1})$ and $\xi_n = (\alpha, \beta)$:
$$\eta^{-1}\xi_n = (t^{-1}\alpha, \, t\beta) \in \mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}} = \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}} \oplus \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}} \iff v_\mathfrak{p}(t^{-1}\alpha) \geq 0 \text{ and } v_\mathfrak{p}(t\beta) \geq 0 \iff -b \leq v_\mathfrak{p}(t) \leq a.$$
On this domain, $\chi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta) = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(t)^2$. Decompose $t = \varpi_\mathfrak{p}^k u$ with $u \in \mathcal{O}_\mathfrak{p}^\times$, $k \in \mathbb{Z}$:
$$W_\mathfrak{p}(g_\mathfrak{p}; \xi_n) = \int_{\substack{t \in F_\mathfrak{p}^\times \\ -b \leq v_\mathfrak{p}(t) \leq a}} \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(t)^2 \, d^\times t = \sum_{k = -b}^a \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p})^{2k} \int_{\mathcal{O}_\mathfrak{p}^\times} \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(u)^2 \, d^\times u.$$
$\chi^+_\mathfrak{p}$ unramified at $\mathfrak{p}$ ⇒ $(\chi^+_\mathfrak{p})^2|_{\mathcal{O}_\mathfrak{p}^\times}$ trivial ⇒ inner integral $= \mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_\mathfrak{p}^\times) = 1$ by the split normalization. Hence $W_\mathfrak{p} = \sum_{k=-b}^a \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2k}$. The closed forms follow by summing the geometric series. ✓

*Proof of (c) — archimedean at $g_\infty = 1$.* The Proposition restricts to $g_\infty = 1$ (per the discussion of the minimal-$K$-type subtlety in (R5) and II.1.d (R3)), so $\omega_\psi(1)\phi_\infty = \phi_\infty$ trivially.

In the split coordinates $\eta = (t, t^{-1}) \in E^1(F_\infty) = \mathbb{C}^\times$, $\xi_n = (z_1, z_2)$:
$$\eta^{-1}\xi_n = (t^{-1}z_1, \, t z_2) \in \mathbb{C}^2 = E_\infty.$$
The archimedean test function is $\phi_\infty(x) = e^{-2\pi q_\infty(x)}$ with $q_\infty(z_1, z_2) = |z_1|_\mathbb{C} + |z_2|_\mathbb{C}$ (using II.1.d boxed formula; recall $|w|_\mathbb{C} = w\bar w^\mathbb{C}$, the C3 module-character notation, which equals the squared ordinary Euclidean modulus). Hence
$$\phi_\infty(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) = \exp\bigl(-2\pi(|t^{-1}z_1|_\mathbb{C} + |t z_2|_\mathbb{C})\bigr) = \exp\bigl(-2\pi(|t|_\mathbb{C}^{-1}|z_1|_\mathbb{C} + |t|_\mathbb{C}|z_2|_\mathbb{C})\bigr),$$
using $|t^{-1} z|_\mathbb{C} = |t|_\mathbb{C}^{-1} |z|_\mathbb{C}$ on $\mathbb{C}$.

In polar coordinates $t = r e^{i\theta}$ ($r > 0$, $\theta \in [0, 2\pi)$), $|t|_\mathbb{C} = r^2$ (since $|\cdot|_\mathbb{C} = $ squared ordinary modulus). Hence:
$$\phi_\infty(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) = \exp\bigl(-2\pi(r^{-2}|z_1|_\mathbb{C} + r^2|z_2|_\mathbb{C})\bigr).$$
The character $\chi^+_\infty(t) = (t/|t|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})^k |t|_\mathbb{C}^{i\tau/2} = e^{ik\theta} r^{i\tau}$, so $\chi^+_\infty(t)^2 = e^{2ik\theta} r^{2i\tau}$. With $d^\times t = \frac{dr}{r}\cdot \frac{d\theta}{2\pi}$:
$$W_\infty(1; \xi_n) = \int_0^{2\pi}\frac{d\theta}{2\pi} e^{2ik\theta} \cdot \int_0^\infty \frac{dr}{r} \, r^{2i\tau} \, \exp\bigl(-2\pi(r^{-2}|z_1|_\mathbb{C} + r^2|z_2|_\mathbb{C})\bigr).$$
The $\theta$-integral equals $\delta_{k, 0}$. Assuming $k = 0$: substitute $u = r^2$, $du = 2r dr$, $\frac{dr}{r} = \frac{du}{2u}$:
$$W_\infty(1; \xi_n) = \tfrac12 \int_0^\infty u^{i\tau} \, e^{-2\pi(u^{-1}|z_1|_\mathbb{C} + u|z_2|_\mathbb{C})} \, \frac{du}{u}.$$
Apply the integral representation $\int_0^\infty u^s \, e^{-Au - B/u} \frac{du}{u} = 2 (B/A)^{s/2} K_s\bigl(2\sqrt{AB}\bigr)$ (Gradshteyn–Ryzhik 3.471.9, for $\mathrm{Re}(A), \mathrm{Re}(B) > 0$) with $A = 2\pi|z_2|_\mathbb{C}$, $B = 2\pi|z_1|_\mathbb{C}$, $s = i\tau$: gives $W_\infty = (|z_1|_\mathbb{C}/|z_2|_\mathbb{C})^{i\tau/2} K_{i\tau}(4\pi \sqrt{|z_1|_\mathbb{C}|z_2|_\mathbb{C}})$. Using $\sqrt{|z_1|_\mathbb{C}|z_2|_\mathbb{C}} = |n|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2}$: result follows. ✓ $\blacksquare$

**Corollary (Friedberg–Hoffstein-shape closed form at unramified data).** Assume $n \in \mathcal{O}_F$ with $(n, q\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$ (i.e., $n$ unramified-data-only), and fix a global representative $\xi_n \in E^\times$ with $\mathrm{Nm}(\xi_n) = n$. Then the Fourier coefficient factors as
$$a_\chi(n; g) = W_\infty(1; \xi_n) \cdot \prod_{\substack{\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2 \\ \mathfrak{p} \mid n}} \lambda_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n) \cdot \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \mid q\mathfrak{p}_2} W_\mathfrak{p}(g_\mathfrak{p}; \xi_n),$$
where the unramified-finite-prime factor $\lambda_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n)$ is the Proposition (II.2.b) closed form: at inert $\mathfrak{p}$, $\lambda_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ (regardless of $v_\mathfrak{p}(n)$); at split $\mathfrak{p}$ with $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) = c$, $\lambda_\mathfrak{p} = \sum_{k=-b}^a \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2k}$ depending on the chosen *local* representative $\xi_n|_\mathfrak{p} = (\alpha, \beta)$ with $v_\mathfrak{p}(\alpha) = a$, $v_\mathfrak{p}(\beta) = b$. The product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p} \nmid n, \mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2} W_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ (each factor is 1 at unramified $\mathfrak{p} \nmid n$). The archimedean factor is the Bessel-K transform (c). The ramified factors at $\mathfrak{p} \mid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ are placeholders, filled by II.1.d.bis ($q$-newform Gauss sum) and II.4 (dyadic). **Important.** The individual factors $\lambda_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n)$ at split $\mathfrak{p}$ depend on the global $\xi_n$ (via its local image $(\alpha, \beta)$ at $\mathfrak{p}$) — *not* on $n$ alone. The well-defined $\xi_n$-invariant is the *global product* on the right-hand side: under $\xi_n \to \eta_0 \xi_n$ with $\eta_0 \in E^1(F)$, each $\lambda_\mathfrak{p}$ multiplies by $\chi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta_0)$, and these local twists multiply globally to $\prod_v \chi_v(\eta_0) = \chi(\eta_0) = 1$ (automorphy at $\eta_0 \in E^1(F)$). The Corollary is "$\xi_n$-invariance up to local twist," matching the II.2.a (R1) Galois symmetry.

**Remarks on II.2.b.**

- **(R1) Comparison to Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 over $\mathbb{Q}$.** Friedberg–Hoffstein §1 has (for an imaginary quadratic $E_0/\mathbb{Q}$ with class number 1) an analogous formula $a_\chi(n) = c \cdot \chi(\xi_n) |\xi_n|_{E_0}^{-1/2} G_n$ with Bessel-K archimedean factor and a Gauss-sum finite-prime factor. In our Bianchi setting (over $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, with $E/F$ quadratic — so $E/\mathbb{Q}$ is *quartic*), the split-prime contribution at each finite $\mathfrak{p}$ is a *generalized* Hecke-eigenvalue-like factor $\sum_{k=-b}^a \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2k}$, *not* $\chi(\xi_n)|\xi_n|^{1/2}$ as in the simpler $E_0/\mathbb{Q}$ case. The discrepancy reflects the additional split-vs-inert dichotomy in $E/F$ that isn't present in $E_0/\mathbb{Q}$ (where $\mathfrak{p}$-adic completion is over the rational prime $p$). The closed form "$a_\chi(n) = c \cdot \chi(\xi_n)|\xi_n|_E^{-1/2}G_n$" of the next-chunk advertisement (II.2.a Done-criterion and the long-horizon file) should be read as a *schematic* statement of the closed form's flavor; the actual Bianchi closed form is the product expression above and is more naturally indexed by the inert-vs-split dichotomy.

- **(R2) Hecke eigenvalue interpretation.** At a split unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ with $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) = c \geq 0$ and choosing the canonical representative $\xi_n = (\varpi_\mathfrak{p}^c, 1)$ (so $a = c$, $b = 0$): $W_\mathfrak{p}(1; \xi_n) = \sum_{k=0}^c \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2k} = (\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2(c+1)}-1)/(\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2-1)$. With $\beta_\mathfrak{p} := \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2$, this is a Hecke-like eigenvalue with Satake parameter $\beta_\mathfrak{p}$, *not* with Satake parameter $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}$. The Satake parameters of the auto-induced GL₂/F form $\mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ at a split $\mathfrak{p}$ are $\{\alpha_\mathfrak{p}, \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}\}$ — a *different* Hecke eigenvalue from the one above (which would correspond to a form with Satake parameters $\{\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2, \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-2}\}$). This discrepancy is expected: the theta-lift Fourier coefficient $a_\chi(n)$ is *not* the Hecke eigenvalue of $\mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ at $\mathfrak{p}^c$; the Bianchi Waldspurger formula (II.3) relates $|a_\chi(1)|^2$ to $L(\tfrac12, \chi)$ via a *single* point evaluation, not via a Hecke-eigenvalue identity. The two-power Satake-parameter shift is consistent with the "$\chi \mapsto |L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$" structure rather than a Hecke-eigenvalue correspondence.

- **(R3) Symmetry under $\xi_n \to \bar\xi_n$.** Switching $\xi_n$ to its Galois conjugate sends $(a, b) \to (b, a)$ at split $\mathfrak{p}$ and $(z_1, z_2) \to (z_2, z_1)$ at $\infty$, with the per-place result transforming by a factor of $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2(b-a)}$ at finite $\mathfrak{p}$ and $(|z_2|/|z_1|)^{i\tau}$ at $\infty$. These local factors multiply globally to $\prod_v \chi_v(\eta_0)$ with $\eta_0 = \bar\xi_n/\xi_n \in E^1(F)$, which equals 1 by global automorphy. ✓ Confirms the II.2.a (R1) global symmetry place-by-place.

- **(R4) Spectral support: $k = 0$ at $\infty$.** The archimedean integral (c) vanishes unless $k = 0$, where $k$ is the $S^1$-weight of $\chi^+_\infty$. This corresponds, on the GL₂/F side, to the *unramified principal series* (Maass form) component of $\mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ at infinity, not the discrete-series (holomorphic) component. Since $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ has no real archimedean places, every Hecke character is "of Maass type" and $k = 0$ is the generic case for the Bianchi cubic moment; the $k \neq 0$ vanishing is consistent with the auto-induced form being a Maass form on $GL_2/F$.

- **(R5) Sphericality caveat at $\infty$.** Proposition (II.2.b)(c) is stated for $g_\infty = 1$ only. For general $g_\infty \in K_\infty = SU(2)$, the Weil-rep $\omega_\psi(g_\infty)\phi_\infty$ is *not* equal to $\phi_\infty$ (II.1.d (R3) — only $\omega_\psi(w_\infty)\phi_\infty = \phi_\infty$ with eigenvalue $+1$). The full $K_\infty$-action sends $\phi_\infty$ to a finite-dim "minimal $K$-type" subspace; for general $g_\infty$, $W_\infty(g_\infty; \xi_n)$ is obtained by acting on the (c)-formula by the appropriate $SU(2)$-representation matrix coefficient. The detail is deferred to II.3 (where the cusp-form pairing makes the matrix coefficient explicit) — for II.2.b's purpose of identifying the Friedberg–Hoffstein closed form, evaluating at $g_\infty = 1$ suffices.

**Done-criterion for chunk II.2.b.** Achieved: the adelic orbital integral from II.2.a is factorized place-by-place via the standard restricted-product formalism (Factorization Lemma). The local factor $W_v$ is computed explicitly at every unramified finite place (Proposition II.2.b parts (a) inert + (b) split) and at the archimedean place (part (c) Bessel-K). The Friedberg–Hoffstein closed form is identified in the Corollary, with explicit unramified contributions and placeholders for the ramified $\mathfrak{p} \mid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ factors. Forward chunks: II.1.d.bis specifies the $q$-newform $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ at $\mathfrak{p} \mid q$ and computes the corresponding Gauss-sum factor $W_\mathfrak{p}$; II.4 handles the dyadic $W_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$. Once all $W_v$ are computed, II.3 pairs $\Theta_\chi$ against a Hecke–Maass cusp form on $[GL_2]$ to extract $|L(\tfrac12, \chi)|^2$.

### Ramified factor $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ and local $W_\mathfrak{p}$ (II.1.d.bis)

**Motivation.** II.2.b factorized the adelic orbital integral $a_\chi(n;g) = \prod_v W_v(g_v;\xi_n)$ and computed $W_v$ at every *unramified* place. The Corollary left two ramified placeholders: $W_\mathfrak{p}$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ (where $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ is ramified of conductor $\mathfrak{p}^1$, since $q$ is squarefree) and $W_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ at the dyadic prime (II.4). This chunk fills the $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ placeholder: it specifies $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ as the Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector at the ramified prime and computes $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n)$ as a Gauss-sum-shaped factor.

**Local setup at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$.** Recall (II.1.d (R4)) $q = \mathrm{disc}(E/F)$, so the extension $E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}$ is ramified quadratic (tame, since $\mathfrak{p}\nmid\mathfrak{p}_2$ rules out wild $p = 2$ ramification of the base). Pick a uniformizer $\pi = \pi_\mathfrak{p}$ of $E_\mathfrak{p}$ with $\bar\pi = -\pi$ (canonical for tame quadratic, $E_\mathfrak{p} = F_\mathfrak{p}(\sqrt{D\varpi})$ with $D\in\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$, $\pi = \sqrt{D\varpi}$, $\bar\pi = -\sqrt{D\varpi} = -\pi$); then $\pi^2 = D\varpi$, $\mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(\pi) = \pi\bar\pi = -D\varpi$ has valuation 1, residue field of $E_\mathfrak{p}$ equals that of $F_\mathfrak{p}$ ($e = 2, f = 1$), $\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}} = \pi\mathcal{O}_E$ (tame quadratic), $\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p} = \pi\mathcal{O}_E$ (combining with $\mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p} = \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$ from C2). The self-dual Haar measure on $E_\mathfrak{p}$ has $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E) = |\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p}|^{1/2}_E = q_F^{-1/2}$ where $q_F := |\mathbb{F}_{q_F}|$ is the residue cardinality of $F_\mathfrak{p}$.

**The character $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$.** Since $q$ is squarefree, $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ has conductor exactly $\pi\mathcal{O}_E$ (the unique non-trivial conductor at a tame ramified prime — depth-1 ramification). Hence $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ is trivial on $1 + \pi\mathcal{O}_E$ and factors through $\mathcal{O}_E^\times/(1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E) = (\mathcal{O}_E/\pi\mathcal{O}_E)^\times = \mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ (residue field of $E_\mathfrak{p}$ = residue field of $F_\mathfrak{p}$).

Two global conditions are in play.

**Conjugate-self-duality** ($\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$, $\sigma$ the non-trivial element of $\mathrm{Gal}(E/F)$). For $\eta \in E^\times$, $\chi(\eta)\chi(\bar\eta) = \chi(\mathrm{Nm}(\eta)) = 1$; by local class field theory, $\mathrm{Nm}(\mathbb{A}_E^\times)/F^\times = \ker(\chi_{E/F})$ has index 2 in $\mathbb{A}_F^\times/F^\times$, so $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times}$ factors through $\mathbb{A}_F^\times/\mathrm{Nm}(\mathbb{A}_E^\times) \cong \{\pm 1\}$ and equals either $1$ or $\chi_{E/F}$.

**Two types** for conjugate-self-dual $\chi$:
- **Type-I** (FH 1995 / YZZ 2009 convention): $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$, the quadratic character cutting out $E$.
- **Type-II**: $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = 1$ (Galois-fixed Hecke characters).

**Claim.** For our family — self-dual Hecke characters of conductor exactly $q$ — only Type-I is admissible.

**Argument.** Suppose $\chi$ is Type-II, $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = 1$ globally, hence $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = 1$ locally at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$. Restrict to units: $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times} = 1$. Since $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ has conductor exactly $\pi\mathcal{O}_E$, it factors through $\mathcal{O}_E^\times/(1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E) = \mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ (residue field of $E$ at tame quadratic $=$ residue field of $F$). Now the reduction map $\mathcal{O}_F^\times \twoheadrightarrow (\mathcal{O}_F/\mathfrak{p})^\times = \mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ is *surjective*, identifying the image of $\mathcal{O}_F^\times$ in $\mathcal{O}_E^\times/(1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E)$ with all of $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$. Hence "$\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ trivial on $\mathcal{O}_F^\times$" forces "$\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ trivial on all of $\mathcal{O}_E^\times/(1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E)$" — contradiction with conductor exactly $\pi$.

**Resolution.** The cubic-moment family at conductor $q$ consists of Type-I characters. Locally at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$: $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$, the (ramified) quadratic character at $\mathfrak{p}$ — non-trivial on $\mathcal{O}_F^\times/(1+\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F) = \mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$, kernel the squares. The character $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ descends to a character of $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ whose restriction to the image of $\mathcal{O}_F^\times$ (which is all of $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$) equals the quadratic character of $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$.

**Caveat — retroactive consistency at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$.** Previous chunks (II.2.b and earlier) used "type-I" with $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = 1$, which is the *wrong* convention; the present chunk corrects this. Consistency check at unramified primes:
- **Split unramified $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q$:** $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ is the unramified-quadratic character of $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$, *trivial* on $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$ because $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times \subset \mathrm{Nm}(E_\mathfrak{p}^\times)$ at split places (everything is a norm). So $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = 1$ under either convention; II.2.b (b) split formula unchanged.
- **Inert unramified $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q$:** $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ is the *non-trivial* unramified quadratic character of $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$ (with kernel $\mathrm{Nm}(E_\mathfrak{p}^\times)$ of index 2). The Type-I convention gives $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$, not 1 — *different* from the previous convention. However, II.2.b (a) inert depends only on $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})}$, which is unaffected by the global type (the local norm-1 subgroup is intrinsic to $E_\mathfrak{p}^\times$), and the formula $W_\mathfrak{p} = \mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$ goes through.

Both checks pass for the per-place $W_v$ values stated in II.2.b. The Conventions sheet (II.1.c) is amended below to state the global type definitively as Type-I.

**The test function $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ (Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector).** Define
$$\boxed{\quad \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x) := \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(x) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times}(x), \qquad x \in E_\mathfrak{p}, \quad}$$
where we set $\phi_\mathfrak{p}(x) := 0$ for $x \notin \mathcal{O}_E^\times$ (the formula $\chi^{-1}(x)$ is only defined on units). Equivalently, $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \sum_{\xi \in (\mathcal{O}_E/\pi\mathcal{O}_E)^\times} \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\xi + \pi\mathcal{O}_E}$, a finite sum of (character-twisted) indicators of cosets of $\pi\mathcal{O}_E$ inside $\mathcal{O}_E^\times$. The character $\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$ is well-defined on each coset since $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ has conductor exactly $\pi$.

**Properties of $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$.**

- (a) **Schwartz–Bruhat.** Locally constant on the cosets $\xi + \pi\mathcal{O}_E$ (a finite refinement of $\mathcal{O}_E^\times$); compactly supported on $\mathcal{O}_E^\times \subset \mathcal{O}_E$.

- (b) **$K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-newform on the $SL_2$ side.** Define $K_1(\mathfrak{p}) := \{\gamma \in SL_2(\mathcal{O}_F) : \gamma \equiv \binom{*\ *}{0\ 1} \mod \mathfrak{p}\}$. We verify $\omega_{\psi_\mathfrak{p}}(\gamma) \phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$ for $\gamma$ in $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$'s Bruhat-cell generators:
    - **$n(b)$, $b \in \mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$:** $(\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi_\mathfrak{p})(x) = \psi_\mathfrak{p}(b\cdot \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(x))\phi_\mathfrak{p}(x)$. For $x \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times$, $\mathrm{Nm}(x) \in \mathcal{O}_F^\times$, so $b\cdot\mathrm{Nm}(x) \in \mathcal{O}_F = \mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^{-1}$ (using $\mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}} = \mathcal{O}_F$ at unramified-base $\mathfrak{p}\nmid\mathfrak{p}_2$), hence $\psi_\mathfrak{p}(b\cdot\mathrm{Nm}(x)) = 1$. So $\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$. ✓
    - **$m(a)$, $a \in 1 + \mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}$:** $(\omega_\psi(m(a))\phi_\mathfrak{p})(x) = \chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\cdot|a|_\mathfrak{p}\cdot\phi_\mathfrak{p}(ax)$. With $a \equiv 1 \mod \mathfrak{p}$: $|a|_\mathfrak{p} = 1$; $\chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}}(a) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a) = 1$ (since $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ has conductor $\mathfrak{p}$, trivial on $1+\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F$); $\phi_\mathfrak{p}(ax) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(ax)\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(ax) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(a)\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(x)\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x) = 1 \cdot \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x)$ (using $\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(a) = 1$ since $a \in 1+\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_E$ and $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ has conductor $\pi$). So $\omega_\psi(m(a))\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$. ✓
    - **Iwahori upper-triangular:** $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$ is generated topologically by $\{n(b) : b \in \mathcal{O}_F\}$, $\{m(a) : a \in 1+\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F\}$, and $\{\bar n(c) : c \in \mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F\}$ (lower unipotent at level $\mathfrak{p}$). The third generator $\bar n(c)$ for $c \in \mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F$: write $\bar n(c) = w^{-1} n(-c) w$, so $(\omega_\psi(\bar n(c))\phi_\mathfrak{p})(x) = (\omega_\psi(w^{-1})\omega_\psi(n(-c))\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p})(x)$. With $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ computed in (d) below as $G_\mathfrak{p} \cdot \phi'_\mathfrak{p}$ for a Gauss sum $G_\mathfrak{p}$ and a related $\phi'_\mathfrak{p}$ supported on $\pi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times$ (the "Atkin-Lehner-transformed" newvector), the action of $\bar n(c)$ for $c \in \mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F$ multiplies $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ by $\psi(c\cdot\mathrm{Nm}(x))$ in the Schrödinger model on $\pi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times$; for $x \in \pi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times$, $\mathrm{Nm}(x) \in \pi^{-2}\mathcal{O}_F^\times = D^{-1}\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_F^\times$, hence $c\cdot\mathrm{Nm}(x) \in \mathfrak{p}\cdot\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_F^\times \subset \mathcal{O}_F$, trivializing $\psi$. So $\omega_\psi(\bar n(c))$ fixes $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ as well. ✓

Together: $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant, the local Hecke-newform condition for ramified $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ at depth 1.

- (c) **Atkin-Lehner / $m(a)$ for $a \in \mathcal{O}_F^\times$:** For $a \in \mathcal{O}_F^\times$ (not in $1+\mathfrak{p}$), the analogous calculation gives $(\omega_\psi(m(a))\phi_\mathfrak{p}) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a) \cdot \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(a) \cdot \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a) \cdot \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}^{-1}(a) \cdot \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x) = \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x)$ — using $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ from the type adjustment. So in fact $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is invariant under the full $K_0(\mathfrak{p}) = \{c \equiv 0\}$ on its diagonal Bruhat piece (a stronger statement than $K_1$-invariance). The central character of the Weil-rep restricted to $K_0(\mathfrak{p})/K_1(\mathfrak{p}) \cong (\mathcal{O}_F/\mathfrak{p})^\times = \mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ is *trivial* — consistent with the type adjustment, $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ canceling against $\chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}}(a) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)$ in the Weil-rep formula.

- (d) **$w$-eigenvalue is a Gauss sum.** Compute $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ via:
$$\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(y) = \int_{E_\mathfrak{p}}\phi_\mathfrak{p}(x)\psi_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{tr}_{E/F}(x\bar y))dx = \int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(x)\psi_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{tr}(x\bar y))dx.$$
By a standard Tate-style computation (carried out below): $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(y) = G(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p}) \cdot \chi_\mathfrak{p}(\pi y) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\pi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(y)$, where $G(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})$ is the local Gauss sum
$$G(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p}) := \int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times} \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(x) \psi_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{tr}(x/\pi)) \, dx = q_F^{-1/2} \sum_{x \in (\mathcal{O}_E/\pi)^\times} \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(x)\psi_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{tr}(x/\pi)),$$
absolute value $|G(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})| = 1$ (standard Gauss-sum modulus, using Tate-self-dual normalization). Hence
$$\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}(x) = \gamma_\mathfrak{p}(\psi_\mathfrak{p}, V_2)\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(x) = G(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p}) \cdot \gamma_\mathfrak{p}(\psi_\mathfrak{p}, V_2) \cdot \chi_\mathfrak{p}(\pi x) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\pi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x),$$
the Atkin-Lehner-transformed newvector at level $\pi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times = $ "the depth-(-1) shell." The Gauss-sum prefactor $G(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})$ is the substantive content; the local Weil index $\gamma_\mathfrak{p}(\psi_\mathfrak{p}, V_2) \in \mu_4$ is a sign-correction recorded in (II.1.d) for general $V_2$.

*Computation of $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$.* For $y \in E_\mathfrak{p}$, write $\bar y = \pi^m v$ with $v \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times$ and $m = v_{\mathfrak{P}}(\bar y) = v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y)$. Substituting $u = x v$ (over $\mathcal{O}_E^\times$) — since multiplication by $v$ preserves $\mathcal{O}_E^\times$ — gives $x = uv^{-1}$, $x\bar y = u\pi^m$, and
$$\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(y) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}(v) \int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(u)\psi_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^m))du,$$
where we used $\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(uv^{-1}) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(u)\chi_\mathfrak{p}(v)$. The integral depends only on $m$. Now:
- $m \geq 0$: $u\pi^m \in \mathcal{O}_E$, $\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^m) \in \mathfrak{d}_{E/F}^{-1}\cap F$. For $m \geq 1$, $u\pi^m \in \pi\mathcal{O}_E$, $\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^m) \in \pi\mathcal{O}_E\cap F = \varpi\mathcal{O}_F$ (using $\mathrm{tr}(\pi\mathcal{O}_E) = $ image of $\pi\mathcal{O}_E$ under trace), so $\psi_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^m)) = 1$. Then $\int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(u)du = 0$ since $\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}|_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ is non-trivial. For $m = 0$: $u\pi^0 = u \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times$, $\mathrm{tr}(u) \in \mathcal{O}_F$, $\psi(\mathrm{tr}(u)) = 1$. Again $\int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\chi^{-1}(u)du = 0$. So $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(y) = 0$ for $m \geq 0$, i.e., $y \in \mathcal{O}_E$.
- $m = -1$: $u\pi^{-1} \in \pi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E$. $\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^{-1}) = u\pi^{-1} + \bar u\bar\pi^{-1} = u\pi^{-1} - \bar u\pi^{-1} = (u-\bar u)/\pi$. Coordinate computation: write $u = a + b\pi$ with $a\in\mathcal{O}_F^\times$, $b \in \mathcal{O}_F$ (so $u \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times$ iff $a \in \mathcal{O}_F^\times$); then $u - \bar u = 2b\pi$, $(u-\bar u)/\pi = 2b \in \mathcal{O}_F$. Also $\chi^{-1}(u) = \chi^{-1}(a(1+(b/a)\pi)) = \chi^{-1}(a)$ (using $\chi$ trivial on $1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E$). Under Type-I, $\chi^{-1}|_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}^{-1}|_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}|_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}$. The integrand thus factors:
$$\int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\chi^{-1}(u)\psi(\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^{-1}))du = q_F^{-1/2}\int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\,da \cdot \int_{\mathcal{O}_F}\psi(2b)\,db,$$
where the volume factor $q_F^{-1/2} = \mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E)/\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_F)^2$ comes from $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E) = q_F^{-1/2}$ (Tate self-dual measure at tame ramified, $|\mathfrak{d}_{E/\mathbb{Q}_p}|^{1/2} = q_F^{-1/2}$) versus $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_F) = 1$. **The two integrals do not both vanish:** at $\mathfrak{p}\nmid 2$ (odd residue, our case since $\mathfrak{p}\nmid\mathfrak{p}_2$), $2\in\mathcal{O}_F^\times$, so $\psi(2\cdot)$ has the same conductor as $\psi$ on $F_\mathfrak{p}$ (namely $\mathfrak{d}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^{-1} = \mathcal{O}_F$), hence is trivial on $\mathcal{O}_F$, and $\int_{\mathcal{O}_F}\psi(2b)db = \mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_F) \neq 0$. The vanishing of $\widehat\phi(y)$ at $m=-1$ comes *solely* from the $a$-integral: $\int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)da = 0$ by character orthogonality on $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ non-trivial on $\mathcal{O}_F^\times$. So $\widehat\phi(y) = 0$ at $v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y) = -1$.

- $m \leq -2$: at deeper levels the trace splits by parity of $m$:
    - **Even $m = -2k$, $k\geq 1$**: $\bar\pi^m = \pi^m$ (even power), $\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^m) = (u+\bar u)\pi^m = 2a\pi^m$, depends *only on $a$*. At $m = -2$: $\pi^{-2} = (D\varpi)^{-1}$, $\psi(2a/(D\varpi))$ is a non-trivial additive character of $a\in\mathcal{O}_F^\times$ with conductor $\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$ — paired with $\chi^{-1}(a) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)$ this is a genuine Gauss sum $G_a := \int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\psi(2a/(D\varpi))da \neq 0$. The $b$-integral is $\int_{\mathcal{O}_F}db = 1$. Hence $\widehat\phi$ is non-zero at $m = -2$.
    - **Odd $m \leq -3$**: $\bar\pi^m = -\pi^m$, $\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^m) = (u-\bar u)\pi^m = 2b\pi^{m+1}$, depends only on $b$. The $a$-integral $\int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)da = 0$ kills it.
    - **Even $m \leq -4$**: $\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^m) = 2a\pi^m$, $\psi(2a\pi^m)$ has conductor $\mathfrak{p}^{m/2} \subset \mathfrak{p}^{-2}$ — *deeper* than $\chi$'s conductor on $\mathcal{O}_F^\times$. Standard coset-decomposition argument: $\int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\psi(2a\pi^m)da = 0$ because the $\psi$-conductor exceeds $\chi$'s, so $\chi$ averaging on principal-unit cosets of $\mathcal{O}_F^\times$ kills the integral.

**Refined diagnosis.** $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ is supported precisely at $v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y) = -2$, NOT at $-1$. The structural reason: the trace pairing on tame quadratic $E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}$ alternates "depends on $b$" (odd $m$) vs "depends on $a$" (even $m$), and the Gauss sum requires *alignment* of the $\chi$-coordinate (= $a$, since $\chi$ on $\mathcal{O}_E^\times$ descends to $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ through the $a$-residue) with the $\psi$-coordinate. Alignment first occurs at $m = -2$ (where the additive character is at depth $-1$ in $\varpi$, the right depth to match $\chi$'s conductor-1 in $\mathfrak{p}$). The depth-(-1) shell is the wrong place to seek a Gauss sum eigenvector.

**Caveat — author's earlier conjectured fix was wrong.** An earlier draft of this chunk proposed $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}}(x) := \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\pi x)\mathbf{1}_{\pi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x)$ at depth $-1$ as the "correct" Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector, and proposed a "quadratic-form vs trace pairing" distinction as the structural reason. **Both are wrong.** First, at $\mathfrak{p}\nmid 2$ the symmetric-bilinear form $\mathrm{Nm}(x,y) = \tfrac12\mathrm{tr}(x\bar y)$ agrees with the trace pairing up to the unit $\tfrac12 \in \mathcal{O}_F^\times$, so the trace-vs-quadratic distinction is moot at odd-residue primes — it cannot resolve the depth-0 vanishing. Second, by isometry of $\omega_\psi(w)$ (in particular $\omega_\psi(w)\phi^{(0)} \neq 0$ since $\phi^{(0)} \neq 0$), the Fourier-transform support cannot be empty; the calculation above pinpoints it at $m = -2$, not $-1$. **The correct depth-of-support for the FH newvector at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ in this Weil model is $v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y) = -2$**, equivalently $v_\mathfrak{p} = -1$ in the $\varpi$-normalization of $F$. The natural candidate is
$$\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}(x) := \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\varpi x) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\pi^2 x)\mathbf{1}_{\pi^{-2}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x),$$
the Atkin-Lehner translate of $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ by the $\varpi$-scaling. Under this prescription, the Schrödinger Fourier transform sends $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$ back to a $\chi$-twisted function on $\mathcal{O}_E^\times$ with Gauss-sum prefactor $G_a$. The "?" marks the prescription as a *conjecture* requiring verification in II.1.d.bis.2 — including the $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariance check and the explicit eigenvalue calculation.

**Status of this chunk.** Partial. Achieved: (a) Type-I global convention $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ established and retroactively checked at split + inert unramified primes; (b) depth-0 ansatz $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^{-1}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ specified and $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariance verified; (c) orbital integral $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\cdot\mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}))$ derived under depth-0 ansatz; (d) **Fourier-transform-support diagnosis** showing $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ supported at $v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y) = -2$, NOT at $-1$; (e) *conjectured* correct FH newvector $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$ at depth -2, formal verification deferred to II.1.d.bis.2.

**Partial result on $W_\mathfrak{p}$.** Under the (incorrect-newvector but Hecke-invariant) $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^{-1}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ choice, the orbital integral at $g_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ is:
$$W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \int_{E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})}\chi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta)\phi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta^{-1}\xi_n)d\eta_\mathfrak{p}.$$
For $\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times$ (i.e., $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) = 0$): $\eta^{-1}\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times$ for $\eta \in E^1 \subset \mathcal{O}_E^\times$; $\phi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) = \chi^{-1}(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) = \chi(\eta)\chi^{-1}(\xi_n)$. Hence
$$W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi_n)\int_{E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})}\chi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta)^2 d\eta_\mathfrak{p}.$$
Now $\chi_\mathfrak{p}^2|_{E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})}$: claim this is trivial. Two-step argument.

*Step 1: image of $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})$ in residues is $\{\pm 1\}$.* The residue map $\mathcal{O}_E^\times \twoheadrightarrow \mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ has kernel $1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E$. Since $\bar\pi = -\pi$ and $-1 \in F$, the Galois generator $\sigma$ acts on $\mathcal{O}_E/\pi\mathcal{O}_E = \mathbb{F}_{q_F}$ as $\sigma(a + b\pi \mod \pi) = a - b\pi \mod \pi = a \mod \pi$ (the $b\pi$ part lies in $\pi\mathcal{O}_E$ regardless of sign). So $\sigma$ is *trivial on the residue field* at ramified tame quadratic. The norm-1 condition $\eta\bar\eta = 1$ on residues becomes $\bar\eta\cdot\eta = 1$ with $\bar\eta = \eta$ — i.e., $\eta^2 = 1$ in $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$. For odd $q_F$ (always at $\mathfrak{p}\nmid 2 = \mathfrak{p}\nmid\mathfrak{p}_2$), the 2-torsion in $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ is $\{\pm 1\}$. So the image of $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})$ in $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ is $\{\pm 1\}$, and $E^1/(E^1\cap(1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E)) = \{\pm 1\}$.

*Step 2: $\chi^2$ trivial on $\{\pm 1\}\subset E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})$.* Both $\pm 1 \in F^\times$, so $\chi(\pm 1) = \chi|_{F^\times}(\pm 1) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(\pm 1)$ under the Type-I convention. The quadratic character $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ takes values in $\{\pm 1\}$, so $\chi^2(\pm 1) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(\pm 1)^2 = 1$. Combined with $\chi^2$ trivial on the principal-unit subgroup $1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E$ (inherited from $\chi$): $\chi^2|_{E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})} = 1$. (In fact $\chi|_{E^1} = 1$ via $\chi(\pm 1) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(\pm 1) \in \{\pm 1\}$ — at odd residue $-1$ is a square in $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ since $q_F$ is odd and $|\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times| = q_F - 1$ is even, hence $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(-1) = 1$. We use only the weaker $\chi^2|_{E^1} = 1$.)

Hence
$$W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi_n) \cdot \mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})), \qquad (v_\mathfrak{p}(n) = 0, \xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times).$$
For $\xi_n \notin \mathcal{O}_E^\times$ (i.e., $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) \neq 0$): $\eta^{-1}\xi_n \in \pi^k\mathcal{O}_E^\times \setminus \mathcal{O}_E^\times$ for some $k \neq 0$, so $\phi_\mathfrak{p}(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) = 0$, hence $W_\mathfrak{p} = 0$.

**Conclusion for II.1.d.bis (under the depth-0 ansatz).**
$$\boxed{\quad W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}))\cdot \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi_n) \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\xi_n \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times},\quad}$$
the *local twist* of the orbital integral by $\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$ at the unit components. The factor $\mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p}))$ is normalized to 1 by the analog of the inert-prime normalization in II.2.b.

**Remarks on II.1.d.bis.**

- **(R1) Local-newvector caveat.** The depth-0 ansatz $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^{-1}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ is $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant and gives a clean orbital integral $W_\mathfrak{p}$, but it is *not* the canonical Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector: $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ is supported at $v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y) = -2$, not at $-1$. The conjectured correct newvector is $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}(x) := \chi^{-1}(\varpi x)\mathbf{1}_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x)$ at depth $-2$; the $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariance and explicit Gauss-sum $\omega_\psi(w)$-eigenvalue are deferred to **follow-up chunk II.1.d.bis.2**.

- **(R2) Convention adjustment.** The previous-chunk "type-I" convention $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = 1$ was the *wrong* convention at ramified primes — it forces $\chi|_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times} = 1$ at every ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, which combined with conductor-exactly-$\mathfrak{p}$ leads to a contradiction. The correct convention for self-dual + conjugate-self-dual Hecke characters of conductor $q$ is $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ (the global quadratic character cutting out $E$). This is the standard convention in Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 §1 and YZZ 2009. The II.2.b results (at split *unramified* $\mathfrak{p}$) are unaffected because $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ is trivial there.

- **(R3) Symbol $G(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})$.** Reserved for the Gauss sum that emerges from the *correct* newvector $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$ at depth $-2$ in II.1.d.bis.2; concretely $G_a = \int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\psi(2a/(D\varpi))da$. Modulus 1 (standard Tate-self-dual normalization). The dependence on $\chi$'s local twist is the substantive bit; the dependence on $\psi$ is conventional-only (normalization of additive character).

- **(R4) $\xi_n$-dependence.** Under the depth-0 ansatz, $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi_n)$ depends on $\xi_n$ through its $\mathfrak{p}$-local image as a unit. Under $\xi_n \to \eta_0\xi_n$ with $\eta_0 \in E^1(F)$: $W_\mathfrak{p}$ multiplies by $\chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\eta_0)$, which globally multiplies to $\chi^{-1}(\eta_0) = 1$ (automorphy at $\eta_0 \in E^1(F)$ ⇒ $\chi(\eta_0) = 1$, hence $\chi^{-1}(\eta_0) = 1$). The II.2.b (R3) cancellation extends to the ramified factor. ✓

**Done-criterion for chunk II.1.d.bis.** Partial. Achieved: (i) local setup at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ (uniformizer $\pi$, residue field, character conductor); (ii) corrected Type-I convention $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ (rigorous "Claim / Argument / Resolution" derivation, retroactive consistency check at split and inert unramified primes); (iii) test-function $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^{-1}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ (depth-0 ansatz); (iv) $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariance on $n(b), m(a\equiv 1\mod\mathfrak{p}), m(a\in\mathcal{O}_F^\times), \bar n(c\in\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F)$ Bruhat generators; (v) orbital integral $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\cdot\mathrm{vol}(E^1)$, via two-step proof that $\chi^2|_{E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})} = 1$ ($\bar\pi = -\pi$ ⇒ Galois trivial on residues ⇒ $E^1$-image $= \{\pm 1\}\subset\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$; $\chi^2(\pm 1) = 1$); (vi) **Fourier-transform support diagnosis** via parity decomposition $m \in \mathbb{Z}$: $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ supported at $v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y) = -2$ (NOT $-1$), where a genuine Gauss sum $G_a := \int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\psi(2a/(D\varpi))da$ emerges. Earlier conjectured fix at depth $-1$ was wrong (so was the "trace vs quadratic-form pairing" structural explanation — moot at odd-residue $\mathfrak{p}$). Not achieved: (vii) the formal $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariance + explicit Gauss-sum $\omega_\psi(w)$-eigenvalue for the *conjectured* correct newvector $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}(x) = \chi^{-1}(\varpi x)\mathbf{1}_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x)$ at depth $-2$, deferred to II.1.d.bis.2. Forward chunks: II.1.d.bis.2 ($\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$ verification + Gauss-sum computation) and II.4 (dyadic).

**Note added 2026-05-16 (session 9, II.1.d.bis.2):** Item (vii) above is reversed below in §Atkin-Lehner translate. The conjectured "depth-$-2$ FH newvector" $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$ is NOT a separate newvector — it is precisely $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$, the Atkin-Lehner translate of the depth-0 $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$. By Casselman uniqueness, the depth-0 $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ IS the unique-up-to-scalar Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$. The session-8 framing was a mis-identification; see II.1.d.bis.2 for the corrected derivation.

### Atkin-Lehner translate $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ and Casselman reversal (II.1.d.bis.2)

**Reversal of session-8 mis-identification.** Session 8 (II.1.d.bis above) concluded that the depth-0 $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ is "not the canonical Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector" because $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ is supported at $v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y) = -2$, and conjectured a "depth-$-2$ FH newvector" $\phi^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}_\mathfrak{p}(x) = \chi^{-1}(\varpi x)\mathbf{1}_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x)$.

**This chunk reverses that conclusion.** The depth-0 $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ IS the canonical Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector. The "$\phi^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}_\mathfrak{p}$ at depth $-2$" is *not* a separate newvector — it is precisely the *Atkin-Lehner translate* $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ (up to a Gauss-sum scalar). There is no second newvector; the depth-shift in $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ is the Atkin-Lehner phenomenon, not a sign that the depth-0 ansatz failed.

**Two-vs-one $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-line argument (more careful than session-9 first draft).** The full Casselman-type uniqueness statement requires the conductor of the local theta-lift representation $\pi^{\mathrm{theta}}_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ on $SL_2(F_\mathfrak{p})$, which involves a subtle local-Howe / dihedral-supercuspidal calculation. The Bianchi-side correspondent of $\chi_\mathfrak{p}$ (depth-1 ramified Hecke character on the ramified quadratic $E_\mathfrak{p}$) under the local Howe map $(SL_2, O(V_2))$ produces a representation whose $GL_2$-similitude lift is $\mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi_\mathfrak{p})$ — typically a *dihedral supercuspidal* of $GL_2(F_\mathfrak{p})$ of conductor $\mathfrak{p}^{1+d_{E/F}} = \mathfrak{p}^2$ (Tunnell / Bushnell-Kutzko conductor formula for induced parameters from ramified quadratic). The $SL_2$-side conductor may equal $\mathfrak{p}$ or $\mathfrak{p}^2$ depending on the precise $K$-type decomposition under restriction.

The argument we actually need is *weaker* than full Casselman uniqueness and is established directly below: the depth-0 $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ and the depth-$-2$ $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ are NOT both $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant (the second is not, by direct check). So the session-8 picture — "$\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is *not* the FH newvector because $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ lives at depth $-2$, and there must be a separate FH newvector at depth $-2$" — is incorrect for an entirely concrete reason: the depth-$-2$ Schrödinger function is $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p}) = wK_1(\mathfrak{p})w^{-1}$-invariant (the *transposed* Iwahori), NOT $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant. The two functions live on *different* parahoric-invariant lines; they are exchanged by the Weyl element $w$ (= Atkin-Lehner involution at the ramified prime).

**Status of the "newvector" label for $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$.** We do *not* claim Casselman-uniqueness within $\pi^{\mathrm{theta}}_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ in the strong form $\dim\pi^{K_1(\mathfrak{p})} = 1$ (this depends on the $SL_2$-conductor of the local lift, which we do not pin down here). We do claim:
- $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is a $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant vector in $\pi^{\mathrm{theta}}_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ (verified in II.1.d.bis (b)).
- $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is the canonical "FH-style" choice realizing the Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 Fourier-expansion structure (the over-$\mathbb{Q}$ analog with cusp-$\infty$ coefficient $\chi(\sqrt{n})$ on $n$ coprime to $D$, Gauss-sum cocycle at the Atkin-Lehner side).
- The depth-$-2$ "$\phi^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$" of session 8 is *not* a $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant vector (direct check below), so it cannot be a "second newvector" in the strict Casselman sense. It IS the Atkin-Lehner translate $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$, $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant.

These three statements suffice to reverse the session-8 mis-identification without needing the full Casselman / dihedral-supercuspidal conductor calculation.

**Why session-8's "depth-shift" reasoning was wrong.** Session 8's implicit argument was: the FH newvector should be the function whose Schrödinger Fourier transform sits at the "same" depth (so that $\omega_\psi(w)$ acts by a scalar), and since $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ is supported at depth $-2$ rather than depth $0$, $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ couldn't be the newvector. This conflates two distinct properties:
- $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariance — the *newvector* condition (parahoric fixed line, 1-dimensional by Casselman).
- $\omega_\psi(w)$-eigenvector — the *Atkin-Lehner* condition (eigenline of the Weyl element).

A $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-newvector at conductor $\mathfrak{p}^1$ in a *ramified* principal series is generically NOT an $\omega_\psi(w)$-eigenvector — it transforms under $\omega_\psi(w)$ into the $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p}) = w K_1(\mathfrak{p})w^{-1}$-invariant line (a different parahoric), with a Gauss-sum prefactor. This is the standard Atkin-Lehner involution exchanging the two cusps of $\Gamma_1(\mathfrak{p})\backslash\mathbb{H}^3$. The newvector and its Atkin-Lehner image are both 1-dimensional invariant lines, but for different parahoric subgroups ($K_1$ vs $K_1^{op}$), realized in the Schrödinger model at *different shells* of $E_\mathfrak{p}$.

**Computation of $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$.** The session-8 calculation locating $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}$ at $v_{\mathfrak{P}}(y) = -2$ gives the explicit formula. At $y \in E_\mathfrak{p}$ with $\bar y = \pi^{-2}v$, $v \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times$, the parity-of-$m$ derivation (§II.1.d.bis, item 8) gives
$$\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(y) = \chi(v)\cdot\int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\chi^{-1}(u)\psi(\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^{-2}))du.$$
Decomposing $u = a + b\pi$ with $a \in \mathcal{O}_F^\times$, $b \in \mathcal{O}_F$: $\mathrm{tr}(u\pi^{-2}) = 2a\pi^{-2} = 2a/(D\varpi)$, $\chi^{-1}(u) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)$ (Type-I + $\chi$ trivial on $1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E$). The integral factors as
$$\int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\cdots du = q_F^{-1/2}\int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\psi(2a/(D\varpi))da \cdot \int_{\mathcal{O}_F}db = q_F^{-1/2}\cdot G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}\cdot 1,$$
where $q_F^{-1/2}$ is the Jacobian $du = q_F^{-1/2}\,da\,db$ from $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E) = q_F^{-1/2}\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_F)^2$ (Tate self-dual measure at tame ramified, $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E) = |\mathfrak{d}_{E_\mathfrak{p}/\mathbb{Q}_p}|^{1/2}_E = q_F^{-1/2}$ and $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_F) = 1$ at unramified-base $\mathfrak{p}\nmid\mathfrak{p}_2$), and
$$G_a^{\mathrm{raw}} := \int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\psi(2a/(D\varpi))da$$
is the local Gauss sum at conductor 1.

To re-express in canonical form involving $y$ directly: $v = \bar y\pi^2 = \bar y D\varpi$, so $\chi(v) = \chi(\bar y)\chi(D\varpi)$. Conjugate-self-duality $\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$ gives $\chi(\bar y) = \chi^{-1}(y)$. For $y \in \varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times$, $\varpi y \in \mathcal{O}_E^\times$ and $\chi^{-1}(\varpi y) = \chi^{-1}(\varpi)\chi^{-1}(y)$. Substituting:
$$\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}}(y) = q_F^{-1/2}\chi(D)\chi(\varpi)^2 G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}\cdot \chi^{-1}(\varpi y)\mathbf{1}_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(y).$$
