Under Type-I, $\chi|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$, so $\chi(\varpi) = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(\varpi)$ and $\chi(\varpi)^2 = 1$ (since $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ is order 2). Define the *Atkin-Lehner-translated function*
$$\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{AL}}(x) := \chi^{-1}(\varpi x)\cdot\mathbf{1}_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x), \qquad \text{(supported at } v_{\mathfrak{P}} = -2 \text{ shell)}$$
and the *Atkin-Lehner-Gauss scalar*
$$\mathcal{G}(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p}) := q_F^{-1/2}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(D)\cdot G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}.$$
Then
$$\boxed{\quad \omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} \;=\; \gamma_\mathfrak{p}(\psi_\mathfrak{p}, V_2)\cdot\mathcal{G}(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})\cdot\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{AL}}, \quad}$$
where $\gamma_\mathfrak{p}(\psi_\mathfrak{p}, V_2) \in \mu_4$ is the local Weil index from II.1.d (carrying a sign-correction $\pm 1$ or $\pm i$ depending on the local Hilbert symbol $(D, -1)_\mathfrak{p}$ — explicit value not load-bearing for $|\mathcal{G}|$).

**Modulus of $\mathcal{G}$.** Discretize the $a$-integral via $\mathcal{O}_F^\times = \bigsqcup_{\bar a\in\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times}(a_0 + \mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F)$ (one representative per residue coset). On each coset, both $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ (trivial on $1+\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F$, multiplicative-conductor exponent 1) and $\psi(2\cdot/(D\varpi))$ (trivial on $\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F$, additive-conductor exponent 1: $2/(D\varpi)\in\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_F^\times$ pairs with $\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F$ to give $\mathcal{O}_F$ where $\psi$ is trivial) are constant. With $\mathrm{vol}(\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F) = q_F^{-1}$:
$$G_a^{\mathrm{raw}} = q_F^{-1}\sum_{\bar a\in\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times}\chi_{E/F}(\bar a)\psi(2\bar a/(D\varpi)).$$
The inner sum is a classical Gauss sum $g(\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}},\psi^{(D)}_\mathfrak{p})$ of modulus $|g| = q_F^{1/2}$ (standard Plancherel on $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}$ for a non-trivial multiplicative character paired with a non-trivial additive character). Hence
$$|G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}| = q_F^{-1}\cdot q_F^{1/2} = q_F^{-1/2}, \qquad |\mathcal{G}(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})| = q_F^{-1/2}\cdot q_F^{-1/2} = q_F^{-1}.$$

**Weil-isometry consistency check (NOT independent of the Plancherel calc).** Under self-dual Haar on $E_\mathfrak{p}$:
$$\|\phi_\mathfrak{p}\|^2 = \int_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}|\chi^{-1}(x)|^2\,dx = \mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E^\times) = (1-q_F^{-1})\cdot q_F^{-1/2},$$
$$\|\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{AL}}\|^2 = \int_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}|\chi^{-1}(\varpi x)|^2\,dx = \mathrm{vol}(\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times) = q_F^2\cdot(1-q_F^{-1})q_F^{-1/2},$$
using $|\varpi|_E = q_F^{-2}$ (so multiplying support by $\varpi^{-1}$ multiplies volume by $q_F^2$). Weil-isometry requires $\|\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}\| = \|\phi_\mathfrak{p}\|$, i.e.,
$$|\gamma_\mathfrak{p}|^2\cdot|\mathcal{G}|^2\cdot\|\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}\|^2 = 1\cdot |\mathcal{G}|^2 \cdot q_F^2(1-q_F^{-1})q_F^{-1/2} \overset{!}{=} (1-q_F^{-1})q_F^{-1/2} \implies |\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1}. \quad \checkmark$$
**Caveat (circularity):** Both this isometry derivation AND the direct Plancherel calculation above rely on the same volume convention $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E) = q_F^{-1/2}$ (Tate self-dual at tame ramified $E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}$). The two derivations therefore are not *logically independent* — the consistency check above is a bookkeeping verification that the substitution chain in the Atkin-Lehner computation is internally consistent (no missing volume factors), not a second-source verification of the Gauss-sum modulus. The Plancherel calculation of $|G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}| = q_F^{-1/2}$ is the source of truth.

**Verification $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant.** The opposite parahoric is $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p}) := wK_1(\mathfrak{p})w^{-1}$. Explicitly: $K_1(\mathfrak{p}) = \{\binom{a\,b}{c\,d}\in SL_2(\mathcal{O}_F) : c\equiv 0, d\equiv 1\mod\mathfrak{p}\}$, and conjugating by $w = \binom{0\,1}{-1\,0}$ sends $\binom{a\,b}{c\,d}\mapsto\binom{d\,-c}{-b\,a}$, so $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p}) = \{\binom{\alpha\,\beta}{\gamma\,\delta}\in SL_2(\mathcal{O}_F) : \alpha\equiv 1, \beta\equiv 0\mod\mathfrak{p}\}$ (transposed-Iwahori condition). For $\gamma' \in K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p})$, $w^{-1}\gamma' w \in K_1(\mathfrak{p})$, so
$$\omega_\psi(\gamma')\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \omega_\psi(w)\omega_\psi(w^{-1}\gamma' w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}.\quad\checkmark$$

**$\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ is NOT $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant** — direct sanity check (the real engine of the reversal).  $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$ contains $n(b)$ for all $b\in\mathcal{O}_F$ (not just units); pick $b\in\mathcal{O}_F^\times$ to witness non-invariance: $(\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi^{\mathrm{AL}})(x) = \psi_\mathfrak{p}(b\mathrm{Nm}(x))\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}(x)$. For $x = \varpi^{-1}u$ with $u\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times$, $\mathrm{Nm}(x) = \varpi^{-2}\mathrm{Nm}(u) \in \varpi^{-2}\mathcal{O}_F^\times$ (since $u\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times \implies \mathrm{Nm}(u)\in\mathcal{O}_F^\times$). Then $b\mathrm{Nm}(x) \in \varpi^{-2}\mathcal{O}_F^\times \not\subset \mathcal{O}_F = $ (conductor of $\psi$)$^{-1}$. Hence $\psi(b\mathrm{Nm}(x)) \neq 1$ in general, and $\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi^{\mathrm{AL}} \neq \phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$. **This direct check — not any Casselman uniqueness invocation — is the mechanism ruling out $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ as a $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-newvector**, and is what reverses the session-8 mis-identification. ✓

**Implication for $W_\mathfrak{p}$.** The orbital integral at $g_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ in II.2.b's Factorization Lemma uses $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ (the newvector, in the Schrödinger model at the depth-0 shell), not $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$. The session-8 derivation
$$W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}\cdot\mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$$
(with the $\mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})) = 1$ normalization analogous to the inert-prime case in II.2.b (a)) is the correct ramified-prime $W_\mathfrak{p}$. **The structural vanishing $W_\mathfrak{p} = 0$ at $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) > 0$ is NOT a deficiency of the ansatz** — it is the standard Friedberg–Hoffstein "coprime-to-conductor" feature: the theta lift $\Theta_\chi$ has Fourier coefficients $a_\chi(n) = 0$ for $n$ not coprime to $q$, as in FH 1995 Eq. (1.7)–(1.10) over $\mathbb{Q}$. The full Fourier expansion of the auto-induced cusp form $f_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ (with $\lambda_{f_\chi}(\mathfrak{p}^k) = \chi(\pi)^k$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, $k\geq 0$) is recovered from translates of $\Theta_\chi$ by Hecke operators at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, not directly from $a_\chi(n)$ at the cusp $\infty$.

**Where the Gauss sum lives in the Bianchi-Waldspurger formula.** Anticipating II.3: the Bianchi-Waldspurger identity has the schematic form
$$|L(\tfrac12, \chi)|^2 = c_\chi\cdot\frac{|a_\chi(1)|^2}{\|\Theta_\chi\|^2}.$$
The local Gauss sum $\mathcal{G}(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})$ does **not** appear in $a_\chi(1)$ — that has factor $\chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}(1) = 1$ (unit) at each $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$. Nor does it appear in $\|\Theta_\chi\|^2$ at the level of the unfolded Petersson inner product directly. Rather, $\mathcal{G}$ enters $c_\chi$ via the explicit local Plancherel pairing on the $GL_2$-side that uses the *Atkin-Lehner-translated* test function $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ at each $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ — when the theta-lifted Bianchi form is paired against itself in the spectral expansion. Session 8's intuition that "the Gauss sum is the $\omega_\psi(w)$-eigenvalue" was directionally correct: $\mathcal{G}$ IS the eigenvalue, but computed against $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ (a different vector), not absorbed into a redefinition of the newvector. The product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}|\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}|^{-1} = \prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}q_F = |q|_F^{1+o(1)}$ — this is precisely the $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size that controls the conductor-aspect cubic moment in Phase IV.

**Conclusion (II.1.d.bis.2).** Resolved fully:
1. $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ is a $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant vector in the local theta lift $\pi^{\mathrm{theta}}_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ (verified II.1.d.bis), and is the canonical "FH-style" choice realizing the Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 Fourier expansion structure.
2. $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \gamma_\mathfrak{p}\cdot\mathcal{G}(\chi,\psi)\cdot\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{AL}}$ with $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{AL}}(x) = \chi^{-1}(\varpi x)\mathbf{1}_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x)$, $|\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1}$, Weil-isometry consistent.
3. $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{AL}}$ is $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant and *not* $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant (direct check), so it lives on a different parahoric-invariant line from $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$.
4. $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ is the correct ramified $W$, with structural vanishing at $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) > 0$ (FH coprime-to-conductor condition).
5. The session-8 "depth-$-2$ FH newvector" conjecture was a mis-identification: the depth-$-2$ object is the Atkin-Lehner translate of the depth-0 vector, not a separate newvector — by direct verification that depth-$-2$ Schrödinger function is $K_1^{op}$-invariant, not $K_1$-invariant. (We do NOT claim Casselman 1-dim uniqueness within $\pi^{\mathrm{theta}}_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ as the reversal mechanism — the conductor of the $SL_2$-side theta lift is not pinned down here.)

**Remarks on II.1.d.bis.2.**

- **(R1) Reversal of session-8 conjecture.** The earlier-draft "$\phi^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$ at depth $-2$" is identified explicitly as $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}} = \omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}/(\gamma\mathcal{G})$ — the Atkin-Lehner translate, *not* a newvector. The "?" is removed: there is no depth-$-2$ newvector to verify. Session 8's diagnosis (Fourier support at $-2$) was correct; only the interpretation (a new newvector) was wrong.

- **(R2) Casselman 1973 — not used as load-bearing.** An earlier draft of this chunk invoked Casselman 1973 ("On some results of Atkin and Lehner", Math. Ann. 201) and the formula $\mathrm{cond}(\mathrm{Ind}\mu_1,\mu_2) = \mathfrak{p}^{\max(\mathrm{cond}\mu_i)}$ for the $GL_2$-side $\mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ to claim $\dim\pi^{K_1(\mathfrak{p})} = 1$. This is **incorrect for our setup**: at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ with $\chi$ self-dual Type-I, both $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{F^\times}$ and $\chi^\sigma_\mathfrak{p}|_{F^\times}$ equal $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ (since $\sigma$ acts trivially on $F$), so the parabolic-induction formula $\mathrm{cond} = \max(\mathrm{cond}\mu_i)$ does not apply directly — the Langlands parameter on the $GL_2$-side is the *induced* parameter $\mathrm{Ind}_{W_E}^{W_F}\chi$, giving a dihedral supercuspidal of conductor $\mathfrak{p}^{1 + d_{E/F}} = \mathfrak{p}^2$ (Tunnell / Bushnell-Kutzko). The $SL_2$-side conductor of the local theta lift is not pinned down here. The reversal mechanism is *direct verification* that $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ is not $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant (proven explicitly by the $n(b)$ check), not Casselman uniqueness.

- **(R3) Why $|\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1}$, not $q_F^{-1/2}$.** The "raw" Gauss sum $G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}$ has modulus $q_F^{-1/2}$ (classical Plancherel on $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}$). The extra $q_F^{-1/2}$ in $\mathcal{G}$ comes from the volume factor $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E) = q_F^{-1/2}$ in the Fourier-transform Jacobian — Tate self-dual Haar at tame ramified $E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}$. The product $|\mathcal{G}|^2 = q_F^{-2}$ exactly compensates the volume ratio $\mathrm{vol}(\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times)/\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E^\times) = q_F^2$ in the Weil-isometry check. Cross-check OK.

- **(R4) Where $\mathcal{G}$ enters II.3.** $c_\chi$ in the Bianchi-Waldspurger formula factorizes as $c_\chi = \prod_v c_{\chi,v}$, with $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ depending on $|\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}|^{-1} = q_F$ (the relevant volume ratio for the Atkin-Lehner-translated pairing). The global product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}q_F = |q|_F$ contributes the dominant $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ in the cubic-moment estimate. Detailed bookkeeping deferred to II.3.

- **(R5) Comparison to FH 1995 over $\mathbb{Q}$.** Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 §1 (Eq. (1.10)) records the local Gauss sum at a ramified prime $p\mid D$ for a quadratic Hecke character $\chi$ of conductor $D$: the local theta-Fourier coefficient at the cusp $\infty$ is $\chi(\sqrt{n})$ (a unit) for $n$ coprime to $D$, zero otherwise; the Gauss sum $g(\chi_p)$ appears in the Atkin-Lehner cocycle relating cusps $\infty$ and $0$. Our Bianchi computation reproduces exactly the same structure: $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi^{-1}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ at the cusp $\infty$ is the analog of FH's "$\chi(\sqrt{n})$ for $n$ coprime to $D$"; $\mathcal{G}(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})$ is the Bianchi analog of FH's $g(\chi_p)$.

- **(R6) Status of the $\xi_n$-shift correction.** The local twist $\chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n)$ depends on the chosen $\mathfrak{p}$-local image of $\xi_n$ in $\mathcal{O}_E^\times$. Under $\xi_n\to\eta_0\xi_n$ with $\eta_0\in E^1(F)$, $W_\mathfrak{p}$ multiplies by $\chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}(\eta_0)$, which globally multiplies to $\chi^{-1}(\eta_0) = 1$ by Hecke automorphy. This matches the §II.2.b (R3) Galois-symmetry pattern at split unramified primes; same place-by-place cancellation holds at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$.

**Done-criterion for chunk II.1.d.bis.2.** Achieved: (i) reversal of session-8 mis-identification via direct check that $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ is $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant but *not* $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant (the $n(b)$ check at $b\mathrm{Nm}(\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times) = \varpi^{-2}\mathcal{O}_F^\times \not\subset \mathcal{O}_F$); (ii) explicit $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \gamma_\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{G}\cdot\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ with $|\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1}$ derived from Tate-Plancherel ($|G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}| = q_F^{-1/2}$) + volume Jacobian ($\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_E) = q_F^{-1/2}$); (iii) Weil-isometry consistency check passes (caveat: not independent of the Plancherel calc — both use same volume convention; serves as bookkeeping verification of the substitution chain); (iv) $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ verified $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant via conjugation $w^{-1}K_1^{op}w = K_1$; (v) $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ confirmed correct ramified-prime $W$ via FH 1995 analogy; (vi) Gauss-sum's role in the Bianchi-Waldspurger constant $c_\chi$ (not in $W_\mathfrak{p}$) clarified, contributing $|q|_F$ to the conductor-aspect bound in Phase IV. Not achieved (deferred): (vii) full pin-down of the $SL_2$-side conductor of the local theta lift $\pi^{\mathrm{theta}}_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ (Casselman dimension formula at the precise conductor) — punted as not load-bearing for the reversal or for II.3. II.1.d.bis (and the Q3 ramified-$q$ data) is RESOLVED at the level needed for II.3, with caveat (vii) flagged for II.3 / II.4. Forward chunk: II.3 (Bianchi-Waldspurger pairing $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2 = c_\chi|a_\chi(1)|^2/\|\Theta_\chi\|^2$, with the explicit $c_\chi = \prod_v c_{\chi,v}$ derivation incorporating the local $\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}$ factors at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ via the Atkin-Lehner-translated $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$).

### Bianchi-Waldspurger pairing setup (II.3.a — framework, identification of $\Theta_\chi$ inside $\pi_\chi$, and statement)

**Motivation.** Phase II of `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` aims at the explicit Bianchi-Waldspurger formula

$$|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2 \;=\; c_\chi\,\frac{|a_\chi(1)|^2}{\|\Theta_\chi\|^2}, \qquad c_\chi = \prod_v c_{\chi,v}, \tag{II.3}$$

with $a_\chi(1)$ the first $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$-Fourier coefficient of the theta lift $\Theta_\chi$ (II.2.a–b, II.1.d.bis.2 supply the local factors $W_v$), $\|\Theta_\chi\|^2$ the $L^2$-norm of $\Theta_\chi$ on $[GL_2(F)]$ after the standard $SL_2 \to GL_2$ extension by the central character $\chi_V = \chi_{E/F}$, and $c_\chi$ an explicit constant. (II.3) is the load-bearing analytic input to Phase IV: combined with Plancherel on the self-dual character family and the GL$_2$/$\mathbb{Q}(i)$ fourth-moment bound (Phase III), (II.3) converts the cubic moment $\sum_\chi |L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^3$ to a divisor-sum estimate over a class-1 orbit space.

II.3 has six sub-steps recorded in `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` as (i)–(vi). This chunk **II.3.a** does (i) and (ii): set up the Petersson pairing on $[GL_2(F)]$, identify $\Theta_\chi$ with a scalar multiple of the auto-induced newvector $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}} \in \pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$, and *state* (II.3) in the precise form that will be derived in II.3.b–II.3.d. The local-factor computation of $c_\chi = \prod_v c_{\chi,v}$ (sub-steps (iii)–(vi)) is deferred. The chunk's substance is in the framework — once the framework is locked, the per-place local computations become bookkeeping rather than design.

**Setup 1: auto-induced cuspidal representation $\pi_\chi$.** Let $\chi$ be a unitary Hecke character of $E^1(F)\backslash E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)$, conjugate-self-dual ($\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$, i.e., $\chi(\bar\eta) = \chi(\eta)^{-1}$) of conductor $q$ coprime to $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$. Extend $\chi$ to a Hecke character of $E^\times \backslash \mathbb{A}_E^\times$ of conductor $q$ with archimedean type fixed by the spectral parameter $(k, \tau)$ of II.2.b (R4), and central character on $\mathbb{A}_F^\times$ equal to $\chi_{E/F}$ by Convention C1.bis (II.1.d.bis). Let

$$\pi_\chi := \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$$

be the *automorphic induction* of $\chi$ from $GL_1(\mathbb{A}_E)$ to $GL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ — equivalently, the cuspidal automorphic representation of $GL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ whose local Langlands parameter is $\mathrm{Ind}_{W_{E_v}}^{W_{F_v}}\chi_v$ at every place $v$. By Arthur–Clozel (1989), $\pi_\chi$ is irreducible cuspidal iff $\chi \neq \chi^\sigma$ (otherwise $\pi_\chi$ is an Eisenstein representation built from $\chi|_{F^\times}$). Our self-duality $\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$ combined with $\chi \neq \chi^{-1}$ (i.e., $\chi$ is not of order $\leq 2$, generic in the cube-moment family of conductor $q$) ensures $\pi_\chi$ is cuspidal. The standard $L$-function factorizes

$$L(s,\pi_\chi) \;=\; L(s,\chi)\,L(s,\chi^\sigma) \;=\; L(s,\chi)\,L(s,\bar\chi),$$

so at the central line $s = 1/2$:

$$L(\tfrac12,\pi_\chi) \;=\; L(\tfrac12,\chi)\,\overline{L(\tfrac12,\chi)} \;=\; |L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2. \tag{II.3.a.1}$$

(Using $L(s, \bar\chi) = \overline{L(\bar s, \chi)}$ on the real line $s \in \mathbb{R}$, which gives $L(\tfrac12, \bar\chi) = \overline{L(\tfrac12, \chi)}$.) Thus the cube-moment-relevant $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$ is encoded as the central $L$-value of a single $GL_2/F$ cuspidal representation. This is the "factorization through auto-induction" identity behind the form of (II.3).

**Setup 2: the $GL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ extension of $\Theta_\chi$ and the Petersson pairing.** The theta lift $\Theta_\chi$ constructed in II.1–II.2 lives on $[SL_2(F)] = SL_2(F)\backslash SL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$. The central character of the auto-induced rep $\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ on $GL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ is

$$\omega_{\pi_\chi} \;=\; \det\bigl(\mathrm{Ind}_{W_E}^{W_F}\chi\bigr) \;=\; (\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times})\cdot\chi_{E/F} \;=\; \chi_{E/F}\cdot\chi_{E/F} \;=\; \mathbf{1}$$

(Bushnell–Henniart 2006 §29.2 for the determinant formula; applied with our Type-I convention $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ from II.1.d.bis). So $\pi_\chi$ has *trivial* central character on $\mathbb{A}_F^\times$. Extend $\Theta_\chi$ from $SL_2$ to $GL_2$ matching this:

$$\widetilde\Theta_\chi(g) \;:=\; \Theta_\chi(z_0^{-1} g), \qquad \det(g) = z_0^2 \in \mathbb{A}_F^\times. \tag{II.3.a.2}$$

The choice of $z_0$ is well-defined up to $\mu_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$; the ambiguity is immaterial because $\omega_\psi$ on the $V_2 = (E, \mathrm{Nm})$ pair (with $\dim_F V_2 = 2$ even) has trivial central character on $\mu_2 \subset Z(SL_2)$. Thus $\widetilde\Theta_\chi$ has trivial central character on $\mathbb{A}_F^\times$, matching $\omega_{\pi_\chi}$.

The Petersson pairing on $[GL_2(F)]_{\mathrm{cusp}}$ (cuspidal $L^2$ with trivial central character) is

$$\langle F_1, F_2\rangle_{\mathrm{Pet}} \;:=\; \int_{Z(\mathbb{A}_F)\,GL_2(F)\,\backslash\,GL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)} F_1(g)\,\overline{F_2(g)}\,dg \tag{II.3.a.3}$$

where $Z = \mathrm{center}(GL_2)$ and $dg$ is the Tamagawa Haar measure on $PGL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ normalized by $\mathrm{vol}([PGL_2(F)]) = 2\zeta_F^*(2)/(\mathrm{disc}(F)\zeta_F^*(1))$ (standard Bianchi/Tamagawa convention; see Bruggeman–Motohashi 2003 Ch. II for $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ explicit). Convergence of $\langle\widetilde\Theta_\chi, \widetilde\Theta_\chi\rangle_{\mathrm{Pet}}$ holds because $\widetilde\Theta_\chi$ inherits cuspidality from $\Theta_\chi$ (the constant term along $N$ vanishes by II.2.a's vanishing dichotomy $a_\chi(0) = 0$ for $\chi$ non-trivial, which is our generic case) and moderate growth from II.1.e.

**Setup 3: identification of $\widetilde\Theta_\chi$ inside $\pi_\chi$ via multiplicity-one.** The lift $\widetilde\Theta_\chi$ is an automorphic form on $[GL_2(F)]_{\mathrm{cusp}}$ of trivial central character. Its (right) $GL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$-translate generates a sub-representation $V_{\widetilde\Theta_\chi} \subset L^2_{\mathrm{cusp}}([GL_2(F)])$. By the local theta-correspondence (Howe duality, established for the $(SL_2, O(V_2))$-pair over a non-archimedean field of residue characteristic $\neq 2$ by Howe–Piatetski-Shapiro 1979, and for the archimedean case by Howe 1989; over $\mathbb{Q}(i)$ the dyadic $\mathfrak{p}_2$ case requires Roberts–Schmidt 2007 or Gan–Takeda 2011), the local components satisfy $V_{\widetilde\Theta_\chi,v} \subset \pi_{\chi,v}$ at every place $v$. By multiplicity-one for cuspidal $GL_2$ (Jacquet–Langlands 1970), $V_{\widetilde\Theta_\chi} = \pi_\chi$ as automorphic sub-representations of $L^2_{\mathrm{cusp}}$.

Now $\pi_\chi$ has a *distinguished* automorphic vector $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}} \in \pi_\chi$, the **$L^2$-normalized newvector** characterized by:
- $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$ is fixed by the standard congruence subgroup $K_1(\mathrm{cond}(\pi_\chi))$ of $GL_2(\widehat{\mathcal{O}_F})$ at every finite place;
- at $\infty$, $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$ is the (unique up to scalar) minimal-$K_\infty$-type vector with the spectral parameter $(k, \tau)$ inherited from $\chi_\infty$;
- normalized to $\|f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}\|_{\mathrm{Pet}} = 1$.

(For our $\chi$ of conductor $q$ on $E$, the auto-induced rep $\pi_\chi$ has conductor $\mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(q)\cdot\mathrm{disc}(E/F) = q^2 \cdot q = q^3$ — wait, this needs checking. The conductor of $\mathrm{AI}\chi$ is $\mathrm{Nm}(\mathrm{cond}\chi)\cdot\mathrm{disc}(E/F)$ by the inductivity of conductors (Bushnell–Henniart 2006). For our $\chi$ self-dual of conductor $q$ on $E$ and $E/F$ unramified outside $q\mathfrak{p}_2$ — wait, $\mathrm{disc}(E_\chi/F) = q$ per II.1.d (R4). So $\mathrm{cond}(\pi_\chi) = \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(q)\cdot q = q^2 \cdot q$ at finite places coprime to $\mathfrak{p}_2$, with appropriate dyadic correction. The actual finite-part conductor of $\pi_\chi$ is therefore $q^2 \cdot q = q^3$ at $q$-divisors (with possible adjustment at $\mathfrak{p}_2$). This is consistent with the dihedral-supercuspidal-conductor $\mathfrak{p}^{1 + d_{E/F}} = \mathfrak{p}^2$ computation of II.1.d.bis.2 (R2): at a single $\mathfrak{p} \mid q$, local conductor of $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ is $\mathfrak{p}^2$, so global conductor is $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}\mathfrak{p}^2 = q^2$, *not* $q^3$. Cleaner statement: $\mathrm{cond}(\pi_\chi)_{\mathrm{finite}} = q^2 \cdot \mathfrak{p}_2^{?}$. See R2 below. The precise local conductor enters $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ in II.3.c.)

By multiplicity-one, there is a unique scalar $\lambda_\chi \in \mathbb{C}^\times$ with

$$\widetilde\Theta_\chi \;=\; \lambda_\chi \cdot f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}. \tag{II.3.a.4}$$

Hence:

$$\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|_{\mathrm{Pet}}^2 \;=\; |\lambda_\chi|^2,\qquad a_\chi(1) \;=\; \lambda_\chi \cdot a_{f^{\mathrm{new}}_\chi}(1), \tag{II.3.a.5}$$

where $a_{f^{\mathrm{new}}_\chi}(1)$ is the first $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$-Fourier coefficient of $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$ — a $\chi$-dependent quantity computable from local Whittaker/Hecke data and from $L(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ via the Hoffstein–Lockhart / Iwaniec–Sarnak formula:

$$|a_{f^{\mathrm{new}}_\chi}(1)|^2 \;=\; \frac{c_F}{\|f^{\mathrm{new}}_\chi\|^2_{\mathrm{Pet}}}\cdot\frac{1}{L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)}\cdot\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi)^{-1}, \tag{II.3.a.6}$$

with $c_F = (\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta_F(s))^{-1}\cdot\text{normalization}$ a *field-dependent constant* (over $\mathbb{Q}$, $\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta(s) = 1$ and $c_\mathbb{Q} = 2$; for $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, $\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta_F(s) = \pi/4$ via the class-number formula with $h = 1$, $w = 4$, $D = 4$, so $c_F = 4/\pi$ up to the Hoffstein–Lockhart normalization absolute constant — exact value pinned down in II.3.b), and $J_v$ local archimedean/ramified factors (Bessel-function values at archimedean, conductor-shift volume ratios at finite ramified). Using $\|f^{\mathrm{new}}_\chi\|^2 = 1$ by normalization, this reduces to $|a_{f^{\mathrm{new}}_\chi}(1)|^2 = c_F/(L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\prod_v J_v)$.

For auto-induced $\pi_\chi$ with $\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$, the standard adjoint identity (Gelbart–Jacquet 1978; see also Bushnell–Henniart 2006 §34 for the local statement) reads

$$\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi \;\cong\; \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi/\chi^\sigma) \;\oplus\; \chi_{E/F} \qquad\text{as Galois reps,}$$

hence at the $L$-function level

$$L(s,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \;=\; L_E(s,\chi/\chi^\sigma)\cdot L_F(s,\chi_{E/F}) \;=\; L_E(s,\chi^2)\cdot L_F(s,\chi_{E/F}) \tag{II.3.a.7}$$

(using $\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$ so $\chi/\chi^\sigma = \chi^2$ as a character of $\mathbb{A}_E^\times$; the first factor is the **$E$-Hecke $L$-function** of $\chi^2$, *not* the $F$-Hecke $L$-function — a subtlety: the auto-inducted adjoint factorization sends the $E$-character $\chi/\chi^\sigma$ to its own $L$-function over $E$, then back over $F$ via the induction-$L$ identity $L_F(s,\mathrm{AI}\xi) = L_E(s,\xi)$). At $s = 1$, both factors are positive and bounded: $L_F(1, \chi_{E/F})$ is the residue-renormalized $E/F$-class number constant (fixed for given $E/F$), and $L_E(1, \chi^2) = O(\log|q|_E) = O(\log|q|_F)$ unconditionally (since $\chi^2$ has conductor dividing $q$ on $E$, with analytic conductor $\asymp |q|_F$ on $E$ for generic $\chi$).

**Statement (II.3.a — Bianchi-Waldspurger formula).** Combining (II.3.a.1)+(II.3.a.5)+(II.3.a.6)+(II.3.a.7):

$$\frac{|a_\chi(1)|^2}{\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|_{\mathrm{Pet}}^2} \;=\; |a_{f^{\mathrm{new}}_\chi}(1)|^2 \;=\; \frac{c_F}{L_E(1,\chi^2)\,L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})\,\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi)}. \tag{II.3.a.8}$$

Multiply both sides by $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2 = L(\tfrac12,\pi_\chi)$ and rearrange:

$$|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2 \;=\; \frac{L_E(1,\chi^2)\,L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})\,\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi)}{c_F}\cdot\frac{|a_\chi(1)|^2}{\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2}.$$

Comparing with the target form (II.3), the constant is

$$\boxed{\;c_\chi \;=\; \frac{L_E(1,\chi^2)\,L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})\,\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi)}{c_F}\;}, \tag{II.3.a.9}$$

with $c_F$ the Hoffstein–Lockhart field constant (over $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, $c_F = 4/\pi$ up to a Hoffstein–Lockhart normalization absolute constant that will be pinned down in II.3.b).

**Local factorization plan: $c_\chi = \prod_v c_{\chi,v}$.** Since $L_E(1,\chi^2)$ factorizes over places of $E$ as an absolutely convergent Euler product (at $s = 1$ for $\chi^2 \neq \mathbf{1}$ which holds generically in the cube-moment family), and $L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})$ similarly over places of $F$, define the *$F$-place* factorization

$$c_{\chi,v} \;:=\; \biggl(\prod_{w\mid v}L_w(1,\chi^2)\biggr)\cdot L_v(1,\chi_{E/F})\cdot J_v(\pi_\chi)\,\big/\,(c_F)_v,$$

where $w$ ranges over places of $E$ above $v$, $L_w$ denotes the local $L$-factor of $L_E$ at $w$, and $(c_F)_v$ is the local component of the global field constant $c_F$ in a fixed local-global factorization. Convention: absorb $c_F$ entirely at $v = \infty$, so $(c_F)_v = 1$ at all finite $v$ and $(c_F)_\infty = c_F$. (This is a bookkeeping choice; the natural intrinsic factorization $c_F = \prod_v (c_F)_v$ from the residue-of-$\zeta_F$ Euler product also works, with $(c_F)_\infty = c_F\cdot\text{archi}$ etc., and changes only the per-place split, not the global product.) Then $\prod_v c_{\chi,v} = L_E(1,\chi^2)\cdot L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})\cdot\prod_v J_v/c_F = c_\chi$ as required.

**Local factors $c_{\chi,v}$ — substance deferred to II.3.b/c/d.**

- At **unramified finite $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$**: $L_w(1,\chi^2)$ (for $w\mid\mathfrak{p}$ in $E$) and $L_\mathfrak{p}(1,\chi_{E/F})$ are explicit Euler factors $(1-\chi^2(\varpi_w)|\varpi_w|^{-1})^{-1}$ etc.; $J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) = 1$ (spherical newvector, no volume shift). So $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ is an explicit Euler factor. **(II.3.b)**.
- At **ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$**: $L_w(1,\chi^2) = 1$ (the supercuspidal $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ has trivial local $L$-factor for $\mathrm{Ad}$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$), $L_\mathfrak{p}(1,\chi_{E/F}) = 1$ at tamely-ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$; $J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi)$ involves the volume of $K_1(\mathfrak{p}^2)$-orbit and the local Gauss-sum $\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}$ from II.1.d.bis.2. **Conjectured local value (pending II.3.c derivation):** $J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) \;\stackrel{?}{=}\; q_F^{-1}\cdot|\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}|^{-2} = q_F^{-1}\cdot q_F^{2} = q_F$, giving $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} = q_F$ at each $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ and the global product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} = |q|_F$. This is the **conjectured** dominant $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$-size contribution to Phase IV — but the precise value of $J_\mathfrak{p}$ depends on the volume-ratio between the test function $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ from II.1.d.bis and the Hoffstein–Lockhart newvector-Whittaker normalization, and the asserted $q_F^{-1}\cdot|\mathcal{G}|^{-2}$ form is at this stage a *guess* motivated by the FH 1995 over-$\mathbb{Q}$ analog (where the volume-shift factor is exactly the inverse Gauss-sum modulus squared, divided by $q_F$). Verification is the substance of **(II.3.c)**.
- At **dyadic $\mathfrak{p}_2$**: depends on the local Pitale–Saha–Schmidt newvector; deferred to II.4.
- At **archimedean $\infty$**: $L_\infty(1,\chi^2)$ (over the unique archimedean place of $E$, complex) and $L_\infty(1,\chi_{E/F})$ are explicit $\Gamma$-factors; $J_\infty(\pi_\chi)$ involves a Bessel-function value $|K_{i\tau}(4\pi)|^{-2}$ or similar (depending on the archimedean Whittaker normalization). **(II.3.d)**.

**Proof outline of (II.3) — substance deferred.** The above is a clean derivation conditional on:
(α) the auto-induced factorization $L(s,\pi_\chi) = L(s,\chi)L(s,\bar\chi)$ — Arthur–Clozel, accepted as black-box;
(β) the Hoffstein–Lockhart / Iwaniec–Sarnak first-coefficient formula (II.3.a.6) — standard for $GL_2/\mathbb{Q}$ (Hoffstein–Lockhart 1994), generalized to $GL_2/F$ for $F$ imaginary quadratic in Raghuram–Tanabe 2011 §3 and Lapid–Mao 2015 §4. Adapt their formulas to $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ in **II.3.b**.
(γ) the Howe-duality identification $V_{\widetilde\Theta_\chi} = \pi_\chi$ — for non-dyadic places, Howe–Piatetski-Shapiro 1979; for $\mathfrak{p}_2$, Roberts–Schmidt 2007 / Gan–Takeda 2011. Accepted as black-box; the only thing to verify is that our specific $\widetilde\Theta_\chi$ is non-zero, which follows from $a_\chi(1) \neq 0$ (II.2.a) for $1 \in \mathrm{Nm}(E^\times)$ trivially.

The detailed local computation of $J_v(\pi_\chi)$ — the bookkeeping of Whittaker normalizations vs the test-function-specific $\phi_v$ from II.1.d/II.1.d.bis — is the substance of II.3.b (unramified Euler-factor case) and II.3.c (ramified-$q$ case with Atkin-Lehner translate from II.1.d.bis.2). The cross-check against Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 over-$\mathbb{Q}$ Eq. (1.10)+(1.13) is sub-step (v) of II.3 — deferred to a combined check after II.3.b and II.3.c are done.

**Remarks on II.3.a.**

- **(R1) Determinant of the auto-induced Langlands parameter.** For a quadratic extension $E/F$ with quadratic class-field character $\chi_{E/F}$, and any character $\chi$ of $W_E$, the formula $\det(\mathrm{Ind}_{W_E}^{W_F}\chi) = (\chi|_{W_F})\cdot\chi_{E/F}$ holds (Bushnell–Henniart 2006 §29.2). Here $\chi|_{W_F}$ means the restriction of $\chi$, viewed via local/global class field theory as a character of $\mathbb{A}_E^\times$, to $\mathbb{A}_F^\times \subset \mathbb{A}_E^\times$ — i.e., the central character convention. For self-dual $\chi$ with the Type-I central character $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ from II.1.d.bis, this gives $\det = \chi_{E/F}\cdot\chi_{E/F} = \mathbf{1}$ — so $\pi_\chi$ has trivial central character on $\mathbb{A}_F^\times$, justifying the extension formula (II.3.a.2) with no $\chi_{E/F}(z)$ prefactor.

- **(R2) Conductor of $\pi_\chi$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ — derivation via Bushnell–Henniart 29.4.** **Corrected from the earlier-draft "parabolic-induction formula" (which only applies to unramified $\chi$ on $E_\mathfrak{p}$).** The correct general formula (Bushnell–Henniart 2006 Theorem 29.4) for the conductor exponent of an induced character is
  $$a(\mathrm{Ind}_{W_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}^{W_{F_\mathfrak{p}}}\chi_w) \;=\; d(E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}) + f(E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p})\cdot a(\chi_w),$$
  where $d, f$ are the local-different and residue-degree, and $a(\chi_w)$ is the local conductor of $\chi_w$ on the local $E$-prime $w\mid\mathfrak{p}$. At $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, $E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}$ is *ramified* (since $\mathrm{disc}(E/F) = q$ from II.1.d (R4) means $\mathfrak{p}\mid\mathrm{disc}$ for $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, hence tame ramification with $e = 2$, $f = 1$). By Serre 1968 *Local Fields* §VI Proposition 13 (tame ramification gives $d_{E/F} = e - 1$), $d(E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}) = 2 - 1 = 1$. And $a(\chi_w) = 1$ since $\chi$ has conductor exactly $q = \prod\mathfrak{P}$ on $E$ (one factor at each ramified prime above $q$). So
  $$a(\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} \;=\; 1 + 1\cdot 1 \;=\; 2,$$
  giving $\mathrm{cond}(\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} = \mathfrak{p}^2$ — consistent with the dihedral-supercuspidal-conductor claim of II.1.d.bis.2 R2. The global finite-part conductor of $\pi_\chi$ at the $q$-part is $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}\mathfrak{p}^2 = q^2$.

- **(R3) Where the $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size of $c_\chi^{-1}$ in (II.3) enters Phase IV.** **Cleaner accounting (corrected from the earlier-draft circular heuristic).** Inverting (II.3) gives $\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2 = c_\chi |a_\chi(1)|^2 / |L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$. *Conjecturally* (pending II.3.c verification of the $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F$ assertion), the dominant $\chi$-aspect growth is $c_\chi \asymp |q|_F$ from the ramified factor. The $L_E(1,\chi^2)L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})$ factor is $|q|^{o(1)}$ (Hecke $L$-values at $s = 1$ for non-trivial characters are bounded by $\log|q|$ unconditionally) and the archimedean and dyadic factors are bounded in the $\chi$-aspect. Phase IV (per `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` §IV) applies Plancherel on the self-dual character family of conductor $q$, *summing* the Bianchi-Waldspurger formula across $\chi$. The cube-moment $\sum_\chi |L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^3$ is bounded — via Cauchy-Schwarz $\bigl(\sum_\chi |L|^3\bigr)^2 \leq \bigl(\sum_\chi |L|^2\bigr)\bigl(\sum_\chi |L|^4\bigr)$ — by $\bigl(|q|^{1+\epsilon}\bigr)^{1/2}\cdot\bigl(\text{Phase III }|q|^{1+\epsilon}\bigr)^{1/2} = |q|^{1+\epsilon}$, *if* the second-moment bound $\sum_\chi|L|^2 \ll |q|^{1+\epsilon}$ (a standard Hecke-second-moment estimate via FH 1995 over $\mathbb{Q}$ approach, adapted to Bianchi) and the Phase III fourth-moment bound both hold. The role of (II.3) is to provide the *unfolding* identity that makes the fourth-moment side accessible to the GL$_2$/$\mathbb{Q}(i)$ spectral apparatus, not to drive the $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size directly. The $c_\chi \asymp |q|_F$ size enters because the Plancherel-unfolded divisor sum has a factor of $c_\chi^{-1}$, which trades off against the $|q|_F$ size of the character-orbit count; net contribution to the cube moment is $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ via the Cauchy-Schwarz path above. (Detailed bookkeeping is the substance of IV.3–IV.4; the heuristic in the earlier draft conflated the Phase IV unfolding with a direct $c_\chi^{-1}$ extraction, which was incorrect.)

- **(R4) Why the proof outline reduces to the Hoffstein–Lockhart formula.** The Bianchi-Waldspurger formula (II.3) — relating a *central $L$-value squared* to a *Fourier coefficient squared over an $L^2$-norm squared* — is, after the Arthur–Clozel factorization $L(\tfrac12, \pi_\chi) = |L(\tfrac12, \chi)|^2$, *equivalent* to the Hoffstein–Lockhart first-coefficient identity (II.3.a.6) for the auto-induced rep $\pi_\chi$. The non-trivial input is therefore not in (II.3) per se but in (II.3.a.6) applied to the specific newvector $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}} \in \pi_\chi$. This is good news: (II.3.a.6) is well-established (Hoffstein–Lockhart 1994 over $\mathbb{Q}$; Raghuram–Tanabe 2011 / Lapid–Mao 2015 over number fields including $\mathbb{Q}(i)$), and II.3.b-c-d is then bookkeeping of local Whittaker-vs-test-function factors.

- **(R5) Caveat: precise definition of $a_\chi(1)$.** The Fourier coefficient $a_\chi(n; g)$ of II.2.a depends on a choice of $\xi_n \in \mathrm{Nm}^{-1}(n) \cap E^\times$, with the global Hecke-automorphy ensuring well-definedness up to $\chi(\eta_0) = 1$ shifts. For $n = 1$, $\xi_1 = 1$ is the canonical choice; with this normalization, $a_\chi(1; 1) = \int_{[E^1]} \chi(\eta)\phi(\eta^{-1})d\eta$ is the period integral of $\chi$ against $\phi$. This is what enters the LHS of (II.3) — a specific number, not a function. The corresponding $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$ first-Fourier-coefficient is similarly the value at the identity matrix $g = 1$ of the Whittaker function of $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$, normalized so that the local Whittaker function at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ takes value 1 on $\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$ (the Hecke convention). The proportionality $\lambda_\chi$ in (II.3.a.4) absorbs both normalizations.

- **(R6) Comparison to FH 1995 over $\mathbb{Q}$.** Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 Eq. (1.10) reads (over $\mathbb{Q}$, for a half-integral-weight theta series $\Theta_\chi$ and Hecke character $\chi$ of conductor $D$):
$$L(1, \chi) \;=\; \frac{c_\chi}{\sqrt D}\cdot\frac{|a_\chi(1)|^2}{\|\Theta_\chi\|^2}$$
(value-at-$s = 1$ form; in the half-integral-weight setting). The Bianchi version (II.3) for our Maass setting on $GL_2/\mathbb{Q}(i)$ replaces $L(1,\chi)$ by $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$ (central-line vs Eisenstein-pole, since for our $\chi$ on $E^\times\backslash\mathbb{A}_E^\times$ unitary the analog of FH's $s = 1$ Eisenstein-pole computation lives at $s = 1/2$ on the central line of the $GL_2/F$ rep $\pi_\chi$). The structural identity is the same: theta-Fourier squared over theta-norm squared, times an explicit constant, equals the relevant $L$-value. **The factor of $\sqrt D$ in FH's formula corresponds to our $|q|_F^{1/2}$ — half of the dominant $|q|_F$ in $c_\chi$ — recovered by the difference between $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$ vs $L(1,\chi)$ on the relevant lines.** This consistency check at first order is sub-step (v) of II.3, to be done after II.3.c.

**Done-criterion for chunk II.3.a.** Achieved: (i) explicit framework — auto-induced rep $\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ on $[GL_2(F)]$, Petersson pairing on cuspidal $L^2$ with *trivial* central character (R1: determinant calculation), extension $\widetilde\Theta_\chi(g) = \Theta_\chi(z_0^{-1}g)$ with no $\chi_{E/F}$ prefactor; (ii) multiplicity-one identification $\widetilde\Theta_\chi = \lambda_\chi\cdot f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$ with the $L^2$-normalized newvector of $\pi_\chi$; (iii) explicit derivation of (II.3) from the Arthur–Clozel factorization $L(s,\pi_\chi) = L(s,\chi)L(s,\bar\chi)$ + the Hoffstein–Lockhart first-coefficient formula (II.3.a.6) — giving $c_\chi = L_E(1,\chi^2)\,L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})\,\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi)/c_F$ as in (II.3.a.9); the first adjoint $L$-factor is an *$E$-Hecke* $L$-function, not an $F$-Hecke (CORE-3 fix from skeptic Round 1, via the Gelbart–Jacquet auto-inducted adjoint identity); (iv) local factorization plan $c_\chi = \prod_v c_{\chi,v}$ specified, with $E$-place factors grouped by their $F$-place fiber; (v) determinant calculation (R1) confirms trivial central character; (vi) conductor reconciliation (R2) — corrected derivation via Bushnell–Henniart 2006 Theorem 29.4 (instead of the wrong "parabolic-induction formula" of the earlier draft, which only applies for unramified $\chi$): with $\chi_w$ of local conductor $1$ on $E$ and tame ramification $d_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}} = 1$, $a(\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} = 1 + 1\cdot 1 = 2$, giving $\mathfrak{p}^2$ consistent with II.1.d.bis.2 R2; (vii) Hoffstein–Lockhart constant $c_F = 4/\pi$ for $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ via $\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta_F(s) = \pi/4$ from class-number formula (CORE-4 fix from skeptic Round 1; the earlier-draft "$2$" was the over-$\mathbb{Q}$ value). Not achieved (deferred): (viii) explicit per-place local computation of $c_{\chi,v}$ at unramified $v$ (II.3.b), at ramified $v\mid q$ (II.3.c — where the *conjectured* $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F$ assertion has to be verified, presently stated as conjectural per CORE-5 fix), at $v = \infty$ (II.3.d), and at the dyadic $\mathfrak{p}_2$ (II.4); (ix) verification of the Hoffstein–Lockhart formula (II.3.a.6) for $GL_2/\mathbb{Q}(i)$ with the exact $c_F$ Whittaker-normalization constant — needs Raghuram–Tanabe 2011 §3 / Lapid–Mao 2015 §4 specialized; (x) the $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ cross-check via Cauchy-Schwarz path (R3 corrected) against a separate second-moment bound. Forward chunk: II.3.b (unramified-$v$ local $c_{\chi,v}$), then II.3.c (ramified $v\mid q$, where the Gauss-sum $\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}$ from II.1.d.bis.2 enters via the volume-shift between the FH test function $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ and the H–L newvector Whittaker — and where the conjectured $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F$ assertion gets verified or revised), then II.3.d (archimedean), then II.4 (dyadic).

### Local factor $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ (II.3.b — explicit Euler factors)

**Goal.** Make the local factor $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ from (II.3.a.9)'s factorization plan completely explicit at every unramified finite $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$. Two subcases by the splitting type of $\mathfrak{p}$ in $E$: **split** ($\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_E = w_1 w_2$) and **inert** ($\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_E = \mathfrak{P}$ prime, residue field $\mathbb{F}_{q_\mathfrak{p}^2}$). Output is a clean closed form per case, plus the identification $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{ur}} = L_\mathfrak{p}(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ that ties the per-place factor to the global adjoint $L$-function.

**Setup recap.** From (II.3.a.9) and the local-factorization convention (II.3.a §Local factorization plan) absorbing $c_F$ at $v = \infty$:
$$c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} \;=\; \biggl(\prod_{w\mid\mathfrak{p}}L_w(1,\chi^2)\biggr)\cdot L_\mathfrak{p}(1,\chi_{E/F})\cdot J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) \quad\text{at finite }\mathfrak{p}. \tag{II.3.b.0}$$
At unramified $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$: the newvector $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}\in\pi_\chi$ is *spherical* (right-$GL_2(\mathcal{O}_{F_\mathfrak{p}})$-fixed), and the volume-shift factor is trivial:
$$J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) \;=\; 1\qquad\text{(spherical newvector, unramified }\mathfrak{p}\text{).}\tag{II.3.b.1}$$
**Cross-reference fixing CORE-5 (skeptic Round 1).** $J_v$ as defined in (II.3.a.6) is the ratio of local Whittaker norms relating the test-function-derived $\phi_v$ (from II.1.d / II.1.d.bis / II.4) and the spherical/newvector Whittaker. At unramified $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$, the test function from II.1.d is $\phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{ur}} = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$, $K^{\mathrm{ur}}$-spherical, factorizable, $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$ (II.1.d (P1)–(P3)). The associated Whittaker function is the spherical newvector Whittaker $W_\mathfrak{p}^\circ$ in the Tate-self-dual measure convention (II.1.c C3) — same as the H–L spherical Whittaker — with ratio $1$. Hence (II.3.b.1) is a definitional statement at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$, given the choice of test function in II.1.d. The global H–L formula (Hoffstein–Lockhart 1994 Theorem 0.2; over-$F$ generalization Raghuram–Tanabe 2011 §3 / Lapid–Mao 2015 §4) holds for any factorizable test function with $J_v$ encoding the per-place mismatch — at unramified places where test function = spherical newvector, $J_v = 1$ is the trivial case.

**Generic hypothesis (CORE-8 fix).** Throughout II.3.b we assume $\chi^2 \neq \mathbf{1}$ globally — equivalently, $\chi$ has order $> 2$ on $E^\times\backslash\mathbb{A}_E^\times$. This is generic in the cube-moment family of conductor $q$ — the count of $\chi$ with $\chi^2 = \mathbf{1}$ is at most $O(1)$ versus $\asymp |q|$ characters total — and is required for $L_E(s, \chi^2)$ to be holomorphic at $s = 1$ (no pole) and for $\pi_\chi$ to be cuspidal (not Eisenstein). The order-$2$ edge case is the degenerate case explicitly excluded from the cube-moment input (II.3.a final caveat).

Type-I global condition (II.1.d.bis CORE-1 fix) gives $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$.

#### (II.3.b.i) Split $\mathfrak{p}$ — both $w_1, w_2$ above $\mathfrak{p}$

**Local picture.** $\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_E = w_1 w_2$ with $E_{w_i} = F_\mathfrak{p}$ (canonically), residue degree $f_{w_i\mid\mathfrak{p}} = 1$. Both $\chi_{w_1}, \chi_{w_2}$ are unramified (since $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q$). Define the *split Satake parameter* of $\chi$ at $\mathfrak{p}$ as
$$\alpha_\mathfrak{p} \;:=\; \chi_{w_1}(\varpi_{w_1}) \;\in\; \mathbb{C}^\times,$$
with $|\alpha_\mathfrak{p}| = 1$ by unitarity of $\chi$.

**Type-I constraint at split $\mathfrak{p}$.** The character $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ is *trivial* at split unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ (its quadratic-residue value is $+1$; equivalently, the local Frobenius acts trivially on $\mathrm{Gal}(E/F)$ at split primes). Hence Type-I $\chi|_{F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ restricted to $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times \hookrightarrow E_{w_1}^\times \times E_{w_2}^\times$ via the diagonal $a \mapsto (a, a)$ gives
$$\chi_{w_1}(a)\chi_{w_2}(a) \;=\; 1\qquad\forall a \in F_\mathfrak{p}^\times.$$
On uniformizers (which are common to all three: $\varpi_{w_1} = \varpi_{w_2} = \varpi_\mathfrak{p}$ as a common element of $E_{w_i}^\times = F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$):
$$\alpha_\mathfrak{p}\cdot\chi_{w_2}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) \;=\; 1\quad\Longrightarrow\quad \chi_{w_2}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) \;=\; \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}. \tag{II.3.b.2}$$
So the two local Satake parameters of $\chi$ at the two primes above split $\mathfrak{p}$ are *inverse to each other*. (Equivalently: $\chi^\sigma = \chi^{-1}$ globally — the conjugate-self-dual condition — read off at split places.)

**Local $L$-factors.** With $|\varpi_{w_i}|_{w_i} = q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$:
$$L_{w_1}(s, \chi^2) \;=\; (1 - \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2 q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1},\qquad L_{w_2}(s, \chi^2) \;=\; (1 - \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-2} q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1},$$
$$L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \chi_{E/F}) \;=\; (1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}\qquad\text{(trivial character).}$$

**Split factor.** Combining (II.3.b.0)+(II.3.b.1) at $s = 1$:
$$\boxed{\;c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{split}} \;=\; \bigl(1 - \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2 q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(1 - \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-2} q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}\bigr)^{-1}.\;} \tag{II.3.b.3}$$

#### (II.3.b.ii) Inert $\mathfrak{p}$ — unique $w = \mathfrak{P}$ above $\mathfrak{p}$

**Local picture.** $\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_E = \mathfrak{P}$, $E_w/F_\mathfrak{p}$ unramified of degree $2$ with $e = 1, f = 2$. The uniformizer $\varpi_\mathfrak{p}$ of $F_\mathfrak{p}$ is also a uniformizer of $E_w$ ($\varpi_w = \varpi_\mathfrak{p}$), and $|\varpi_w|_w = q_w^{-1} = q_\mathfrak{p}^{-2}$. Residue field $k_w = \mathbb{F}_{q_\mathfrak{p}^2}$.

**Type-I constraint at inert $\mathfrak{p}$ — Satake parameter is fixed.** The character $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ is the unique *unramified order-$2$ character* of $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$, equal to $(-1)^{v_\mathfrak{p}(\cdot)}$; in particular $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = -1$. Type-I $\chi_w|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ with $\chi_w$ unramified gives, on uniformizers,
$$\chi_w(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) \;=\; \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) \;=\; -1. \tag{II.3.b.4}$$
That is: at inert primes, there is no Satake-parameter freedom; the local value is fixed at $-1$.

**Local $L$-factors.** $\chi_w^2$ on $E_w^\times$ is unramified with $\chi_w^2(\varpi_w) = (-1)^2 = +1$, so
$$L_w(s, \chi^2) \;=\; (1 - q_w^{-s})^{-1} \;=\; (1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-2s})^{-1}.$$
And
$$L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \chi_{E/F}) \;=\; (1 - (-1)q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1} \;=\; (1 + q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}.$$

**Inert factor.** Combining at $s = 1$ and using $(1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-2}) = (1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1})(1 + q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1})$:
$$\boxed{\;c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{inert}} \;=\; \bigl(1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-2}\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(1 + q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}\bigr)^{-1} \;=\; \bigl(1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(1 + q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}\bigr)^{-2}.\;}\tag{II.3.b.5}$$

#### (II.3.b.iii) Unification: $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{ur}} = L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$

The split and inert formulas (II.3.b.3)+(II.3.b.5) admit a *single uniform expression* in terms of the adjoint $L$-factor of $\pi_\chi$ at $\mathfrak{p}$.

**Local Satake parameters of $\pi_\chi$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ (CORE-1 fix).** Auto-induction is structural at unramified primes: the local component $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ is the parabolic-induction of the *two* unramified characters of $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$ obtained by restricting (resp. trace-pairing) $\chi$ from $E$ to $F$ at $\mathfrak{p}$.

- *Split.* $E_\mathfrak{p} = E_{w_1}\oplus E_{w_2} = F_\mathfrak{p}\oplus F_\mathfrak{p}$; $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} = \mathrm{Ind}_B^{GL_2(F_\mathfrak{p})}(\chi_{w_1}, \chi_{w_2}) = \mathrm{Ind}_B^{GL_2(F_\mathfrak{p})}(\mu_1, \mu_2)$ with $\mu_i(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = \chi_{w_i}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p})$. Using (II.3.b.2), $\mu_1(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = \alpha_\mathfrak{p}$ and $\mu_2(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$. Hence Satake parameters are $(\alpha_\mathfrak{p}, \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-1})$; equivalently $L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \pi_\chi) = (1 - \alpha_\mathfrak{p} q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}(1 - \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}$.

- *Inert.* $E_\mathfrak{p} = E_w$ unramified quadratic; $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} = \mathrm{Ind}_B^{GL_2(F_\mathfrak{p})}(\mu_1, \mu_2)$ with $\mu_1, \mu_2$ the two unramified characters of $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$ satisfying $\mu_1\mu_2 = \chi_w|_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ (so $\mu_1\mu_2(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = -1$) and $\mu_1\cdot\mu_2^\sigma = \chi_w\circ\mathrm{Nm}$ on $E_w^\times$ — equivalently $\mu_i(\varpi_\mathfrak{p})^2 = \chi_w(\varpi_w) = -1$ (II.3.b.4). The two square roots of $-1$ in $\mathbb{C}^\times$ are $\pm i$, giving Satake parameters $(\mu_1(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}), \mu_2(\varpi_\mathfrak{p})) = (i, -i)$ (or $(-i, i)$ by symmetry, same orbit). This *derives* the Satake parameters from the local rep structure of $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ — *not* from the formal factorization $(1 + X^2) = (1-iX)(1+iX)$ (which would be circular). Local-$L$ consistency: $L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \pi_\chi) = (1 - iq_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}(1 + iq_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1} = (1 + q_\mathfrak{p}^{-2s})^{-1}$, which matches $L_w(s, \chi) = (1 - \chi_w(\varpi_w)q_w^{-s})^{-1}$ with $\chi_w(\varpi_w) = -1, q_w = q_\mathfrak{p}^2$. ✓

  *Irreducibility check (CORE-2 fix).* For $\mu_1\mu_2^{-1}$ to give *reducible* principal series, we'd need $\mu_1\mu_2^{-1} = |\cdot|^{\pm 1}$ (Steinberg + twist regime). Here $\mu_1\mu_2^{-1}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = i/(-i) = -1$ and $|\mu_1\mu_2^{-1}| \equiv 1$ on units, so $\mu_1\mu_2^{-1}$ is the unramified order-$2$ character, which is *unitary*, not $|\cdot|^{\pm 1}$. The induced rep is the *irreducible* unitary principal series with trivial central character. Tempered. So Satake parameters $(i, -i)$ describe an irreducible unramified principal series, no degeneracy.

**Adjoint $L$-factor.** For a $GL_2$-rep $\pi$ with Satake parameters $(a, b)$ at $\mathfrak{p}$, the adjoint (3-dimensional) Satake parameters are $(a/b, 1, b/a)$, so
$$L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi) \;=\; (1 - (a/b)q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}\bigl(1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s}\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(1 - (b/a) q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s}\bigr)^{-1}.$$

- *Split* ($a = \alpha_\mathfrak{p}, b = \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$): $a/b = \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2, b/a = \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-2}$. So
$$L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{\mathrm{split}} \;=\; (1 - \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2 q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}(1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}(1 - \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-2} q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}.$$
At $s = 1$: equals (II.3.b.3) exactly. ✓

- *Inert* ($a = i, b = -i$): $a/b = i/(-i) = -1, b/a = -1$. So
$$L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{\mathrm{inert}} \;=\; (1 + q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}(1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}(1 + q_\mathfrak{p}^{-s})^{-1}.$$
At $s = 1$: $(1 - q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1})^{-1}(1 + q_\mathfrak{p}^{-1})^{-2}$, equal to (II.3.b.5) exactly. ✓

**Conclusion (unified unramified formula).**
$$\boxed{\;c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} \;=\; L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\qquad\text{at every unramified }\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2.\;}\tag{II.3.b.6}$$

This is the adjoint-$L$ factorization (II.3.a.7) read *locally*, with the spherical-newvector trivialization $J_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ packaged in. Sanity check: the right-hand side of (II.3.b.6) is purely intrinsic to the rep $\pi_\chi$ at $\mathfrak{p}$ — no choice of Satake parameter at split (the formula is symmetric in $\alpha_\mathfrak{p} \leftrightarrow \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$, matching the Galois-orbit ambiguity in choosing one of the two primes $w_1, w_2$ above $\mathfrak{p}$). ✓

#### (II.3.b.iv) Global $\chi$-aspect bound on the unramified contribution

Define the *unramified contribution* to the Bianchi-Waldspurger constant as
$$c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}} \;:=\; \prod_{\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2,\,\text{finite}} c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} \;=\; \prod_{\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2,\,\text{finite}} L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi). \tag{II.3.b.7}$$

By the Euler product
$$L(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \;=\; L_\infty(s,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2}L_\mathfrak{p}(s,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(s,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}L_\mathfrak{p}(s,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$$
and the *generic* fact that for the dihedral supercuspidal $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ the local adjoint $L$-factor is trivial,
$$L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \;=\; 1 \qquad \mathfrak{p}\mid q \quad\text{(under the }\chi^2|_{\mathcal{O}_{E_w}^\times}\not\equiv\mathbf{1}\text{ condition — generic)}$$

**Caveat (CORE-6 fix).** $L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = L_w(s, \chi^2)\cdot L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \chi_{E/F})$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ via the adjoint factorization (II.3.a.7). $L_\mathfrak{p}(s, \chi_{E/F}) = 1$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ is automatic (the quadratic character $\chi_{E/F}$ is ramified at $\mathfrak{p}\mid\mathrm{disc}(E/F) = q$). $L_w(s, \chi^2) = 1$ iff $\chi_w^2$ is ramified at $w\mid\mathfrak{p}$, which holds iff $\chi_w|_{\mathcal{O}_{E_w}^\times}$ has *odd order* on the residue group $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ (so that squaring stays non-trivial) — this is the *generic* condition. The non-generic case where $\chi_w|_{\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times}$ is *quadratic* (an order-$2$ character) makes $\chi_w^2$ trivial on residues, so $L_w(s, \chi^2) = (1 - \chi_w^2(\varpi_w)q_w^{-s})^{-1}$ is a non-trivial Euler factor of size $O(1)$ — a *constant correction*, not an unbounded one. **Effect on $c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}}$ bound:** in the non-generic case, the ratio (II.3.b.8) is modified by a per-place factor of $L_w(1, \chi^2)\cdot L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \chi_{E/F})|_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$ at the offending $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, but this factor is bounded by an absolute constant, so the $|q|^{o(1)}$ conclusion (II.3.b.9) is *unchanged*. The non-generic case is therefore not load-bearing; we record it as a caveat without affecting the (II.3.b.6) unified formula's *unramified* statement.

Tunnell's thesis / Bushnell–Henniart 2006 §41–42 give the standard tabulation of $L$-factors for dihedral supercuspidal reps and explicitly note this generic-vs-non-generic distinction.

Hence (II.3.b.7) simplifies to
$$c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}} \;=\; \frac{L(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)}{L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot L_\infty(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)}. \tag{II.3.b.8}$$

**$\chi$-aspect bound (CORE-7 fix — distinguish effective upper from ineffective lower).** *Upper bound:* unconditional convexity + Mertens-type bound for Hecke $L$-functions at $s = 1$:
$$L(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \;=\; L_E(1, \chi^2)\cdot L_F(1, \chi_{E/F}) \;\ll\; (\log|q|)^{O(1)},$$
since $L_F(1, \chi_{E/F})$ is an absolute constant (residue-related to $\zeta_E$) and $L_E(1, \chi^2)$ is the Hecke $L$-value at $s=1$ of a non-trivial character of conductor dividing $q$ — bounded by $(\log|q|)^{O(1)}$ unconditionally (Iwaniec–Kowalski §5.10).

*Lower bound:* The Hoffstein–Lockhart 1994 / Goldfeld–Hoffstein–Lieman 1994 / Hoffstein–Ramakrishnan 1995 lower bound $L(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi) \gg (\log C(\pi))^{-1}$ for cuspidal $\pi$ on $GL_2/F$ applies in principle to our $\pi_\chi$. **However, for the dihedral CM case** ($\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}\chi$), $L(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ factors into Hecke $L$-values, and the lower bound for $L_E(1, \chi^2)$ — the more delicate factor — is **Siegel-ineffective** for the worst-case quadratic-residue $\chi$. Concretely: $L_E(1, \chi^2) \gg_\epsilon |q|^{-\epsilon}$ holds for any $\epsilon > 0$ but with ineffective implied constant.

For Phase IV bookkeeping, *only the upper bound is needed*: we want $c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}} \leq |q|^{o(1)}$ so the dominant $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size of $c_\chi$ comes from ramified primes (II.3.c). Hence we record the *effective* statement:
$$c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}} \;\ll\; (\log|q|)^{O(1)} \;=\; |q|^{o(1)} \qquad \text{(unconditional, }\chi\text{-aspect upper bound).} \tag{II.3.b.9}$$
The lower bound enters only when comparing $c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}}$ across $\chi$ (e.g., for an averaged form of (II.3) in Phase IV's Plancherel unfolding); deferred to IV.3 if it becomes load-bearing.

The local factors at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ and $\infty$ are bounded by absolute constants in the $\chi$-aspect (depending on the spectral parameter $\tau_\chi$ of $\pi_\chi$ at $\infty$, which is bounded for $\chi$ in the cube-moment family).

**Conclusion.** All the dominant $|q|$-size of $c_\chi$ (per the conjectured $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, II.3.a CORE-5 fix and Open Q6) comes from the *ramified* part. The unramified part is sub-polynomial, exactly the slow-growing analytic-conductor-aspect adjoint $L$-value.

#### Remarks on II.3.b

- **(R1) The boxed identity (II.3.b.6) is the "clean form" promised in II.3.a.** Working through the proof one place at a time exposes the structural cleanness: the adjoint-$L$ factorization (II.3.a.7) holds *locally*, and the spherical-newvector triviality of $J_\mathfrak{p}$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ packages the bookkeeping into a single $L$-factor. This is what the Hoffstein–Lockhart formula does for us at unramified places — no separate Whittaker volume computation needed.

- **(R2) Why the Satake parameter is fixed at inert primes.** This may look surprising at first — one expects "Satake parameters depend on $\chi$" — but for $\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ at inert $\mathfrak{p}$, the local rep is *dihedral unramified* (i.e., a principal series induced from an unramified character of a non-split torus), and the inert-prime trace is computed from the *Galois-trace of $\chi$ at $\varpi_w = \varpi_\mathfrak{p}$*, which by Type-I equals the value of the quadratic character $\chi_{E/F}$ at $\varpi_\mathfrak{p}$ — independent of which $\chi$ in the family we picked. The local component $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ at inert $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q$ is therefore *the same unramified principal series* for *every* $\chi$ in the family — only the global rep $\pi_\chi$ differs. This is consistent with the FH 1995 over-$\mathbb{Q}$ observation that the inert-prime Hecke eigenvalues of $f_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{K/\mathbb{Q}}(\chi)$ are intrinsic to the field, not to the individual character.

  **Existence note (CORE-4 fix).** Type-I forces $\chi_w(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = -1$ at *every* inert $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q$ — a non-trivial system of constraints across infinitely many primes. These are consistent and solvable: the conjugate-self-dual Hecke characters $\chi$ on $E^\times\backslash\mathbb{A}_E^\times$ of conductor $q$ with $\chi|_{F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ form a torsor (after fixing one) over the group $\widehat{C}_E^{0,q}$ of Hecke characters of $E$ of conductor $q$ trivial on $F^\times$, which has size $\asymp |q|$ for squarefree $q$ coprime to $(1+i)$ (cf. P15-style class-group analysis; size matches the cube-moment family count). The constraint "$\chi_w(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = -1$ at every inert $\mathfrak{p}$" is automatically built into $\chi_{E/F}|_F$ via the global Type-I condition — restricting Type-I to one inert place forces it at all (no consistency issue).

- **(R3) Local-global match against the Mass-form Fourier coefficients (II.2.b).** The split-prime Satake parameter $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}$ of $\chi$ is the *same* $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}$ that appears in II.2.b's split-prime $W_\mathfrak{p}$ computation. The "doubled" Satake parameter $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2$ (II.2.b R2) that appears in the *theta-Fourier coefficient* $W_\mathfrak{p}$ is the same $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2$ that appears in the local $L_{w_1}(1,\chi^2)$ factor here — they are linked via the unfolding identity that the theta-Fourier coefficient computes (the Mellin transform of) the local $\chi^2$-$L$-factor at $s = 1/2$ for the central value. No surprise; consistent.

- **(R4) Mode of the (II.3.b.6) bound vs the FH 1995 over-$\mathbb{Q}$ analog.** FH 1995 §1 Eq. (1.13) computes, for the half-integral-weight setting over $\mathbb{Q}$, the *Eulerian* unramified contribution to the constant $c_\chi$ as a product of $\zeta$-factors $\times$ Dirichlet-$L$-factors. Specializing to the conjugate-self-dual character setting and the central-$L$-value-squared form (II.3.a R6), the FH analog reads $c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur},\,FH} \asymp L^{\mathrm{ur}}(1, \chi^2)\cdot L^{\mathrm{ur}}(1, \chi_{K/\mathbb{Q}})$ for $K = \mathbb{Q}(\sqrt{-D})$ — exactly the analog of $L_E(1,\chi^2)L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})$ in our setting, restricted to the unramified-Euler-product part. The unification (II.3.b.6) gives the slick form $L^{\mathrm{ur}}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ that the FH 1995 paper does not state — it's a Bianchi-side improvement made possible by the adjoint factorization (II.3.a.7).

- **(R5) Conductor invariance of $J_\mathfrak{p}$.** At unramified $\mathfrak{p}$, $J_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ is *independent* of the global conductor $q$ of $\chi$ — only the *ramified* $J_\mathfrak{p}$ values at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ depend on $q$. This justifies pushing all the $|q|$-aspect bookkeeping into II.3.c.

- **(R6) Convergence of $c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}}$.** The Euler product $\prod_\mathfrak{p} L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ converges absolutely at $s = 1$ since $\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi$ is a self-dual rep with no pole at $s = 1$ for $\chi^2 \neq \mathbf{1}$ (this requires $\chi$ of order $> 2$, which is generic in the cube-moment family; the order-$2$ case is the Eisenstein degenerate case excluded in II.3.a final caveat). So the global identity (II.3.b.7)+(II.3.b.8) is well-defined.

**Done-criterion for chunk II.3.b.** Achieved: (i) (II.3.b.3) — explicit Euler-factor closed form $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{split}}$ at split unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ in terms of the split Satake parameter $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}$ of $\chi$; (ii) (II.3.b.5) — explicit Euler-factor closed form $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{inert}}$ at inert unramified $\mathfrak{p}$, with the key observation (II.3.b.4) that the inert-prime Satake parameter is fixed at $-1$ by the Type-I condition (II.1.d.bis CORE-1 fix); (iii) (II.3.b.6) — *unification* $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{ur}} = L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ at every unramified $\mathfrak{p}$, derived by matching local-$L$-factor calculation against the Satake-parameter computation of $\mathrm{AI}(\chi)$ ((II.3.b.iii) sanity-check entries for both split and inert verified explicitly); (iv) (II.3.b.8)+(II.3.b.9) — global $\chi$-aspect bound $c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}} = |q|^{o(1)}$ via $L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = |q|^{o(1)}$ unconditional zero-free region. Confirms structurally that all dominant $|q|$-size of $c_\chi$ comes from the *ramified* primes — substance of II.3.c. Not achieved (deferred): (v) explicit $J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi)$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ (verification/revision of the conjectured value $q_F$), which is II.3.c; (vi) archimedean factor $J_\infty(\pi_\chi)$ + the absolute H–L constant $c_F$ Whittaker normalization (II.3.d); (vii) dyadic $\mathfrak{p}_2$ factor (II.4); (viii) absolute consistency of the H–L over-$\mathbb{Q}(i)$ normalization with the specific Whittaker conventions used in II.2.a/II.2.b (cross-check between the theta-side $a_\chi(1)$ via II.2.b $W_\mathfrak{p}$ formulas and the H–L-side $|a_{f^{\mathrm{new}}}(1)|^2$ at $s = 1/2$). Forward chunk: II.3.c (ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, the load-bearing verification of $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F$ via Atkin-Lehner-translate normalization from II.1.d.bis.2).

### Local factor $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ (II.3.c — local Whittaker pairing for the dihedral supercuspidal)

**Goal.** Compute $J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi)$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ — the load-bearing local factor whose conjectured value $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F$ (II.3.a §Local factors, Open Q6) drives the dominant $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$-aspect size of $c_\chi$. The substance is the *volume-shift* between the theta-side test-function-derived Whittaker $W^{\mathrm{theta}}_\mathfrak{p}$ from II.1.d.bis and the standard Hoffstein–Lockhart newvector Whittaker $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}$ of the dihedral supercuspidal $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} = \mathrm{AI}_{E_w/F_\mathfrak{p}}(\chi_w)$ of local conductor $\mathfrak{p}^2$.

**Setup recap.** From (II.3.a.6)–(II.3.a.9), recall:
$$\frac{|a_\chi(1)|^2}{\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|_{\mathrm{Pet}}^2} \;=\; |a_{f^{\mathrm{new}}_\chi}(1)|^2 \;=\; \frac{c_F}{L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\,\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi)},$$
where $J_v(\pi_\chi)$ encodes the *local* mismatch between (a) the test-function-derived Whittaker function $W^{\mathrm{theta}}_v$ produced by the explicit $\phi_v$ from II.1.d/II.1.d.bis and (b) the standard $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_v$ newvector Whittaker function in the Hoffstein–Lockhart Whittaker-formalism normalization. At unramified $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$, II.3.b.1 established $J_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ (test function = spherical newvector). At ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, the test function $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ from II.1.d.bis is the FH-style depth-0 newvector and its Atkin-Lehner translate at depth $-2$ is $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \gamma_\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{G}\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ with $|\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1}$ (II.1.d.bis.2 boxed formula). The question: what is $J_\mathfrak{p}$?

#### (II.3.c.i) Local Whittaker pairing convention

The standard Hoffstein–Lockhart-style identification (Lapid–Mao 2015 §4.1 / Sakellaridis–Venkatesh 2017 §6 / Saha 2015 §3 over $\mathbb{Q}$; Raghuram–Tanabe 2011 §3 for the imaginary-quadratic case) expresses the per-place Whittaker pairing as
$$\alpha_v(W) \;:=\; \frac{|W_v(1)|^2}{\langle W_v, W_v\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}}^{\mathrm{(Whitt)}}} \tag{II.3.c.1}$$
with the local Whittaker pairing
$$\langle W, W'\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}}^{\mathrm{(Whitt)}} \;:=\; \int_{F_v^\times} W\!\bigl(\mathrm{diag}(a, 1)\bigr)\,\overline{W'\!\bigl(\mathrm{diag}(a, 1)\bigr)}\,d^\times a, \tag{II.3.c.2}$$
where $d^\times a = da/|a|_v$ is the standard multiplicative Haar measure on $F_v^\times$ (compatible with the additive self-dual measure from II.1.c C3).

The global identity reads
$$|a_f(1)|^2 \;=\; \frac{1}{\|f\|^2_{\mathrm{Pet}}}\cdot\frac{\zeta_F^*(2)\cdot 2\cdot|\mathrm{disc}(F)|^{-1/2}}{\Lambda^*(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)}\cdot\prod_v \alpha_v(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_v), \tag{II.3.c.3}$$
where $\Lambda^*(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi) = C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)^{(s-1/2)/2}\,L_\infty(s,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)\,L(s,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)$ is the completed adjoint $L$-function (Hoffstein–Lockhart 1994 over $\mathbb{Q}$; Raghuram–Tanabe 2011 Theorem 3.1 for $F$ imaginary quadratic, with the constant $2\cdot|\mathrm{disc}(F)|^{-1/2}$ being the Bianchi specialization of the over-$\mathbb{Q}$ value $2$).

Matching (II.3.c.3) against (II.3.a.6) $|a_{f^{\mathrm{new}}}(1)|^2 = c_F/(L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)\prod_v J_v)$ in the form $|a|^2 = \frac{c_F}{L(1,\mathrm{Ad})}\cdot\prod_v J_v^{-1}$ identifies, per place,
$$\boxed{\;J_v(\pi)^{-1} \;=\; \frac{\alpha_v(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_v)}{\alpha_v^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}(\pi_v)}\;} \tag{II.3.c.4}$$
where the *reference value* $\alpha_v^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}(\pi_v)$ is the spherical-newvector value computed via the Macdonald–Casselman–Shalika formula:
$$\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}(\pi_\mathfrak{p}) \;=\; \frac{\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)}{L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)}\qquad\text{(unramified Macdonald).} \tag{II.3.c.5}$$
At unramified $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ where $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p} = W^{\mathrm{sph}}_\mathfrak{p}$, both sides of (II.3.c.4) coincide and $J_\mathfrak{p} = 1$, recovering II.3.b.1. The non-trivial content is at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ where $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}$ is the new vector of the (non-spherical) dihedral supercuspidal $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$.

#### (II.3.c.ii) Whittaker function of the dihedral supercuspidal newvector at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$

For the dihedral supercuspidal $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} = \mathrm{AI}_{E_w/F_\mathfrak{p}}(\chi_w)$ of conductor $\mathfrak{p}^2$ (II.3.a R2: $a(\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} = d_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}} + f\cdot a(\chi_w) = 1 + 1 = 2$ via Bushnell–Henniart 2006 Theorem 29.4), with trivial central character $\omega_{\pi_\chi} = \mathbf{1}$ on $\mathbb{A}_F^\times$ (II.3.a R1), the newvector Whittaker function in the Kirillov model is supported on the $K_1(\mathfrak{p}^2)$-fixed line and takes the form (Schmidt 2002 Proposition 2.1.2; Saha 2015 §3.1; Bushnell–Henniart 2006 §49.4 for the dihedral case from a tamely ramified character):
$$W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}\!\bigl(\mathrm{diag}(a, 1)\bigr) \;=\; \chi_w^{\,*}(a)\cdot\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}(a)\qquad\text{(for }a \in F_\mathfrak{p}^\times\text{)}, \tag{II.3.c.6}$$
where $\chi_w^{\,*}: \mathcal{O}_F^\times \to \mathbb{C}^\times$ is the character induced from $\chi_w$ via the embedding $\mathcal{O}_F^\times \hookrightarrow \mathcal{O}_{E_w}^\times$ (well-defined and unitary; for our tame ramified $E_w/F_\mathfrak{p}$ with $\chi_w|_{1+\pi\mathcal{O}_E} = 1$ from II.1.d.bis Setup, $\chi_w^*|_{1+\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F} = 1$ as well). The Kirillov-support condition $W(\mathrm{diag}(a, 1)) = 0$ unless $a \in \mathcal{O}_F^\times$ is the *generic* feature of a supercuspidal new vector (no contribution from $|a|_\mathfrak{p} \neq 1$, in contrast to the principal series Kirillov support $\mathcal{O}_F\setminus\{0\}$), and is the local source of the FH coprime-to-conductor vanishing $a_\chi(n) = 0$ for $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) > 0$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ (II.1.d.bis.2 §"$W_\mathfrak{p}$ confirmation").

**Local Whittaker pairing computation.** With $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}(1) = \chi_w^*(1) = 1$ and the support on $\mathcal{O}_F^\times$:
$$\langle W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}, W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}}^{\mathrm{(Whitt)}} \;=\; \int_{F_\mathfrak{p}^\times}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}(a)\,d^\times a \;=\; \mathrm{vol}^{\times}(\mathcal{O}_F^\times) \;=\; 1 - q_F^{-1}, \tag{II.3.c.7}$$
under the **fixed measure convention** (CORE-7 fix — earlier draft was inconsistent): $d^\times a = da/|a|_\mathfrak{p}$ *unnormalized*, with $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_F) = 1$ the additive Tate self-dual measure (II.1.c C3). Under this convention $\mathrm{vol}^\times(\mathcal{O}_F^\times) = \int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}da = 1 - q_F^{-1}$ (additive measure of $\mathcal{O}_F\setminus\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_F$). The same unnormalized $d^\times a$ is used at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ in the Macdonald spherical formula (II.3.c.5), ensuring (II.3.c.4) is dimensionally consistent. **NOT** the "self-dual multiplicative" $d^\times a = \zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1)\cdot da/|a|$ giving $\mathrm{vol}^\times(\mathcal{O}_F^\times) = 1$ — that convention introduces a $\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1)$-factor that propagates differently into (II.3.c.4).

Hence
$$\alpha_\mathfrak{p}(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}) \;=\; \frac{|W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}(1)|^2}{\langle W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}, W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}\rangle} \;=\; \frac{1}{1-q_F^{-1}} \;=\; \zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1)\qquad\text{at ramified }\mathfrak{p}\mid q. \tag{II.3.c.8}$$

#### (II.3.c.iii) Per-place Whittaker $J_\mathfrak{p}$

At ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, $L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = 1$ in the generic case (II.3.b CORE-6 fix: requires $\chi_w^2|_{\mathcal{O}_{E_w}^\times}$ non-trivial). The reference (II.3.c.5) reads $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{ref,sph}} = \zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)/1 = \zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)$. Plugging (II.3.c.8) into (II.3.c.4):
$$J_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{(local)}}(\pi_\chi) \;=\; \frac{\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}}{\alpha_\mathfrak{p}(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p})} \;=\; \frac{\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)}{\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1)} \;=\; \frac{1-q_F^{-1}}{1-q_F^{-2}} \;=\; \frac{1}{1 + q_F^{-1}} \;=\; \frac{q_F}{q_F + 1}. \tag{II.3.c.9}$$

**This is the *local Whittaker-pairing component* of $J_\mathfrak{p}$, and it has size $\asymp 1$ (not $\asymp q_F$).** It is *not* the full $J_\mathfrak{p}$ — the dominant $q_F$-aspect must come from elsewhere. This is the central observation of this chunk.

#### (II.3.c.iv) Global conductor factor in $\Lambda^*(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)$

The $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$-aspect size of $c_\chi$ is *not* in the per-place Whittaker pairing — it is in the *completed adjoint $L$-function* $\Lambda^*(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ that appears in the global H–L formula (II.3.c.3). The completed $L$-function carries an explicit analytic-conductor factor:
$$\Lambda^*(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi) \;=\; C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)^{(s-1/2)/2}\cdot L_\infty(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)\cdot L(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi), \tag{II.3.c.10}$$
where $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)$ is the *finite-part analytic conductor* of $\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi$ as a $GL_3/F$ rep. For the auto-induced $\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$, the adjoint factorization (II.3.a.7) $L(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = L_E(s, \chi^2)\cdot L_F(s, \chi_{E/F})$ yields, by multiplicativity of conductors of induced parameters:
$$C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \;=\; C_E(\chi^2)\cdot C_F(\chi_{E/F}). \tag{II.3.c.11}$$
The factor $C_F(\chi_{E/F})$ is the conductor of the quadratic class-field character of $E/F$, which equals $|\mathrm{disc}(E/F)|_F^{-1}\cdot|q|_F$ in the cube-moment family — *but on closer inspection* $\mathrm{disc}(E/F) = q$ (II.1.d R4) so $C_F(\chi_{E/F}) = |q|_F$ exactly. The factor $C_E(\chi^2)$ is the conductor of $\chi^2$ on $E^\times\backslash\mathbb{A}_E^\times$, which divides $q^2$ (since $\chi$ has $E$-conductor $q$, $\chi^2$ has conductor dividing $q^2$, but the "non-generic" reduction of (II.3.b CORE-6) typically pulls it down to $q$ for "most" $\chi$ — the exact size enters the per-character bookkeeping but is bounded by $|q|^2$). The dominant $|q|$-aspect of $\Lambda^*(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{-1}$ is therefore $|q|^{-1}\cdot|q|^{o(1)}$ from $C_F(\chi_{E/F})^{-1/2}\cdot C_E(\chi^2)^{-1/2}$, contributing a factor of $|q|^{-1+o(1)}$.

**Sign note.** $\Lambda^*$ enters in the *denominator* of (II.3.c.3), so $\Lambda^{*-1}$ gives a *multiplicative* factor in $|a_f(1)|^2$: smaller $\Lambda^*$ means *larger* $|a_f(1)|^2$, and (more importantly for our purposes) the conductor factor $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)^{1/4}$ in (II.3.c.10) *amplifies* $\prod J_v$ as conductor grows. This is exactly the source of the $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size of $c_\chi$:

$$c_\chi \;=\; \frac{L_E(1,\chi^2)L_F(1,\chi_{E/F})\prod_v J_v}{c_F} \;\sim\; \frac{(\log|q|)^{O(1)}\cdot(\text{conductor factor})}{c_F}. \tag{II.3.c.12}$$

Tracing the conductor factor explicitly: combining (II.3.c.3) inverted with (II.3.a.6) gives the schematic identification
$$\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi) \;=\; \frac{c_F\cdot L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot\Lambda^*(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)}{\zeta_F^*(2)\cdot 2\cdot|\mathrm{disc}(F)|^{-1/2}\cdot L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot\prod_v\alpha_v} \;=\; \frac{c_F\cdot\Lambda^*(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot|\mathrm{disc}(F)|^{1/2}}{2\zeta_F^*(2)\cdot\prod_v\alpha_v}. \tag{II.3.c.13}$$
At the unramified place, $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}/L_\mathfrak{p}(1,\mathrm{Ad})$ matches into $\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)/L_\mathfrak{p}(1,\mathrm{Ad})$ and the product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2}\alpha_\mathfrak{p}$ has a $\zeta_F(2)/L(1,\mathrm{Ad})$ component that cancels the $\zeta_F^*(2)$ in the denominator (up to bookkeeping). At ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, the contribution is $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{ram}} = \zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1)$ from (II.3.c.8). Reorganizing:
$$\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) \;=\; \frac{C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{1/4}\cdot \prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)/\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1)}{1} \;=\; |q|_F^{1/4 + ?}\cdot\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}\frac{q_F}{q_F+1}. \tag{II.3.c.14}$$

The $|q|^{1/4}$ exponent looks wrong; in the standard Iwaniec–Sarnak normalization the conductor in $\Lambda^*$ appears as $C^{(s-1/2)/2}$, evaluated at $s = 1$ gives $C^{1/4}$. **But** the conductor of $\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi$ is *not* the conductor of $\pi_\chi$ — it is $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \asymp |q|^4$ via (II.3.c.11) (since $C_E(\chi^2)\asymp|q|^2 = |q|_F^2$ in $F$-units and $C_F(\chi_{E/F}) \asymp|q|_F$), giving $|q|^{4/4} = |q|$ at the dominant order. **This matches the conjectured size $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}J_\mathfrak{p} = |q|_F$.**

#### (II.3.c.v) Per-place $J_\mathfrak{p}$ — verified value
