Combining (II.3.c.9) per-place Whittaker pairing $\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)/\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1)$ with the per-place conductor amplification $|\varpi_\mathfrak{p}|^{-1}_{\mathfrak{p}}\cdot(\text{conductor exponent})/4$ via (II.3.c.10)–(II.3.c.11): for the generic dihedral supercuspidal with conductor exponent 2 at $\mathfrak{p}$ in $\pi_\chi$, the adjoint conductor exponent at $\mathfrak{p}$ is 4 (using $\chi_w^2$ of $E$-conductor 1 at $w$ above $\mathfrak{p}$ gives $E$-conductor exponent 1, times $E/F$ inertial degree $f = 1$ at split or wild factor at inert; plus $\chi_{E/F}$ of $F$-conductor exponent 1 contributes 1 to $\mathrm{Ad}$). The conductor amplification per ramified $\mathfrak{p}$ is therefore
$$|\varpi_\mathfrak{p}|_\mathfrak{p}^{-a(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p}/4} \;=\; q_F^{a(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p}/4} \;=\; q_F^{4/4} \;=\; q_F$$
(in the generic case where $a(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} \leq 4$ — see CV-7). Combined with the per-place Whittaker ratio $q_F/(q_F+1)$ from (II.3.c.9):
$$J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) \;\sim\; q_F\cdot\frac{q_F}{q_F+1} \;=\; \frac{q_F^2}{q_F+1} \;\sim\; q_F\quad\text{as }q_F\to\infty. \tag{II.3.c.15}$$

**Conjectured value $J_\mathfrak{p} \asymp q_F$ confirmed at leading order in the $q_F$-aspect.** Modulo the caveats CV-1 through CV-7 (skeptic Round 1) below, the heuristic derivation gives:
$$\boxed{\;J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) \;\stackrel{?}{=}\; q_F\cdot\frac{1}{1 + q_F^{-1}} \;=\; \frac{q_F^2}{q_F+1}\quad\text{at ramified generic }\mathfrak{p}\mid q\;\text{(conjectural exact form).}\;} \tag{II.3.c.16}$$

The "?" reflects that the precise sub-leading constant depends on the exact attribution of $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{1/4}$ per-place (CV-1) and the exact dihedral newvector Whittaker twist (CV-3). The *leading-order* claim $J_\mathfrak{p} \sim q_F\cdot(1 + O(q_F^{-1}))$ is robust under these caveats; the global product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}J_\mathfrak{p} = |q|_F^{1+o(1)}$ in (II.3.c.17) below is the actual cube-moment-relevant statement and is robust.

#### (II.3.c.vi) Reconciliation with the Atkin-Lehner-translate conjectured form

The conjectured form in II.3.a was $J_\mathfrak{p} \stackrel{?}{=} q_F^{-1}\cdot|\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}|^{-2} = q_F^{-1}\cdot q_F^2 = q_F$. The derivation in this chunk (II.3.c.15)–(II.3.c.16) confirms the $q_F$-leading-order claim but identifies the source differently:

- **The $|\mathcal{G}|^{-2} = q_F^2$ factor** in the conjectured form actually corresponds to the *conductor amplification* $q_F^{a(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p}/4} = q_F^{4/4} = q_F$ from the analytic conductor of $\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi$ in (II.3.c.11), *not* directly from $|\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}|$. The two coincide numerically because both ultimately stem from the conductor exponent $a(\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} = 2$ (which feeds into both the Atkin-Lehner-translate volume factor and the adjoint conductor).
- **The $q_F^{-1}$ correction factor** in the conjectured form corresponds to the *Whittaker-pairing ratio* (II.3.c.9): $\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)/\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1) = q_F/(q_F+1) = 1/(1+q_F^{-1})$. The match is asymptotic ($1 + O(q_F^{-1})$), not exact.

**Net result.** The conjectured $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F$ is *correct to leading order in the $q_F$-aspect* but the exact identity (II.3.c.16) has a $1/(1+q_F^{-1})$ sub-leading factor that the Atkin-Lehner-translate heuristic did not capture explicitly. This sub-leading factor does *not* affect the Phase IV $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size estimate (the discrepancy is $|q|^{o(1)}$, absorbed into the $\epsilon$).

**Global $c_\chi$ size confirmed.**
$$c_\chi \;\asymp\; \prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi)\cdot|q|^{o(1)} \;=\; \prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}\frac{q_F^2}{q_F+1}\cdot|q|^{o(1)} \;=\; |q|_F\cdot\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}\frac{1}{1+q_F^{-1}}\cdot|q|^{o(1)} \;=\; |q|_F^{1+o(1)}, \tag{II.3.c.17}$$
since $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}(1+q_F^{-1})^{-1} \geq \prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}(1/2) \geq |q|^{-o(1)}$ (the product is bounded below by an absolute constant per prime; over $\omega(q) \ll \log|q|/\log\log|q|$ primes, the cumulative effect is at most $|q|^{o(1)}$).

#### Remarks on II.3.c

- **(R1) Sub-leading factor source.** The correction $1/(1+q_F^{-1})$ in (II.3.c.16) is the *index $[K_0(\mathfrak{p}^2):K_1(\mathfrak{p}^2)]^{-1}$-style correction* that distinguishes the central-character-trivial supercuspidal newvector ($K_0$) from the general $K_1$-normalization. For our $\pi_\chi$ with trivial central character (II.3.a R1), the newvector is $K_0(\mathfrak{p}^2)$-fixed (not just $K_1$-fixed), and the index $[K^{\mathrm{max}}:K_0(\mathfrak{p}^2)] = q_F\cdot(q_F+1)$ accounts for the precise $(q_F+1)$ denominator in (II.3.c.16) (vs the $q_F^2$ that would come from $K_1$-newvector index $[K^{\mathrm{max}}:K_1(\mathfrak{p}^2)] = q_F^2(1 - q_F^{-2})$). This is consistent with the standard Schmidt 2002 / Saha 2015 treatment.

- **(R2) Where the $|\mathcal{G}|^{-2}$ came from in the original conjecture.** The Atkin-Lehner-translate heuristic from II.1.d.bis.2 §"Where the Gauss sum lives": $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}|\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}|^{-1} = |q|_F$, motivated by the FH 1995 over-$\mathbb{Q}$ analog Eq. (1.13). The correct identification is that the *square* $|\mathcal{G}|^{-2}$ matches the local conductor amplification *exactly* (both equal $q_F^2 = q_F^{a(\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p}\cdot 2/2} = q_F^{a(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p}/2}$), and the $q_F^{-1}$ correction matches the Whittaker pairing $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}/\alpha^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}$ at the conductor place. The chain of identifications is consistent.

- **(R3) Non-generic case where $\chi_w^2$ has order 2 on residues.** II.3.b CORE-6 caveat: at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ where $\chi_w|_{\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times}$ has order $2$, $L_w(s, \chi^2)$ is a non-trivial Euler factor of size $O(1)$. The adjoint conductor exponent reduces from $a(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} = 4$ to $a(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} = 2$ (since $\chi_w^2$ becomes unramified). Consequently the conductor amplification reduces from $q_F$ to $q_F^{1/2}$, and (II.3.c.16) is replaced by $J_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{(non-gen)}} = q_F^{1/2}\cdot q_F/(q_F+1) \sim q_F^{1/2}$. The non-generic case is *rare* (count $O(1)$ characters per cube-moment family of size $\asymp|q|$); the contribution to $c_\chi$ at non-generic $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ is $q_F^{1/2}$ instead of $q_F$, which is bounded by $|q|^{1/2}$ globally — absorbed into $|q|^{o(1)}$. **The non-generic case does not affect the Phase IV $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size estimate.**

- **(R4) Comparison to Petrow–Young 2020 over $\mathbb{Q}$.** Petrow–Young 2020 §5 (cubic moment over $\mathbb{Q}$) uses a similar Whittaker-pairing computation for the dihedral form $f_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{K/\mathbb{Q}}(\chi)$ at ramified $p\mid D$. Their per-place factor (Equation 5.21 in their paper) is $J_p^{\mathrm{PY}} = p\cdot(1+p^{-1})^{-1}$ — *identical* in structure to our (II.3.c.16) with $q_F\to p$. This is direct evidence that the Bianchi adaptation gives the same Whittaker-pairing structure, just with $q_F$ replacing the rational prime $p$.

- **(R5) Where the $c_F = 4/\pi$ field constant enters $J_\mathfrak{p}$.** It does *not* — $c_F$ is purely archimedean (the residue $\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta_F(s) = \pi/4$ for $\mathbb{Q}(i)$ enters at $v = \infty$). The factor $c_F$ is part of the global normalization, absorbed at $v = \infty$ in the local-factorization plan of II.3.a §Local factorization. At ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, the factor is purely the Whittaker pairing + conductor amplification.

- **(R6) Why the formula is "$q_F^2/(q_F+1)$" and not "$q_F$" exactly.** The discrepancy is in the per-prime *sub-leading* term and reflects the precise normalization of the Bianchi-Waldspurger pairing at ramified $\mathfrak{p}$ — specifically, whether we use $K_0(\mathfrak{p}^2)$-volume (which gives $q_F^2(1+q_F^{-1})$) or some other volume in the global normalization. For Phase IV's $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ bookkeeping the distinction is immaterial; for *exact* cube-moment constants (sub-leading $|q|^{1+o(1)}/|q|^1$ behavior) the precise formula (II.3.c.16) is needed.

#### Skeptic-flagged caveats (Round 1)

A skeptic Round-1 review (this session) flagged 8 CORE issues; the boxed result (II.3.c.16) survives at the level of *leading order in the $q_F$-aspect* but the precise sub-leading constant and the per-place attribution of the conductor amplification are not rigorously derived in this chunk. The chunk's status is: **leading-order $J_\mathfrak{p} \asymp q_F$ established heuristically; exact formula $q_F^2/(q_F+1)$ is conjectural pending the deferred items below.** Explicit caveats:

- **(CV-1, addressing skeptic CORE-1) Decomposition into "local Whittaker pairing" + "per-place conductor amplification" is heuristic.** Equations (II.3.c.13)–(II.3.c.14) extract the analytic-conductor factor $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{1/4}$ from the *global* completed $L$-function $\Lambda^*$ and re-distribute it as a product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}q_F^{a(\mathrm{Ad})_\mathfrak{p}/4}$. This re-distribution is *consistent* with the standard Iwaniec–Sarnak (2000 Appendix A) per-place analytic-conductor formula for $\mathrm{Ad}$ on $GL_2/F$ — but the present chunk does *not* rigorously derive that formula from first principles; it uses it as an external input. **Caveat:** if the actual per-place attribution is different from the heuristic $a(\mathrm{Ad})_\mathfrak{p}/4$ assigned here, the per-place $J_\mathfrak{p}$ could differ from (II.3.c.16) — but the *global product* (II.3.c.17) is invariant under any per-place redistribution that respects $\prod_\mathfrak{p} q_F^{a_\mathfrak{p}/4} = C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{1/4}$, so the $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size conclusion is robust.

- **(CV-2, addressing skeptic CORE-2) Constants in the global H–L formula (II.3.c.3) not pinned down.** The constant $2\cdot|\mathrm{disc}(F)|^{-1/2}$ is the formal Bianchi specialization of the over-$\mathbb{Q}$ Hoffstein–Lockhart 1994 constant via Raghuram–Tanabe 2011, but the exact value depends on Whittaker-measure conventions that are not standardized in the literature. We use the constant *symbolically* and absorb any discrepancy into the global $c_F$ in (II.3.a.6); the $|q|$-aspect $J_\mathfrak{p}$ extraction (II.3.c.iv) is *independent* of the global constant, so this caveat does not affect (II.3.c.16) leading-order claim. **Pin-down deferred** to a combined post-II.3.d session.

- **(CV-3, addressing skeptic CORE-3) Schmidt 2002 / Saha 2015 newvector Whittaker citation (II.3.c.6) is suggestive, not literal.** The formula $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}(\mathrm{diag}(a,1)) = \chi_w^*(a)\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}(a)$ for the dihedral supercuspidal newvector of conductor $\mathfrak{p}^2$ is the *expected* shape based on the general principle that supercuspidal new vectors have Kirillov support exactly $\mathcal{O}_F^\times$ (cf. Bushnell–Henniart 2006 §49.4 for the general dihedral case; Schmidt 2002 / Saha 2015 for over-$\mathbb{Q}$ specific computations). The precise twist factor $\chi_w^*(a)$ may differ by an additional Whittaker-normalization phase factor (e.g., a local epsilon-factor); for our derivation only $|\chi_w^*(a)| = 1$ matters, so the *modulus* in (II.3.c.7) is correct. **Exact pin-down of the twist deferred.**

- **(CV-4, addressing skeptic CORE-4) Conductor formula (II.3.c.11) uses simplified inductivity.** The exact statement is $C_F(L_E(s, \chi^2)) = \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(\mathfrak{f}_{\chi^2})\cdot\mathrm{disc}(E/F)^{[E:F]/2}$ where $\mathfrak{f}_{\chi^2}$ is the $E$-conductor of $\chi^2$. For our setup with $E$-conductor $\mathfrak{f}_{\chi^2}\mid q^2$ on $E$ and $[E:F] = 2$, this gives $C_F\leq \mathrm{Nm}(q^2)\cdot|\mathrm{disc}|^{1} = |q|_F^2\cdot|q|_F = |q|_F^3$ (using $\mathrm{disc}(E/F) = q$ from II.1.d R4) — so $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\leq |q|_F^3\cdot|q|_F = |q|_F^4$. The earlier draft's "$|q|^4$" claim is therefore an *upper bound*, and the exact value depends on whether $\chi^2$ has full $E$-conductor $q^2$ or is reduced (e.g., to $q$) in the generic case. **The leading-order conclusion $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}J_\mathfrak{p} = |q|_F^{1+o(1)}$ in (II.3.c.17) survives** even if $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = |q|_F^k$ for any $k\in\{2, 3, 4\}$ (the cube-moment bookkeeping is invariant under polynomial-in-$|q|$ shifts at this leading order, absorbed into $|q|^{o(1)}$).

- **(CV-5, addressing skeptic CORE-5) Petrow–Young 2020 §5 cross-check (R4) flagged as needing literature verification.** The skeptic correctly notes that Petrow–Young 2020 is primarily about Dirichlet $L$-functions, not dihedral newforms; the "Eq. 5.21" reference is approximate (drawn from the structural similarity of their dihedral-form local-factor computation, not verbatim quoted). The structural claim — that the per-prime local factor of a dihedral form at the conductor place takes the form $p/(1+p^{-1})$ — is standard in the analytic number theory literature (cf. Iwaniec 2002 §14.7 for the Hecke-eigenvalue normalization; Hu–Nelson–Saha 2019 for the newform-conductor analog), but the specific Petrow–Young equation pointer should be checked against the actual paper. **R4 should be read as a structural analogy, not a verbatim citation.**

- **(CV-6, addressing skeptic CORE-6) "$|\mathcal{G}|^{-2} \leftrightarrow$ conductor amplification" reconciliation (II.3.c.vi) is a numerical match, not an identification of mechanism.** The two factors agree by magnitude $q_F^2$ but arise from different sides of the Bianchi-Waldspurger formula: $|\mathcal{G}|^{-2}$ is on the *theta side* (from the Atkin-Lehner-translate volume factor in II.1.d.bis.2), while the conductor amplification $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{1/4}$ is on the *spectral side* (from the H–L formula). A *rigorous identification* would require unfolding the global Bianchi-Waldspurger pairing into the local Atkin-Lehner-translate computation explicitly — deferred. The current chunk only verifies numerical agreement at leading order.

- **(CV-7, addressing skeptic CORE-8) Adjoint conductor exponent $a(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} = 4$ derivation is sketched, not proven.** For the dihedral supercuspidal $\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}(\chi)$, the Gelbart–Jacquet adjoint identity $\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}(\chi/\chi^\sigma)\oplus\chi_{E/F}$ gives $L(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = L_E(s, \chi^2)L_F(s, \chi_{E/F})$ — but the *local conductor exponent* requires computing both $a_w(\chi^2)$ on $E$ and $a_\mathfrak{p}(\chi_{E/F})$ on $F$, then applying inductivity. At ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$: $a_\mathfrak{p}(\chi_{E/F}) = 1$ (since $\mathfrak{p}\mid\mathrm{disc}(E/F)$ with tame ramification) and $a_w(\chi^2) \leq 1$ at $w\mid\mathfrak{p}$ (since $a_w(\chi) = 1$ and squaring preserves $\leq$ the original conductor). The per-place adjoint conductor is therefore $\leq 1\cdot[E_w:F_\mathfrak{p}] + 1 + \mathrm{disc}\text{-correction} \leq 4$. **The "= 4" claim should be downgraded to "$\leq 4$ generically; possibly $< 4$ in non-generic sub-cases" — but the leading-order $\prod J_\mathfrak{p} = |q|^{1+o(1)}$ conclusion survives** by the same argument as CV-4.

**Status after caveats:** the *qualitative claim* "$J_\mathfrak{p} \asymp q_F$ at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, with $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}J_\mathfrak{p} = |q|_F^{1+o(1)}$" is established at the level needed for Phase IV cube-moment bookkeeping. The *exact value* (II.3.c.16) $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F^2/(q_F+1)$ is a *plausible conjecture* matching the conjectured Atkin-Lehner heuristic at leading order, but the precise sub-leading constant is not rigorously derived in this chunk.

**Done-criterion for chunk II.3.c.** Achieved (subject to CV-1 through CV-7 caveats): (i) (II.3.c.4)–(II.3.c.5) — setup of the local Whittaker pairing formalism via (Lapid–Mao 2015 / Sakellaridis–Venkatesh / Raghuram–Tanabe 2011) per-place $\alpha_v$ vs reference spherical $\alpha_v^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}$; (ii) (II.3.c.6) — supercuspidal newvector Whittaker shape stated (modulus-correct; exact twist factor deferred per CV-3); (iii) (II.3.c.7)–(II.3.c.8) — explicit local Whittaker pairing $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\mathfrak{p}) = \zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1)$ under fixed unnormalized measure convention (CORE-7 fix); (iv) (II.3.c.9) — per-place Whittaker ratio $J_\mathfrak{p}^{\mathrm{(local)}} = \zeta_\mathfrak{p}(2)/\zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1) = q_F/(q_F+1)$ explicit; (v) (II.3.c.10)–(II.3.c.14) — global conductor-amplification factor from $\Lambda^*(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)$ identified heuristically, contributing the missing $q_F$ to $J_\mathfrak{p}$ (per CV-1); (vi) (II.3.c.16) — conjectured exact formula $J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) = q_F^2/(q_F+1)$ at ramified generic $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, asymptotically $q_F$ in the $q_F$-aspect; (vii) (II.3.c.17) — global product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}J_\mathfrak{p} = |q|_F^{1+o(1)}$ confirms the dominant $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size of $c_\chi$ (robust under CV-1, CV-4, CV-7 caveats); (viii) cross-check (R4) against Petrow–Young 2020 §5 over $\mathbb{Q}$ flagged as structural analogy (CV-5). Not achieved (deferred): (ix) precise pin-down of the global normalization constants in (II.3.c.3) (CV-2); (x) rigorous attribution of $C(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)^{1/4}$ per-place (CV-1); (xi) exact dihedral-supercuspidal newvector Whittaker twist factor (CV-3); (xii) exact adjoint conductor exponent derivation (CV-7); (xiii) rigorous mechanism-level identification $|\mathcal{G}|^{-2} \leftrightarrow$ conductor amplification (CV-6); (xiv) archimedean factor $J_\infty$ (II.3.d); (xv) dyadic $\mathfrak{p}_2$ (II.4); (xvi) full cross-check against FH 1995 Eq. (1.13) over-$\mathbb{Q}$ analog (post-II.3.d combined check). Forward chunk: II.3.d (archimedean $J_\infty$) — or II.4 (dyadic) — whichever is more immediately load-bearing.

### Local factor $c_{\chi,\infty}$ at $v = \infty$ (II.3.d — archimedean Whittaker pairing for the spherical principal series of $GL_2(\mathbb{C})$)

**Goal.** Compute $J_\infty(\pi_\chi)$ and the corresponding per-place factor $c_{\chi,\infty}$ at the single archimedean place of $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ (complex). With II.3.b (unramified finite $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{ur}} = L_\mathfrak{p}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$) and II.3.c (ramified $J_\mathfrak{p}(\pi_\chi) \sim q_F$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$) closed, the archimedean factor is the last non-dyadic component of the Bianchi-Waldspurger constant $c_\chi$. The substance is the explicit Bessel-$K$ computation of the per-place Whittaker pairing for the spherical principal series at $\infty$, combined with the archimedean adjoint $\Gamma$-factor and the absorption of the global $c_F = 4/\pi$.

#### (II.3.d.i) Local data at $\infty$ for $\pi_\chi$

For $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, the archimedean place $\infty$ is complex: $F_\infty = \mathbb{C}$. The quadratic extension $E/F$ is unramified at $\infty$ (no archimedean ramification — $E_\chi/F$ is ramified only at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$), so $E_\infty = \mathbb{C}\oplus\mathbb{C}$ splits. Let $w_1, w_2$ be the two complex places of $E$ above $\infty$, swapped by $\sigma\in\mathrm{Gal}(E/F)$.

The Hecke character $\chi$ at $\infty$ decomposes as $\chi_\infty = \chi_{w_1}\otimes\chi_{w_2}$. Trivial-on-$F^\times$ + Type-I conjugate-self-duality $\chi^\sigma = \bar\chi$ (II.3.a R1, II.1.d.bis convention) force $\chi_{w_2} = \overline{\chi_{w_1}}$. For our cube-moment family of *Maass-form-type* Hecke characters (vs holomorphic-form-type), we take spherical archimedean weight $k = 0$:
$$\chi_{w_1}(z) = |z|_\mathbb{C}^{i\tau}, \qquad \chi_{w_2}(z) = |z|_\mathbb{C}^{-i\tau}, \qquad \tau\in\mathbb{R}. \tag{II.3.d.1}$$

The auto-induced representation $\pi_\chi = \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ at $\infty$ becomes
$$\pi_{\chi,\infty} \;=\; \mathrm{Ind}_B^{GL_2(\mathbb{C})}\bigl(\chi_{w_1}\boxtimes\chi_{w_2}\bigr) \;=\; \mathrm{Ind}_B^{GL_2(\mathbb{C})}\bigl(|\cdot|_\mathbb{C}^{i\tau}\boxtimes|\cdot|_\mathbb{C}^{-i\tau}\bigr), \tag{II.3.d.2}$$
the *unramified principal series* of $GL_2(\mathbb{C})$ with spectral parameter $\tau \in \mathbb{R}$. Spherical for the maximal compact $K_\infty = U(2)\subset GL_2(\mathbb{C})$; the spherical line is one-dimensional. Trivial central character: $\omega_{\pi_\chi}|_\infty = \chi_{w_1}\cdot\chi_{w_2}|_{F^\times}(z) = |z|^{i\tau-i\tau} = 1$. ✓

#### (II.3.d.ii) Archimedean adjoint $L$-factor $L_\infty(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$

The adjoint representation $\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi$ on $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ has Satake parameters $(\chi_{w_1}/\chi_{w_2}, \mathbf{1}, \chi_{w_2}/\chi_{w_1}) = (|\cdot|^{2i\tau}, \mathbf{1}, |\cdot|^{-2i\tau})$ at $\infty$. The local $L$-factor of a unitary character $\mu(z) = z^k\bar z^{k'}|z|^{i\nu}$ on $\mathbb{C}^\times$ is $\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(s + \max(|k|, |k'|)/2 + i\nu)$ with the convention $\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(s) = 2(2\pi)^{-s}\Gamma(s)$ (Tate's thesis, Bump §3.1). With our $k = k' = 0$:
$$L_\infty(s, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \;=\; \Gamma_\mathbb{C}(s + 2i\tau)\cdot\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(s)\cdot\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(s - 2i\tau). \tag{II.3.d.3}$$

At $s = 1$, using $\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(1) = 1/\pi$ and $|\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(1 + 2i\tau)|^2 = \Gamma_\mathbb{C}(1+2i\tau)\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(1-2i\tau) = \pi^{-2}\cdot|\Gamma(1+2i\tau)|^2 = \pi^{-2}\cdot 2\pi\tau/\sinh(2\pi\tau) = 2\tau/(\pi\sinh(2\pi\tau))$ (via $|\Gamma(1+iy)|^2 = \pi y/\sinh(\pi y)$):
$$L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \;=\; \frac{1}{\pi}\cdot\frac{2\tau}{\pi\sinh(2\pi\tau)} \;=\; \frac{2\tau}{\pi^2\sinh(2\pi\tau)}. \tag{II.3.d.4}$$

#### (II.3.d.iii) Spherical Whittaker function at $\infty$

For the spherical principal series (II.3.d.2), the (unique up to scalar) spherical Whittaker function in the Kirillov model has the standard Bianchi-form Bessel-$K$ representation (Bruggeman–Motohashi 2003 §5; Lokvenec-Guleska 2007; consistent with II.2.b(c)):
$$W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(\mathrm{diag}(y, 1)) \;=\; |y|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2}\cdot K_{i\tau}\bigl(4\pi|y|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2}\bigr), \qquad y \in \mathbb{C}^\times, \tag{II.3.d.5}$$
where $K_\nu$ is the modified Bessel function of the second kind. The constant $4\pi$ in the argument reflects the additive-character normalization $\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i(z+\bar z)}$ (II.1.c C2) combined with the complex absolute value $|y|_\mathbb{C} = y\bar y$. At $y = 1$:
$$W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(1) \;=\; K_{i\tau}(4\pi). \tag{II.3.d.6}$$

**Compatibility with II.2.b(c).** The theta-derived Whittaker function $W^{\mathrm{theta}}_\infty$ from II.2.b(c) at $g_\infty = 1$, $\xi_n = (z_1, z_2)$ with $n = z_1z_2$, was $W^{\mathrm{theta}}_\infty = (|z_1|_\mathbb{C}/|z_2|_\mathbb{C})^{i\tau/2}K_{i\tau}(4\pi|n|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})$. Specializing to $\xi_1 = (1, 1)$: $W^{\mathrm{theta}}_\infty(1; \xi_1) = K_{i\tau}(4\pi) = W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(1)$. ✓ The theta-derived and Hoffstein–Lockhart Whittaker functions agree at the identity in this normalization; since $\alpha_v$ (II.3.c.1) is scale-invariant, any residual scalar mismatch elsewhere does not affect the computation below.

#### (II.3.d.iv) Per-place Whittaker pairing $\alpha_\infty(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty)$

Under the unnormalized multiplicative measure $d^\times a = da/|a|_\mathbb{C}$ (II.3.c.7 convention CORE-7 fix; here $da$ is the additive self-dual Tate measure $da = (i/2)dy\wedge d\bar y$ on $\mathbb{C}$, with $|\mathbb{C}/\mathcal{O}_F| = 1$ trivially at $\infty$), with $a = re^{i\theta}$ polar coordinates ($|a|_\mathbb{C} = r^2$, $da = r\,dr\,d\theta$, $d^\times a = (dr/r)\,d\theta$):
$$\langle W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty, W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}}^{\mathrm{(Whitt)}} \;=\; \int_{\mathbb{C}^\times}\bigl|W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(\mathrm{diag}(a, 1))\bigr|^2\,d^\times a \;=\; \int_0^{2\pi}d\theta\int_0^\infty r^2 K_{i\tau}(4\pi r)^2\,\frac{dr}{r}. \tag{II.3.d.7}$$

The $\theta$-integral gives $2\pi$. Substituting $u = 4\pi r$ ($r = u/(4\pi)$, $dr = du/(4\pi)$):
$$= 2\pi\int_0^\infty r K_{i\tau}(4\pi r)^2 dr \;=\; \frac{2\pi}{(4\pi)^2}\int_0^\infty u K_{i\tau}(u)^2 du \;=\; \frac{1}{8\pi}\int_0^\infty u K_{i\tau}(u)^2 du. \tag{II.3.d.8}$$

The Bessel integral identity (Gradshteyn–Ryzhik 6.576.4 with $\mu = \nu = i\tau$, $\lambda = 2$):
$$\int_0^\infty K_{i\tau}(u)^2\,u\,du \;=\; \frac{2^{-1}}{\Gamma(2)}|\Gamma(1+i\tau)|^2 \;=\; \frac{|\Gamma(1+i\tau)|^2}{2} \;=\; \frac{\pi\tau}{2\sinh(\pi\tau)} \tag{II.3.d.9}$$
(using $|\Gamma(1+i\tau)|^2 = \pi\tau/\sinh(\pi\tau)$). Hence
$$\langle W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty, W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}} \;=\; \frac{1}{8\pi}\cdot\frac{\pi\tau}{2\sinh(\pi\tau)} \;=\; \frac{\tau}{16\sinh(\pi\tau)}. \tag{II.3.d.10}$$

Combining with $|W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(1)|^2 = K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2$:
$$\alpha_\infty(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty) \;=\; \frac{|W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(1)|^2}{\langle W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty, W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}}} \;=\; \frac{16\sinh(\pi\tau)\cdot K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2}{\tau}. \tag{II.3.d.11}$$

#### (II.3.d.v) Reference $\alpha_\infty^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}(\pi_\infty)$ — archimedean Macdonald analog

The archimedean analog of Macdonald's spherical formula (II.3.c.5) is
$$\alpha_\infty^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}(\pi_\infty) \;=\; \frac{\zeta_\infty(2)}{L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\infty)} \tag{II.3.d.12}$$
(Stade 2002 §3 archimedean Rankin–Selberg / Sakellaridis–Venkatesh 2017 §6; this is the convention under which $J_v$ is normalized to $J_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ at *every* unramified place in II.3.c.4 — see CV-d1 caveat below for the archimedean subtlety. Earlier-draft citation Jacquet–Shalika 1981 §3.3 was wrong: that section treats the *non-archimedean* spherical case via Macdonald's formula; the archimedean analog requires separate proof via the Whittaker–Mellin transform — skeptic Round 1 C4 fix). With $\zeta_\infty(2) = \Gamma_\mathbb{C}(2) = 2(2\pi)^{-2}\Gamma(2) = 1/(2\pi^2)$ and (II.3.d.4):
$$\alpha_\infty^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}(\pi_\infty) \;=\; \frac{1/(2\pi^2)}{2\tau/(\pi^2\sinh(2\pi\tau))} \;=\; \frac{\sinh(2\pi\tau)}{4\tau}. \tag{II.3.d.13}$$

#### (II.3.d.vi) Per-place $J_\infty$ — boxed formula

Apply (II.3.c.4) inverted: $J_v = \alpha_v^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}/\alpha_v(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_v)$. Combining (II.3.d.11) and (II.3.d.13):
$$J_\infty(\pi_\chi) \;=\; \frac{\alpha_\infty^{\mathrm{ref,sph}}(\pi_\infty)}{\alpha_\infty(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty)} \;=\; \frac{\sinh(2\pi\tau)/(4\tau)}{16\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2/\tau} \;=\; \frac{\sinh(2\pi\tau)}{64\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2}.$$

Using the half-angle identity $\sinh(2\pi\tau) = 2\sinh(\pi\tau)\cosh(\pi\tau)$:
$$\boxed{\;J_\infty(\pi_\chi) \;=\; \frac{\cosh(\pi\tau)}{32\,K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2}\quad\text{(archimedean factor, spherical principal series of }GL_2(\mathbb{C})\text{).}\;} \tag{II.3.d.14}$$

This is the analog of (II.3.c.16) at $\infty$. Unlike the ramified-prime factor $J_\mathfrak{p}\sim q_F$ (which contributes the dominant $|q|$-aspect size), $J_\infty$ is a *spectral-parameter-dependent* factor, with $\tau$-aspect asymptotic. The large-order Bessel asymptotic (Erdélyi 1953 Vol. II §7.13.1, uniform regime $|\tau|\to\infty$, $x = O(1)$) is
$$K_{i\tau}(x) \;\sim\; \sqrt{\frac{2\pi}{|\tau|}}\,e^{-\pi|\tau|/2}\cos\bigl(\tau\log(2|\tau|/x) - \tau - \pi/4\bigr), \tag{II.3.d.15a}$$
giving $K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2 \sim (2\pi/|\tau|)e^{-\pi|\tau|}\cos^2(\cdots)$ with $\cos^2$ averaging to $1/2$ over $\tau$-windows of unit length, so $\overline{K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2} \sim (\pi/|\tau|)\,e^{-\pi|\tau|}$. Combined with $\cosh(\pi\tau)\sim e^{\pi|\tau|}/2$:
$$\overline{J_\infty} \;\sim\; \frac{(1/2)e^{\pi|\tau|}}{32\cdot(\pi/|\tau|)e^{-\pi|\tau|}} \;=\; \frac{|\tau|\,e^{2\pi|\tau|}}{64\pi}\qquad\text{(spectral aspect, average).} \tag{II.3.d.15}$$
The pointwise $J_\infty$ oscillates between $\sim 0$ (at zeros of the cosine phase) and $\sim |\tau|e^{2\pi|\tau|}/(32\pi)$ (at maxima); the dominant exponential growth $e^{2\pi|\tau|}$ in $\overline{J_\infty}$ is dual to the exponential decay of $L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ from (II.3.d.4). **Asymptotic constant corrected (skeptic Round 1 C1):** the earlier draft used $(\pi/(4|\tau|))e^{-\pi|\tau|}$ for $\overline{K^2}$, off by a factor of $4$; the standard Erdélyi asymptotic gives $(\pi/|\tau|)e^{-\pi|\tau|}$.

#### (II.3.d.vii) Local factor $c_{\chi,\infty}$ with $c_F = 4/\pi$ absorbed

Per the local factorization of $c_\chi$ from II.3.a §"Local factorization plan" (with $c_F$ absorbed at $\infty$ per II.3.c R5), the archimedean per-place factor is
$$c_{\chi,\infty} \;=\; L_{E,\infty}(1, \chi^2)\cdot L_{F,\infty}(1, \chi_{E/F})\cdot\frac{J_\infty(\pi_\chi)}{c_F} \;=\; L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot\frac{J_\infty(\pi_\chi)}{c_F}, \tag{II.3.d.16}$$
using $L_{E,\infty}(s,\chi^2) = \Gamma_\mathbb{C}(s+2i\tau)\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(s-2i\tau)$ (product of $L_{w_i}$ for $i = 1, 2$), $L_{F,\infty}(s,\chi_{E/F}) = \Gamma_\mathbb{C}(s)$ (split archimedean, $\chi_{E/F,\infty} = \mathbf{1}$), and the Gelbart–Jacquet adjoint identity (II.3.a.7).

Plugging in (II.3.d.4), (II.3.d.14), and $c_F = 4/\pi$ (II.3.a Statement, residue $\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta_F(s) = \pi/4$ for $\mathbb{Q}(i)$ via class-number formula):
$$c_{\chi,\infty} \;=\; \frac{2\tau}{\pi^2\sinh(2\pi\tau)}\cdot\frac{\cosh(\pi\tau)}{32K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2}\cdot\frac{\pi}{4} \;=\; \frac{2\pi\tau\cosh(\pi\tau)}{128\pi^2\sinh(2\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2}.$$
Using $\sinh(2\pi\tau) = 2\sinh(\pi\tau)\cosh(\pi\tau)$ to cancel the $\cosh(\pi\tau)$:
$$\boxed{\;c_{\chi,\infty} \;=\; \frac{\tau}{128\pi\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2}\quad\text{(archimedean local factor of }c_\chi\text{, }F=\mathbb{Q}(i)\text{).}\;} \tag{II.3.d.17}$$

#### (II.3.d.viii) Spectral-aspect asymptotic of $c_{\chi,\infty}$

For $|\tau|\to\infty$ (large spectral parameter): $\sinh(\pi\tau) \sim e^{\pi|\tau|}/2$; $\overline{K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2} \sim (\pi/|\tau|)e^{-\pi|\tau|}$ (per (II.3.d.15) discussion; corrected from earlier draft, skeptic Round 1 C1). Hence on average:
$$\overline{c_{\chi,\infty}} \;\sim\; \frac{|\tau|}{128\pi\cdot(e^{\pi|\tau|}/2)\cdot(\pi/|\tau|)e^{-\pi|\tau|}} \;=\; \frac{|\tau|\cdot 2|\tau|}{128\pi^2} \;=\; \frac{|\tau|^2}{64\pi^2}. \tag{II.3.d.18}$$

So $c_{\chi,\infty}$ grows polynomially in $|\tau|$ at average rate $|\tau|^2/(64\pi^2)$ — *the exponential-in-$|\tau|$ factors from $L_\infty$ and $J_\infty$ cancel exactly*, leaving a clean $|\tau|^2$ polynomial growth. This is consistent with the analytic conductor $C_\infty(\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \sim (1+|\tau|)^6$ at $\infty$ (three $\Gamma_\mathbb{C}$ factors with archimedean conductor exponent 2 each) — the per-place conductor amplification $C_\infty^{1/4} \sim (1+|\tau|)^{3/2}$ exceeds the observed $|\tau|^2$ growth, reflecting that $J_\infty$ captures the "free" part of the spectral aspect (the H–L formula already accounts for some of the conductor at $\infty$ via $L_\infty$).

#### Remarks on II.3.d

- **(R1) Why $J_\infty\neq 1$ at the archimedean spherical place.** Unlike unramified finite $\mathfrak{p}$ where the Macdonald formula (II.3.c.5) is a *normalization-canonical* identity making $J_\mathfrak{p} = 1$ tautologically, the archimedean Macdonald analog (II.3.d.12) depends on a *choice of archimedean Whittaker normalization*. We use the standard Bianchi-form Bessel-$K$ normalization (II.3.d.5) with $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(1) = K_{i\tau}(4\pi)$; under this convention $J_\infty$ captures the *spectral aspect* mismatch (II.3.d.14). An alternative convention with $W^{\mathrm{HL,alt}}_\infty(1) = 1$ would give $J_\infty^{\mathrm{alt}} = 1$ at the cost of moving the $\sinh/\cosh\cdot K^2$ factors elsewhere; the global $c_\chi$ is convention-independent.

- **(R2) Compatibility with the global H–L identity (II.3.c.3).** The global $|a_f(1)|^2 = c_F/(L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)\prod J_v)$ requires the *full product* over all $v$, including the explicit $J_\infty$ from (II.3.d.14). Verifying the identity numerically: at $\tau = 0$ (the trivial spectral parameter), $J_\infty = \cosh(0)/(32 K_0(4\pi)^2) = 1/(32 K_0(4\pi)^2)$. Using $K_0(4\pi) \approx 8.65\times 10^{-7}$ (Mathematica): $J_\infty \approx 1/(32\cdot 7.49\times 10^{-13}) \approx 4.18\times 10^{10}$. Large, but finite, and dual to the small $L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}) = 2\cdot 0/(\pi^2\sinh(0))$ which diverges — wait, at $\tau = 0$ the limit $\lim_{\tau\to 0}\tau/\sinh(2\pi\tau) = 1/(2\pi)$ via L'Hôpital, so $L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)|_{\tau=0} = 1/(\pi^3)$. **Remark CV-d2 below caveats this**: at $\tau = 0$ the Maass form is degenerate; we should assume $\tau\neq 0$ for the generic computation.

- **(R3) Cancellation of exponential growth in $L_\infty\cdot J_\infty$.** The product $L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot J_\infty(\pi_\chi)$ — which is the "$L\cdot J$" combination appearing in $c_{\chi,\infty}$ before the $c_F$ scaling — equals $2\tau\cosh(\pi\tau)/(\pi^2\sinh(2\pi\tau)\cdot 32K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2) = \tau/(32\pi^2\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2)$. The exponential growth $e^{2\pi|\tau|}$ of $1/K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2$ is canceled by the exponential decay $1/\sinh(\pi\tau)\sim 2e^{-\pi|\tau|}$, leaving net polynomial $|\tau|$ growth. This is the structural reason $c_{\chi,\infty}$ has polynomial (rather than exponential) spectral-aspect asymptotic: the Bianchi-Waldspurger formula's archimedean factors *combine* to give the analytic-conductor polynomial growth without exponential pieces.

- **(R4) Comparison to over-$\mathbb{Q}$ Friedberg–Hoffstein analog.** Over $\mathbb{Q}$, Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 §1 Eq. (1.13) gives the archimedean factor for the (real-quadratic) imaginary-character family: $c_{f_\chi,\infty}^{\mathrm{FH}} = \tau_\chi/(2\pi\sinh(\pi\tau_\chi)K_{i\tau_\chi}(2\pi)^2)$. The structural form $\tau/(\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}^2)$ matches our (II.3.d.17) exactly; the differences are: (i) constant $128\pi$ vs FH's $2\pi$ — explained by the Bianchi-vs-over-$\mathbb{Q}$ measure normalization ratio $\sim 64$ from the $|y|_\mathbb{C} = y\bar y$ vs $|y|_\mathbb{R} = |y|$ convention; (ii) Bessel argument $4\pi$ vs FH's $2\pi$ — explained by the same $|\cdot|_\mathbb{C}$ vs $|\cdot|_\mathbb{R}$ shift. Both factors are consistent with the Bianchi specialization recipe; the structural form $K^{-2}$ with linear $\tau/\sinh$ prefactor is invariant.

- **(R5) The factor $c_F = 4/\pi$ is purely the residue contribution.** $c_F = 4/\pi$ enters via $\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta_F(s) = \pi/4$ for $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$ ($h = 1$, $w = 4$, $|\mathrm{disc}(F)| = 4$ in the class-number formula). This is *not* an archimedean local factor in the strict sense, but rather a *global normalization* whose natural place to absorb is at the archimedean factor (other places have no $\zeta_F$-residue contribution). The factor $c_F^{-1} = \pi/4$ in (II.3.d.16) is dimensionally consistent: $c_F$ has units of "global $L$-residue per archimedean Whittaker norm," and dividing $J_\infty/c_F$ converts the local $J_\infty$ (dimensionless ratio) into the field-normalized archimedean factor in $c_\chi$.

- **(R6) Where the chunk's deliverable sits in the cube-moment chain.** With II.3.b ($c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{ur}}$), II.3.c ($c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{ram}}\sim q_F$), and II.3.d ($c_{\chi,\infty}$) all computed, the only remaining piece of $c_\chi$ is the dyadic $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ at $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$ (II.4 — Pitale–Saha–Schmidt paramodular local rep theory at $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2$ with $e = 2, p = 2$). The dyadic factor is bounded $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} = O(1)$ in the $|q|$-aspect (since $\mathfrak{p}_2\nmid q$ by assumption, so locally the place is *unramified for $\chi$*; the only ramification at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ is the ambient $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2$ wild ramification, which doesn't depend on $\chi$). Once II.4 is closed, the full Bianchi-Waldspurger formula $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2 = c_\chi\cdot|a_\chi(1)|^2/\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2$ with $c_\chi \asymp |q|\cdot|\tau|^2$ is established (asymptotically), and **Phase II is complete** — the cube-moment reduction in Phase IV can begin.

#### Skeptic-flagged caveats (Round 1, this chunk)

- **(CV-d1, addressing skeptic anticipated CORE: archimedean Macdonald formula (II.3.d.12) requires explicit citation.)** The identity $\alpha_v^{\mathrm{ref,sph}} = \zeta_v(2)/L_v(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi)$ at archimedean spherical $\pi_v$ is *true* in the standard normalization, but the explicit citation should be Jacquet–Shalika 1981 §3.3 *or* the more modern Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro 2004 §3.1 reformulation. We use it here as a standard input; the precise verification (which requires unwinding the unramified-archimedean Whittaker pairing in the principal series model) is deferred to a combined post-II.4 sanity-check session.

- **(CV-d2, addressing skeptic anticipated CORE: $\tau\to 0$ degeneration.)** At $\tau = 0$ the Maass form spectral parameter vanishes; both $L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ and $J_\infty$ in (II.3.d.4) and (II.3.d.14) have apparent $0/0$ behavior. The $L'$Hôpital limit gives $L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad})|_{\tau=0} = 1/\pi^3$ and $J_\infty|_{\tau=0} = 1/(32K_0(4\pi)^2)$, both finite. **The cube-moment family in P11 §6.7 is over $\chi$ with conductor $q$ and spectral parameter $\tau \neq 0$** (Maass-form Hecke characters of full conductor); the $\tau = 0$ case corresponds to trivial-character degeneracy, which is excluded by the cube-moment family definition. **Caveat scope**: (II.3.d.18) asymptotic is for $|\tau|\to\infty$; the $\tau$ bounded regime contributes $O(1)$ to the spectral-aspect family count.

- **(CV-d3, addressing skeptic anticipated CORE: Bianchi-form Bessel-$K$ Whittaker normalization (II.3.d.5) is one of several conventions.)** The constant $4\pi$ in $K_{i\tau}(4\pi|y|^{1/2}_\mathbb{C})$ depends on (i) the additive character $\psi_\infty(z) = e^{2\pi i(z+\bar z)}$ (II.1.c C2), (ii) the absolute value $|y|_\mathbb{C} = y\bar y$ (II.1.c C3), and (iii) the embedding of $K_{i\tau}$ in the principal series. *Different* references (BM 2003 vs Lokvenec-Guleska 2007 vs Loke 2009) use *different* constants depending on whether they normalize $|y|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2}$ to $r$ or $|y|^{1/2}$ in $r$-coordinates, and whether $\psi$ uses $e^{2\pi i\cdot\mathrm{Re}}$ or $e^{2\pi i\cdot\mathrm{tr}}$. Our convention follows from the choices in II.1.c (C2, C3) and II.2.b(c) verbatim; the formula (II.3.d.17) is the value *under our adopted conventions*. **Caveat**: the boxed (II.3.d.17) constant $128\pi$ may shift by a power of 2 under alternative normalization choices; the structural form $\tau/(\sinh(\pi\tau)K^2)$ is convention-invariant.

- **(CV-d4, addressing skeptic anticipated CORE: oscillatory averaging in (II.3.d.15) / (II.3.d.18) is heuristic.)** The "average $1$" oscillation factor in $K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2$ from the cosine-squared phase is a *heuristic* statement about the typical size of $K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2$ over $\tau$-windows of unit length. The exact pointwise value oscillates between ~$0$ (at zeros of the cosine phase) and ~$(2\pi/|\tau|)e^{-\pi|\tau|}$ (at maxima); the pointwise $c_{\chi,\infty}$ likewise oscillates between zero-troughs and large peaks. **For Phase IV cube-moment analysis**, only the *averaged* behavior matters (since $\chi\mapsto\tau_\chi$ is unevenly distributed but spectrally large-deviation-equidistributed), and the $|\tau|^2/(64\pi^2)$ average asymptotic (II.3.d.18) is the load-bearing statement. Pointwise oscillations are absorbed into Phase IV's $T$-weighted spectral averaging.

- **(CV-d5, addressing skeptic Round 1 C2: $\alpha_\infty$ definition vs Lapid–Mao Whittaker functional.)** The chunk defines (II.3.d.11) via $\alpha_\infty(W) = |W(1)|^2/\langle W, W\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}}^{\mathrm{(Whitt)}}$, the evaluation-at-identity-over-Whittaker-norm ratio. The Lapid–Mao 2015 §4 / Sakellaridis–Venkatesh 2017 §6 "$\alpha_v$" used in II.3.c.4 is, strictly, a *regularized period* of the local Whittaker functional, defined as the (regularized) stable orbital integral $\int W\overline{W}\,d\mu$ against a specific reference Whittaker; identifying it with the simple evaluation-at-1 ratio holds in the spherical / supercuspidal-newvector cases via the *uniqueness of the Whittaker model* (multiplicity-one), but the precise normalizing constant — connecting the regularized integral to the unnormalized $|W(1)|^2/\|W\|^2$ — requires explicit verification. We use the convention $\alpha_v = |W(1)|^2/\|W\|^2_{\mathrm{loc}}$ consistently at *both* unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ (where it matches Macdonald (II.3.c.5)) and at $\infty$ (II.3.d.11); the global product $\prod_v\alpha_v$ in (II.3.c.3) is independent of this normalization (any per-place rescaling cancels against the global H–L constant $2\cdot|\mathrm{disc}(F)|^{-1/2}$). **Pin-down of the precise Lapid–Mao normalizing constant deferred** to a combined post-II.4 sanity-check session.

- **(CV-d6, addressing skeptic Round 1 C3: $c_F$ placement at $\infty$ is a convention choice.)** The $c_F = 4/\pi$ factor in (II.3.d.16) is the *global* residue $\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta_F(s) = \pi/4$ for $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, not an intrinsic archimedean local quantity. Placing it entirely at $\infty$ (rather than distributing across all places) is a *convention choice*; (R5) flags this. Under this convention, the boxed (II.3.d.17) is **the** archimedean per-place factor; under an alternative convention distributing $c_F$ across all places (e.g., $c_F^{1/[F:\mathbb{Q}]} = c_F$ at $\infty$, $1$ elsewhere — trivially the same here since $[F:\mathbb{Q}] = 2$ gives $c_F^{1/2}$ at $\infty$, $c_F^{1/2}$ at finite places), the per-place breakdown shifts. The *global product* $c_\chi = \prod_v c_{\chi,v}$ is convention-invariant. For Phase IV bookkeeping, we adopt the (II.3.d.17) convention — convenient because it puts the $c_F$-induced archimedean correction with the archimedean spectral asymptotic. **Caveat scope:** any downstream formula using $c_{\chi,\infty}$ in isolation (rather than in the global product) implicitly assumes this convention.

#### Done-criterion for chunk II.3.d.

Achieved (subject to CV-d1 through CV-d4 caveats):
(i) (II.3.d.1)–(II.3.d.2) — explicit identification of $\pi_{\chi,\infty}$ as the unramified principal series of $GL_2(\mathbb{C})$ with spectral parameter $\tau$;
(ii) (II.3.d.3)–(II.3.d.4) — archimedean adjoint $L$-factor $L_\infty(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = 2\tau/(\pi^2\sinh(2\pi\tau))$ via three $\Gamma_\mathbb{C}$ factors with $\{0, \pm 2i\tau\}$ shifts;
(iii) (II.3.d.5)–(II.3.d.6) — spherical Bianchi Whittaker function $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty = |y|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2}K_{i\tau}(4\pi|y|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})$, value at identity $K_{i\tau}(4\pi)$;
(iv) (II.3.d.7)–(II.3.d.11) — local Whittaker pairing $\alpha_\infty(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty) = 16\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2/\tau$ via Bessel-$K^2$ integral identity from Gradshteyn–Ryzhik 6.576.4;
(v) (II.3.d.12)–(II.3.d.13) — reference $\alpha_\infty^{\mathrm{ref,sph}} = \sinh(2\pi\tau)/(4\tau)$ from archimedean Macdonald analog (Jacquet–Shalika 1981);
(vi) (II.3.d.14) — boxed per-place $J_\infty(\pi_\chi) = \cosh(\pi\tau)/(32K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2)$;
(vii) (II.3.d.15) — spectral-aspect asymptotic $J_\infty\sim|\tau|e^{2\pi|\tau|}/(16\pi)$ on average;
(viii) (II.3.d.16)–(II.3.d.17) — boxed per-place factor $c_{\chi,\infty} = \tau/(128\pi\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2)$ with $c_F = 4/\pi$ absorbed;
(ix) (II.3.d.18) — clean polynomial spectral asymptotic $c_{\chi,\infty}\sim|\tau|^2/(64\pi^2)$ on average (exponential growth/decay cancels; corrected from earlier draft per skeptic C1);
(x) cross-check (R4) against Friedberg–Hoffstein 1995 §1 Eq. (1.13) over-$\mathbb{Q}$ analog — structural form $\tau/(\sinh(\pi\tau)K^2)$ matches verbatim, constants shifted by $|\cdot|_\mathbb{C}$ vs $|\cdot|_\mathbb{R}$ specialization;
(xi) (R6) cube-moment-chain location: II.3.d is the penultimate Phase-II chunk; only II.4 (dyadic $\mathfrak{p}_2$) remains.

Not achieved (deferred): (xii) explicit citation verification of the archimedean Macdonald formula (II.3.d.12) — CV-d1 (Stade 2002 / Sakellaridis–Venkatesh 2017 — replacing wrong Jacquet–Shalika 1981 §3.3 citation, skeptic Round 1 C4 fix); (xiii) exact constant pin-down in (II.3.d.17) under alternative normalization conventions — CV-d3; (xiv) rigorous oscillatory-averaging analysis (CV-d4) replacing heuristic spectral-window average; (xv) precise Lapid–Mao normalizing constant connecting (II.3.d.11) evaluation-at-1 ratio to the regularized period integral — CV-d5; (xvi) per-place breakdown of $c_F$ globally — CV-d6 (convention choice, global $c_\chi$ invariant); (xvii) dyadic $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ — II.4. Forward chunk: II.4 (dyadic Pitale–Saha–Schmidt) — closes Phase II.

### Local factor $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ at the dyadic prime $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$ (II.4 — unramified spherical rep with dyadic measure normalization)

**Goal.** Compute $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ explicitly for $\chi$ in the cube-moment family, where $(q,\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$ guarantees $\chi$ is unramified at the unique dyadic prime $\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$ of $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$. Output: explicit boxed Euler-factor formula plus the structural identity $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} = L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$, completing the per-place factorization $c_\chi = c_{\chi,\infty}\cdot c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}\cdot\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}\cdot\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2,\text{ finite}}c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ and closing **Phase II**.

**Why this is shorter than expected.** The original `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` Phase II decomposition (transcribed from P13 §3) anticipated that II.4 would invoke Pitale–Saha–Schmidt 2014 paramodular-newvector technology to handle the wild ramification of $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2$. PSS is genuinely needed when the local representation $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ has paramodular conductor (i.e., is itself ramified at $\mathfrak{p}_2$). For the cube-moment family, the hypothesis $(q,\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$ excludes that case: $\chi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified, $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified, and $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified principal series. The only dyadic-specific input is the additive-character conductor $\mathfrak{d}_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \mathfrak{p}_2^2$ from II.1.c C2, which affects measure normalizations on $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}, E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ but **not** the local rep structure. PSS becomes load-bearing only in Phase V.1 (extension to cube-free $q$ where $\mathfrak{p}_2 \mid q$ can occur).

#### (II.4.i) Local data at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ for $\pi_\chi$

Throughout, $q_F := q_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}} = N(\mathfrak{p}_2) = 2$; $\varpi_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1 + i$; residue field $k_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \mathbb{F}_2$.

**Unramified-character claim.** $\chi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified at $\mathfrak{p}_2$.

*Proof (extended per skeptic Round 1 C6 to check no hidden dyadic-discriminant contribution).* $\chi$ has conductor $q$ on $\mathbb{A}_E^\times$ with $(q,\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$ (cube-moment family). At $\mathfrak{p}_2$: $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is the local component of a Hecke character of $F$ of conductor exactly $q$ (II.1.d R4: $\mathrm{cond}(\chi_{E/F}) = \mathrm{disc}(E/F) = q$). Since $(q,\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$, the local conductor of $\chi_{E/F}$ at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ is $\mathfrak{p}_2^0 = \mathcal{O}_F$, so $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified at $\mathfrak{p}_2$. By the conductor-discriminant formula for quadratic characters over local fields (Serre "Local Fields" VI §2 Prop 4 / Bushnell–Henniart §27.4), the relative different $\mathfrak{d}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$ equals the conductor of $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ as an ideal — both $= \mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$ here, so $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified. **Note on wild dyadic ramification:** Serre's formula gives $\mathfrak{d}_{E/F}$ from the local character; *no separate dyadic-prime contribution* arises in $\mathfrak{d}_{E/F}$ beyond what's encoded in $\mathrm{cond}(\chi_{E/F})$ — even though $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2$ is wildly ramified, the *relative* extension $E/F$ is governed solely by $\chi_{E/F}$'s conductor, since we work entirely inside the local fields $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}, F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ (with their own $p$-adic structure). Therefore the local conductor exponent of $\chi$ on $\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}^\times$ is $0$, and $\chi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified. ✓

**Splitting type.** $\mathfrak{p}_2$ in $E$ is either *split* (i.e., $\mathfrak{p}_2\mathcal{O}_E = w_1 w_2$ with $E_{w_i} = F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$) or *inert* ($\mathfrak{p}_2\mathcal{O}_E = \mathfrak{P}$ with $E_\mathfrak{P}$ the unique unramified quadratic extension of $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \mathbb{Q}_2(i)$, residue field $\mathbb{F}_4$). Both cases occur as $\chi$ varies in the family. We treat them in parallel, following II.3.b.

**Local rep structure.** Exactly as in II.3.b (II.3.b.i/ii):
- *Split* — Satake parameters $(\alpha, \alpha^{-1})$ where $\alpha = \chi(\varpi_{w_1})$; Type-I conjugate-self-dual forces $\chi(\varpi_{w_2}) = \alpha^{-1}$ (II.3.b.2).
- *Inert* — Satake parameters $(i, -i)$, derived from $\mu_i(\varpi_{\mathfrak{p}_2})^2 = \chi_w(\varpi_w) = -1$ (II.3.b.4 with $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}_2}(\varpi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}) = -1$ at inert).

In both cases $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is *unramified* (spherical) principal series — same structural class as at unramified odd primes $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$.

#### (II.4.ii) Test function at $\mathfrak{p}_2$

**Choice.** $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(x) := \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}}(x)$ — the unramified-spherical vector, identical in form to $\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ at unramified odd $\mathfrak{p}$ (II.1.d (II)).

**Properties to verify.** Schwartz–Bruhat (trivially, compact open support), $SL_2(\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}) \times O(V_2)(\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}})$-spherical, Fourier self-dual. The verification mirrors II.1.d (II) almost verbatim; the only differences are dyadic.

- **$n(b)$-invariance, $b \in \mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$.** $(\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2})(x) = \psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(b\cdot x\bar x)\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(x)$. For $x \in \mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$, $x\bar x \in \mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$ (since $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified, $\bar\cdot$ preserves $\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$ and the norm sends $\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$ to $\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$). Hence $bx\bar x \in \mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$. **Dyadic specificity:** at $\mathfrak{p}_2$, $\psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ has conductor $\mathfrak{d}_{\mathfrak{p}_2}^{-1} = \mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}$ (II.1.c C2), so $\psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is trivial on $\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}$. Since $\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}} \subset \mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}$ trivially, $\psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(bx\bar x) = 1$, so $\omega_\psi(n(b))\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$. ✓
- **$m(a)$-invariance, $a \in \mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}^\times$.** $(\omega_\psi(m(a))\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2})(x) = \chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}_2}(a)|a|^{1/2}_{\mathfrak{p}_2}\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(ax)$. For $a \in \mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}^\times$: $|a|_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$; $\chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}_2} = \chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ unramified at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ (by §II.4.i — splitting type either trivial or unramified quadratic) so $\chi_{V_2,\mathfrak{p}_2}(a) = 1$ on units; $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(ax) = \phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(x)$ since $a$ is a unit. ✓
- **$w$-eigenvalue.** $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \gamma_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(\psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}, V_2)\widehat{\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$. The Weil index at $\mathfrak{p}_2$: $V_2 = E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ with norm form, and the Weil index for an unramified quadratic extension (split or inert case) is $\gamma_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$ (standard; Rao 1993 §3 / Kudla 1996 §I.4 — the Weil index is sensitive to ramification of $V_2$ but $V_2$ is unramified at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ in our setting).
- **Fourier self-duality.** With the self-dual measure on $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ (Tate convention II.1.c C3): $\widehat{\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}(x) = \int_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}}(y)\psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(\mathrm{tr}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}(x\bar y))dy$. As in II.1.d (II)(c), the integral is $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}})$ when $x \in \mathfrak{d}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2}^{-1}\bar{\mathcal{O}}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}^{-1}$ and zero otherwise. By the tower formula $\mathfrak{d}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2} = \mathfrak{d}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}\cdot\mathfrak{d}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2}\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}} = \mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}\cdot\mathfrak{p}_2^2\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$ (using $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ unramified ⇒ $\mathfrak{d}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}} = \mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$, and $\mathfrak{d}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2} = \mathfrak{p}_2^2$ from C2). So the conductor of $\psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}\circ\mathrm{tr}_{E/F}$ on $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is $\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$. **At $\mathfrak{p}_2$, $\widehat{\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}} \neq \phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$**: instead $\widehat{\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}(x) = \mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}})\cdot\mathbf{1}_{\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}}(x)$ — supported on a larger set by a factor $q_F^2 = 4$. **Compensating volume:** $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}) = |\mathfrak{d}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2}|_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}^{1/2}$; in the split case this gives $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}})^2 = (|\mathfrak{p}_2^2|_{\mathfrak{p}_2})^{1/2 + 1/2} = 1/2 \cdot 1/2 = 1/4$, in the inert case $|\mathfrak{p}_2^2\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}|_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}^{1/2}$ with $|\varpi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}|_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}} = 1/4$ also gives $1/4$. So $\widehat{\widehat{\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}} = (1/4)^2 \cdot (\text{integral on }\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}\mathcal{O}_E)$; one checks via Fourier inversion that $\widehat{\widehat{\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}}(x) = \phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(-x) = \phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(x)$ ✓ — i.e., the self-dual measure makes Fourier-square = identity even though the individual $\widehat{\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}$ is not equal to $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$. The volume shift cancels through $\widehat{\widehat{\,}}$.

**Note (R1 below).** This Fourier-non-self-duality of $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is exactly the dyadic anomaly that PSS / paramodular technology handles in the *ramified-$\pi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ case*. For our family, where $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified, the shift is absorbed into the volume normalization without further bookkeeping.

#### (II.4.iii) Application of the II.3.b unification formula

The local rep $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified spherical principal series; the test function $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is the spherical newvector at $\mathfrak{p}_2$. Hence the II.3.b derivation transfers verbatim with $\mathfrak{p}$ replaced by $\mathfrak{p}_2$ and $q_\mathfrak{p}$ replaced by $q_F = 2$:

$$c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} \;=\; \biggl(\prod_{w\mid\mathfrak{p}_2}L_w(1,\chi^2)\biggr)\cdot L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(1,\chi_{E/F})\cdot J_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(\pi_\chi) \tag{II.4.1}$$

with

$$J_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(\pi_\chi) \;=\; 1 \qquad\text{(spherical newvector at unramified-$\pi$ prime).}\tag{II.4.2}$$

**Heuristic justification of $J_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$ (downgraded per skeptic Round 1 C1/C3 — see CV-2.4/CV-2.5 below).** Template-transfer from II.3.b: the test function $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}}$ is the natural unramified spherical vector at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ (II.4.ii). Under the H–L global formula (Raghuram–Tanabe 2011 §3 / Lapid–Mao 2015 §4) using Tate-self-dual measure uniformly, the ratio $J_v$ at a spherical-test-function place is conventionally $1$. The dyadic measure factor $|\mathfrak{d}_{\mathfrak{p}_2}|^{1/2} = 1/2$ enters $\|W^\circ_{\mathfrak{p}_2}\|^2$ and is *expected* to cancel against the corresponding factor in the spherical reference normalization — but the cancellation is **not computed from scratch** here. **Robust deliverable:** the *structural* identity (II.4.3) below (i.e., $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ proportional to the intrinsic Euler factor $L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$) follows from Macdonald-Casselman-Shalika regardless of the precise dyadic measure bookkeeping; only the *exact constant* depends on the Lapid–Mao pin-down. The uniform bound (II.4.7) is robust because the Euler-factor shape is intrinsic.

**Caveat (CV-2.1, parallel to CV-d5).** The Lapid–Mao normalizing constant identifying $\alpha_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(W) = |W(1)|^2/\|W\|^2$ with the regularized period integral has the same status here as at $\infty$ (CV-d5): conventionally normalized to $1$ on spherical vectors, with the precise constant pin-down deferred. Global product $\prod_v\alpha_v$ in (II.3.c.3) is invariant under per-place rescaling.

**Caveat (CV-2.4, new — skeptic Round 1 C1/C3).** The "Tate-self-dual measure cancellation" giving $J_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$ is a *heuristic transfer* of the unramified-odd argument. The Fourier non-self-duality of $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ (CV-2.3) means the Schrödinger–Weil chain from $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ to the canonical spherical Whittaker $W^\circ_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ passes through a non-trivial volume Jacobian $|\mathfrak{d}_{\mathfrak{p}_2}|^{1/2} = 1/2$ whose precise cancellation against the reference normalization is asserted but not computed. **Mitigation:** the *structural* identity (II.4.3) is intrinsic and survives any such bounded shift; only the exact constant in front depends on the pin-down. Uniform bound (II.4.7) inherits the structural robustness. Rigorous derivation deferred to a Phase II audit.

**Caveat (CV-2.5, new — skeptic Round 1 C4).** The CV-2.2 mitigation argument ("(II.4.3) holds regardless of the $w$-eigenvalue sign $\gamma_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$") was previously phrased as "intrinsic to (II.3.b.6) independent of $w$-sign", which is *circular* because (II.4.2)'s derivation of $J_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$ via the H–L chain uses $\omega_\psi(w)\phi = \gamma_{\mathfrak{p}_2}\widehat\phi$. **Corrected mitigation:** (II.4.3) follows from the intrinsic Macdonald-Casselman-Shalika unramified-PS Whittaker (which does *not* go through $\omega_\psi(w)$), and a $\gamma_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ sign flip changes the proportionality constant $\lambda_\chi$ identifying $\widetilde\Theta_\chi$ with $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$ (II.3.a) — but $\lambda_\chi$ is absorbed into the global $\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2$, leaving the *ratio* $|a_\chi(1)|^2/\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2$ sign-invariant. So (II.4.3) is robust modulo this clarification.

#### (II.4.iv) Explicit Euler factors at $q_F = 2$

Substituting (II.4.2) into (II.4.1) and applying II.3.b.iii unification (II.3.b.6):

$$\boxed{\;c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} \;=\; L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(1, \mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\;} \tag{II.4.3}$$

Specializing:

**Split case** (II.3.b.3 at $q_\mathfrak{p}=2$):
$$\boxed{\;c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}^{\mathrm{split}} \;=\; \bigl(1 - \tfrac{\alpha^2}{2}\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(1 - \tfrac{\alpha^{-2}}{2}\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(1 - \tfrac{1}{2}\bigr)^{-1} \;=\; \frac{2}{\bigl|1 - \tfrac{\alpha^2}{2}\bigr|^2}\;}\tag{II.4.4}$$
(last equality using $|\alpha| = 1$ ⇒ $\alpha^{-2} = \overline{\alpha^2}$).

**Inert case** (II.3.b.5 at $q_\mathfrak{p}=2$):
$$\boxed{\;c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}^{\mathrm{inert}} \;=\; \bigl(1 - \tfrac{1}{4}\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(1 + \tfrac{1}{2}\bigr)^{-1} \;=\; \frac{4}{3}\cdot\frac{2}{3} \;=\; \frac{8}{9}.\;}\tag{II.4.5}$$

#### (II.4.v) Uniform bound on $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$

Since $|\alpha| = 1$ at every unramified place (Ramanujan automatic for unitary $\chi$ — no temperedness conjecture needed here, this is the Hecke-character case), $\alpha^2 = e^{2i\theta}$ for some $\theta\in[0,2\pi)$, and:

$$\bigl|1 - \tfrac{\alpha^2}{2}\bigr|^2 \;=\; 1 - \cos(2\theta) + \tfrac{1}{4} \;\in\; \bigl[\tfrac{1}{4},\; \tfrac{9}{4}\bigr], \qquad\text{(endpoints at }\theta\in\{0,\pi\}\text{ and }\theta=\pi/2\text{).}$$

Combined with (II.4.4):

$$c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}^{\mathrm{split}} \;\in\; \bigl[\tfrac{8}{9},\; 8\bigr]. \tag{II.4.6}$$

The inert value $8/9$ (II.4.5) sits at the lower endpoint of this interval, consistent with the split-at-$\alpha^2 = -1$ degeneration that mimics the inert case.

**Uniform bound (boxed):**
$$\boxed{\;c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} \;\in\; \bigl[\tfrac{8}{9},\;8\bigr] \quad\text{for every }\chi\text{ in the cube-moment family.}\;}\tag{II.4.7}$$

In particular: $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} = O(1)$ uniformly in $\chi$, no $|q|$-dependence and no $|\tau|$-dependence.

#### (II.4.vi) Closure of Phase II — global $c_\chi$ assembled

Combining II.3.b, II.3.c, II.3.d, and II.4:

$$c_\chi \;=\; c_{\chi,\infty}\cdot c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}\cdot\biggl(\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}\biggr)\cdot\biggl(\prod_{\substack{\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2\\ \mathfrak{p}\text{ finite}}}c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}\biggr). \tag{II.4.8}$$

With place-by-place contributions:

| Place | Factor | Reference | $\chi$-aspect size |
|-------|--------|-----------|--------------------|
| $\infty$ | $c_{\chi,\infty} = \tau/(128\pi\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2)$ | (II.3.d.17) | $\sim \|\tau\|^2/(64\pi^2)$ (spectrally averaged) |
| $\mathfrak{p}_2$ | $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} \in [8/9, 8]$ | (II.4.7) | $O(1)$ |
| $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ (ramified) | $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} \sim q_F$ per place | (II.3.c.16)–(II.3.c.17) | $\prod \sim \|q\|^{1+o(1)}$ |
| $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ (unramified) | $L_\mathfrak{p}(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ | (II.3.b.6) | $\prod \sim \|q\|^{o(1)}$ |

**Global $\chi$-aspect size:**
$$\boxed{\;|c_\chi| \;\asymp\; |q|^{1+o(1)}\cdot |\tau|^2 \qquad\text{(spectrally averaged, leading order)}.\;}\tag{II.4.9}$$

This is exactly the size needed to enter Phase IV: the cubic moment $\sum_\chi|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^3$ is bounded by $|q|$-many terms each of size $c_\chi\cdot(\text{Fourier-coefficient stuff})$; the $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ from $c_\chi$ saturates the conjectured cube-moment bound, and the spectral $|\tau|^2$ aligns with the analytic-conductor growth (II.3.d.18 R6).

**Phase II is now structurally complete.** The Bianchi-Waldspurger formula $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2 = c_\chi|a_\chi(1)|^2/\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2$ with explicit $c_\chi$-factorization (II.4.8) is in place, subject to the documented caveats (CV-1 through CV-7 at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$, CV-d1 through CV-d6 at $\infty$, CV-2.1/CV-2.2 below at $\mathfrak{p}_2$). Phase IV (cube-moment via theta unfolding + Phase III ★) is now unblocked from the Phase II side.

#### Remarks on II.4

- **(R1) Why PSS is not load-bearing here.** Pitale–Saha–Schmidt 2014 "Transfer of Siegel cusp forms" (and the local analog Schmidt 2002, Saha 2015) provides explicit paramodular newvectors for *ramified-supercuspidal* representations of $GL_2$ over dyadic local fields. Our $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified principal series (the cube-moment family hypothesis $(q,\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$ forces $\chi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ unramified, $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ unramified, hence $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ unramified). PSS reduces to the spherical case here. In Phase V.1 (cube-free $q$ with $\mathfrak{p}_2\mid q$), PSS becomes load-bearing — that is the natural place to invoke the full PSS machinery.
- **(R2) Dyadic measure cancellation.** The dyadic discriminant $\mathfrak{d}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/\mathbb{Q}_2} = \mathfrak{p}_2^2$ contributes a factor of $|\mathfrak{p}_2^2|^{1/2} = 1/2$ to $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}})$ in the Tate self-dual convention (II.1.c C3) — *not* $1/4$ as the placeholder text in `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` stated (typo: that file conflated $|\mathfrak{d}|$ with $|\mathfrak{d}|^{1/2}$; correction recorded in the session log). This volume factor enters the Whittaker norm $\|W^\circ_{\mathfrak{p}_2}\|^2$ and the spherical-reference norm identically, so the ratio $J_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$ is preserved.
- **(R3) Compatibility with $c_F$ — NOT a double-count (clarified per skeptic Round 1 C2).** The global Hoffstein–Lockhart constant $c_F = 4/\pi$ for $\mathbb{Q}(i)$ (II.3.a.9) absorbs the $\zeta_F$-residue $\pi/4 = \pi/(2\sqrt{|D|})$ at $\infty$ in II.3.d (CV-d6 convention). This is a *global residue normalization* — a single overall constant, not a per-place factor. The dyadic Euler factor (II.4.7) here is the **separate** $\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi$-contribution at $\mathfrak{p}_2$, intrinsic to $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$, with no overlap. Earlier draft conflated "$\sqrt{|D|}$ structurally encodes the dyadic prime" (a true but uninformative statement about $\mathbb{Q}(i)$'s discriminant) with "$c_F$ already counts the $\mathfrak{p}_2$-place" (false — $c_F$ is a global constant, not a per-place piece). So (II.4.5)/(II.4.7) are independent and *not* double-counting $c_F$.
- **(R4) Cross-check at $\alpha^2 = 1$ — finite upper endpoint, not a divergence (clarified per skeptic Round 1 C5).** When $\alpha^2 \to 1$, the *local* Euler factor (II.4.4) attains the finite upper endpoint $(1 - 1/2)^{-1}\cdot(1-1/2)^{-1}\cdot(1-1/2)^{-1} = 8$ — there is no local divergence. The *global* $L_E(s,\chi^2)$ has a genuine pole at $s = 1$ when $\chi^2 = \mathbf{1}$ globally (the case excluded by II.3.b CORE-8 hypothesis $\chi^2 \neq \mathbf{1}$). The Euler factor (II.4.4) evaluates this $L$-factor at $s = 1$ in the local Euler product; when $\chi^2 = \mathbf{1}$ globally the *product* over all $\mathfrak{p}$ blows up (Euler-product becomes $\zeta_F(s)$ near $s=1$), but the *individual local factor* at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ remains finite (8). The cube-moment family's "$\chi^2 \neq \mathbf{1}$" generic hypothesis avoids the global pole; (II.4.7) is uniform across the family. Earlier draft incorrectly wrote "split formula diverges as ... 8" — corrected.
- **(R5) Phase-V outlook.** When $\mathfrak{p}_2\mid q$ (Phase V.1), $\chi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is ramified — the PSS prescription becomes load-bearing, and II.4 reopens with a paramodular-newvector $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ of level $\mathfrak{p}_2^{c(\chi_{\mathfrak{p}_2})}$. The expected outcome: $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}^{V.1} \sim q_F$ at each ramified $\mathfrak{p}_2\mid q$, paralleling the ramified-odd case (II.3.c.16). Out of scope here.

#### Skeptic-flagged caveats (Round 1, this chunk)

- **(CV-2.1) Lapid–Mao normalizing constant at $\mathfrak{p}_2$.** Parallel to CV-d5: identifying $\alpha_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(W) = |W(1)|^2/\|W\|^2$ with the Lapid–Mao regularized period integral requires verification that the normalizing constant equals $1$ on the spherical vector. Deferred. Global product invariance argument (CV-d5) applies.
- **(CV-2.2) Weil-index $\gamma_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$ in the inert dyadic case.** The Weil index $\gamma_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(\psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}, V_2)$ for $V_2 = E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ at the dyadic prime: standard references (Rao 1993, Kudla 1996) give $\gamma_v = 1$ for unramified $V$ at unramified-finite-place; dyadic ramification of the *ambient field* $F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ may introduce a sign correction of order $\pm 1$ that hasn't been explicitly verified here. If the correction is $-1$, it would flip the $w$-eigenvalue from $+1$ to $-1$, with downstream effects on the test function's behavior. **Mitigation:** the explicit calculation in II.4.iv goes through (II.4.3) via the *unification formula* (II.3.b.6), which is intrinsic to the local rep and *independent* of the $w$-eigenvalue sign at $\mathfrak{p}_2$. So even if CV-2.2 resolves to $\gamma_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = -1$, (II.4.7) is unaffected.
- **(CV-2.3) Fourier non-self-duality of $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$.** Unlike at unramified-odd places where $\widehat{\phi_\mathfrak{p}} = \phi_\mathfrak{p}$, at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ we have $\widehat{\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}(x) = \mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}})\mathbf{1}_{\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}}(x) \neq \phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(x)$. This is *fine* — Fourier self-duality is not required for the test function in II.1.d; only Fourier-square-invariance $\widehat{\widehat{\phi}} = \phi$ matters for the theta-kernel Poisson-summation step (II.1.b Step A), and that is preserved at $\mathfrak{p}_2$. But it means the depth-$0$ test function differs from the depth-$-2$ shifted version by a non-trivial Atkin-Lehner-style translate (analogous to II.1.d.bis.2 at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$). Since $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified, the spherical newvector is unique and lives at depth $0$; the depth-$-2$ shift is just $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ with the volume Jacobian, not a separate newvector.

#### Done-criterion for chunk II.4.

Achieved (subject to CV-2.1 through CV-2.5 caveats):
(i) (II.4.i) — unramified-character claim at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ proven from the cube-moment family hypothesis $(q,\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$;
(ii) test function $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}}$ specified, $K_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$-spherical properties verified explicitly (II.4.ii) with the dyadic-conductor $\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}$ Weil-rep checks made explicit;
(iii) (II.4.2)–(II.4.3) — $J_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$ and boxed $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} = L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ via direct transfer of the II.3.b unification formula to the dyadic prime;
(iv) (II.4.4)–(II.4.5) — split/inert explicit Euler factors at $q_F = 2$ in closed form;
(v) (II.4.6)–(II.4.7) — boxed uniform bound $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} \in [8/9, 8]$ across the family;
(vi) (II.4.8)–(II.4.9) — boxed global $c_\chi$ assembly with place-by-place size table and confirmed $|c_\chi| \asymp |q|^{1+o(1)}|\tau|^2$ leading-order size;
(vii) R2 corrects the placeholder typo in `bot/longterm/cubic-moment.md` ($\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}) = 1/2$, not $1/4$);
(viii) R1, R5 explain why PSS is not load-bearing here but will be in Phase V.1;
(ix) **Phase II structurally closed.**

Not achieved (deferred): (x) Lapid–Mao constant pin-down at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ — CV-2.1; (xi) explicit Weil-index sign verification at the dyadic inert case — CV-2.2; (xii) PSS prescription for the Phase V.1 ramified-dyadic case — out of scope; (xiii) extension of (II.4.7) to spectrally-averaged $|\chi|^2$ moment estimates as input to Phase IV — handled in Phase IV bookkeeping. Forward chunk: **III.1.a (start of Phase III)** — state the amplified second moment for the $GL_2/\mathbb{Q}(i)$ family. Alternative: combined cross-check of all of Phase II against FH 1995 over-$\mathbb{Q}$ Eq. (1.10)+(1.13) (a "Phase II audit" chunk).

## Open sub-questions

- **Q1 (II.1.b — RESOLVED 2026-05-15 session 2; moderate-growth follow-up RESOLVED 2026-05-15 session 5).** Absolute convergence + left $SL_2(F) \times O(V)(F)$-automorphy verified in Proposition (II.1.b). Moderate growth $|\Theta(g, h; \phi)| \ll_\phi H(g)$ uniformly in $h$ on the compact $[O(V_2)]$ verified in Proposition (II.1.e); see §Moderate growth (II.1.e). Equivariance under the right adelic action holds by construction.
- **Q2 (II.1.c — RESOLVED 2026-05-15 session 3).** Pinning down the metaplectic cocycle for $\widetilde{SL}_2(F_v)$ is **moot for this project**. Per Convention C1 in the Conventions sheet, the active pair is $(SL_2, O(V_2))$ with $V_2 = E$ ($\dim 2$ even); the Weil representation descends to $SL_2$ and the metaplectic cocycle plays no role. The question would re-enter only if we returned to Direction II ($V_3$, $\dim 3$ odd), which is dropped per SK-2.
- **Q3 (II.1.d — PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-05-15 session 4; II.1.d.bis depth-0 ansatz 2026-05-16 session 8; II.1.d.bis.2 Casselman reversal RESOLVED 2026-05-16 session 9; dyadic $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ still deferred to II.4).** Test function $\phi = \otimes_v \phi_v$ specified at all non-dyadic places:
    - $\phi_\infty(x) = e^{-2\pi q_\infty(x)}$ with $q_\infty$ the positive-definite $\mathbb{R}$-quadratic form $|\sigma_1 x|^2_\mathbb{C} + |\sigma_2 x|^2_\mathbb{C}$ on $E_\infty \cong \mathbb{R}^4$ (not the Galois-norm $\mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}$ which is $\mathbb{C}$-valued — see §Test function notation pitfall);
    - $\phi_\mathfrak{p}(x) = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}(x)$ at $\mathfrak{p} \nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$;
    - $\phi_\mathfrak{p}(x) = \chi_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}(x)\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x)$ at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ — the unique-up-to-scalar Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector (Casselman 1973 uniqueness, II.1.d.bis.2). The Schrödinger Fourier transform $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \gamma_\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{G}(\chi,\psi)\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ at the depth-$-2$ shell is the *Atkin-Lehner translate*, not a separate newvector; the session-8 "$\phi^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$ at depth $-2$" conjecture was a mis-identification (reversed in II.1.d.bis.2). The local $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ is the correct ramified-prime closed form, with structural vanishing at $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) > 0$ matching FH 1995's coprime-to-conductor feature. The Gauss-sum scalar $\mathcal{G}$ with $|\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1}$ enters the Bianchi-Waldspurger constant $c_\chi$ (via the Atkin-Lehner pairing in II.3), not the local $W_\mathfrak{p}$.
    - $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ at the dyadic prime (Pitale–Saha–Schmidt paramodular analog): **deferred** to II.4.
    Properties verified: Schwartz–Bruhat, $K^{\mathrm{ur}}$-spherical, Fourier-self-dual, archimedean Weyl-eigenvalue $+1$, $K_1(\mathfrak{p})$-newvector at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$; convention $\chi|_{\mathbb{A}_F^\times} = \chi_{E/F}$ (not 1) — corrected in II.1.d.bis from a previous-chunk overstatement; retroactive consistency checked at split and inert unramified $\mathfrak{p}$.
- **Q4 (II.2.a — RESOLVED 2026-05-15 session 6; II.2.b unramified-data local factorization RESOLVED 2026-05-15 session 7; ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ contributions still deferred).** The Fourier expansion of $\Theta_\chi(g)$ along the unipotent radical $N(\mathbb{A}_F) \subset B(SL_2)$ is computed in §Fourier expansion (II.2.a); the local factorization of the resulting orbital integral and its explicit evaluation at all unramified places is computed in §Local factorization (II.2.b). Outputs: **orbit-unfolded form** $a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1}\xi_n) d\eta$ on $n \in F^\times \cap \mathrm{Nm}(E^\times)$ (II.2.a); **Factorization Lemma** $a_\chi(n; g) = \prod_v W_v(g_v; \xi_n)$ via restricted-product formalism (II.2.b); **closed unramified factors** $W_\mathfrak{p}$ = 1 at inert $\mathfrak{p}$, $W_\mathfrak{p} = \sum_{k=-b}^a \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2k}$ at split $\mathfrak{p}$ (Satake parameter $\alpha_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p})$), $W_\infty = (|z_1|/|z_2|)^{i\tau/2} K_{i\tau}(4\pi|n|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})$ Bessel-K (II.2.b parts (a)–(c)). **Vanishing dichotomy:** $a_\chi(n) = 0$ unless $n = 0$ or $n \in \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(E^\times)$. Friedberg–Hoffstein-shape closed form realized as the product of these unramified factors with placeholders at $\mathfrak{p} \mid q\mathfrak{p}_2$, completed once II.1.d.bis ($q$-newform Gauss sum) and II.4 (dyadic) are done.
- **Q5 (II.1.c — MOOT 2026-05-15 session 3).** The $\widetilde{SL}_2$ vs $\mathrm{Mp}_2$ convention question is moot per Convention C1 (no metaplectic cover used in this project). Historical record preserved.
- **Q6 (II.3+II.4 — PHASE II STRUCTURALLY CLOSED 2026-05-16 session 14 / II.3.a framework + statement + II.3.b unramified local factors + II.3.c ramified $J_\mathfrak{p}$ verified at leading order + II.3.d archimedean $J_\infty$ + $c_{\chi,\infty}$ explicit + II.4 dyadic $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ explicit).** **II.4 (this session) closed the dyadic factor $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$:** the cube-moment family hypothesis $(q,\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$ forces $\chi$ unramified at $\mathfrak{p}_2$ and $E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}/F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ unramified, hence $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified principal series (II.4.i); test function $\phi_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_{E_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}}$ verified $K_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$-spherical with explicit dyadic-conductor $\psi_{\mathfrak{p}_2}$ conductor $\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}$ tracking (II.4.ii); II.3.b unification formula transfers directly to give **boxed $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} = L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ (II.4.3)** with $J_{\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$; explicit Euler factors at $q_F = 2$: **split $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}^{\mathrm{split}} = 2/|1 - \alpha^2/2|^2$ (II.4.4)**, **inert $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}^{\mathrm{inert}} = 8/9$ (II.4.5)**; **boxed uniform bound $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2} \in [8/9, 8]$ (II.4.7)** across the cube-moment family — clean $O(1)$ contribution, no $|q|$ or $|\tau|$ dependence; **boxed global $c_\chi$ assembly (II.4.8)** with place-by-place size table confirming $|c_\chi| \asymp |q|^{1+o(1)}|\tau|^2$ (II.4.9) leading-order spectrally-averaged size. PSS paramodular technology not load-bearing in II.4 (R1) because $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified; PSS becomes load-bearing only in Phase V.1 (cube-free $q$ with $\mathfrak{p}_2\mid q$). Cubic-moment.md placeholder typo corrected (R2: $\mathrm{vol}(\mathcal{O}_{F_{\mathfrak{p}_2}}) = 1/2$, not $1/4$). New "Fourier expansion (II.2.a — orbit-unfolded form)" subsection inserted between II.1.e and "Open sub-questions". **Proposition (II.2.a)** computes the $n$-th Fourier coefficient $a_\chi(n; g)$ of $\Theta_\chi(g; \phi)$ along $N(\mathbb{A}_F)$. **Vanishing dichotomy:** $a_\chi(n; g) = 0$ unless $n = 0$ or $n \in \mathrm{Nm}_{E/F}(E^\times)$ (since $V_2 = (E, \mathrm{Nm})$ is anisotropic). **Orbit-unfolded form** on $n \in F^\times \cap \mathrm{Nm}(E^\times)$, picking any $\xi_n \in E^\times$ with $\mathrm{Nm}(\xi_n) = n$:
$$a_\chi(n; g) = \int_{E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)} \chi(\eta) \, (\omega_\psi(g)\phi)(\eta^{-1} \xi_n) \, d\eta,$$
*no stabilizer factor* — $E^1(F)$ acts simply transitively (free orbit) on the norm-fiber. Three-step proof in $[E^1]$-coordinates: (Step 1) Fubini on $(F\backslash\mathbb{A}_F)\times[E^1]$ + uniform-on-compacta Schwartz convergence (II.1.b) justify swap of integrals + lattice sum; (Step 2) Weil-rep at $n(u)$ + $E^1$-invariance of $\mathrm{Nm}$ + character orthogonality $\int_{F\backslash\mathbb{A}_F}\psi((Q-n)u)du = \mathbf{1}_{Q=n}$ cut to $\mathrm{Nm}(x)=n$; (Step 3) standard $\Gamma$-unfolding for $\Gamma = E^1(F)$ discrete in $E^1(\mathbb{A}_F)$. Crucial setup observation: $[O(V_2)] = [E^1]$ as adelic quotients (Galois generator $\sigma$ lies in $O(V_2)(F)$ globally, cancelling left/right), so $\int_{[O(V_2)]} \chi(h)dh = \int_{[E^1]}\chi(\eta)d\eta$ — eliminates the artificial $\chi(\sigma)$-extension. Five remarks (R1)–(R5): Friedberg–Hoffstein symmetrized form $\{\xi_n, \bar\xi_n\}$; local factorization $W_v(g_v;\xi_n)$ preview (substance of II.2.b); central-character compatibility for $\chi_V = \chi_{E/F}$; connection to Bianchi Waldspurger $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$ via $\xi_1 = 1$ (clean, no $\tfrac12$-factor); $\delta=1$ case recorded as non-load-bearing.
