- 2026-05-15 (session `2026-05-15T21-Z`): chunk II.2.b executed. New "Local factorization (II.2.b — orbital integral $W_v$ at unramified places)" subsection inserted between II.2.a and §Open sub-questions. **Factorization Lemma** identifies the adelic orbital integral from II.2.a as a restricted product $a_\chi(n;g) = \prod_v W_v(g_v;\xi_n)$ of local pieces $W_v = \int_{E^1(F_v)}\chi_v(\eta)(\omega_{\psi_v}(g_v)\phi_v)(\eta^{-1}\xi_n)d\eta_v$. **Proposition (II.2.b)** computes $W_v$ at every unramified place: **(a) inert finite $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$:** $W_\mathfrak{p}(g_\mathfrak{p};\xi_n) = \mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}}$ (constant under the inert-normalization $\mathrm{vol}(E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})) = 1$, regardless of $v_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n)$ since $E^1\subset\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}^\times$). **(b) split finite $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$:** parametrize $E^1(F_\mathfrak{p})\cong F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$ via $(t,t^{-1})\leftrightarrow t$, write $\xi_n = (\alpha,\beta)$ with $a = v_\mathfrak{p}(\alpha)$, $b = v_\mathfrak{p}(\beta)$, $c = a+b = v_\mathfrak{p}(n)$, Satake parameter $\alpha_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p})$; then $W_\mathfrak{p} = \sum_{k=-b}^a\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2k} = (\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2(a+1)}-\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-2b})/(\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2-1)$ (or $c+1$ when $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2 = 1$). **(c) archimedean $\infty$:** Bessel-K. With $\xi_n = (z_1,z_2)\in\mathbb{C}^\times\times\mathbb{C}^\times$ ($z_1z_2=n$), archimedean spectral parameter $(k,\tau)$ from $\chi^+_\infty(z) = (z/|z|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})^k|z|_\mathbb{C}^{i\tau/2}$, and $g_\infty = 1$: $W_\infty = 0$ unless $k = 0$; otherwise $W_\infty = (|z_1|_\mathbb{C}/|z_2|_\mathbb{C})^{i\tau/2} K_{i\tau}(4\pi|n|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})$. Setup at split $\mathfrak{p}$ uses self-dual + type-I identities reducing to $\chi^-_\mathfrak{p} = (\chi^+_\mathfrak{p})^{-1}$, hence $\chi_\mathfrak{p}|_{E^1}(t,t^{-1}) = (\chi^+_\mathfrak{p})^2(t)$ — a Satake-parameter-$\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^2$ unramified character of $F_\mathfrak{p}^\times$; same at $\infty$. Three proofs given: (a) sphericality + unramified-trivial-character; (b) integrating $\chi^+_\mathfrak{p}(t)^2$ over the $\eta^{-1}\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_{E_\mathfrak{p}}$ range $v_\mathfrak{p}(t)\in[-b,a]$; (c) polar coordinates $t = re^{i\theta}$ + $\theta$-integral picks out $k=0$ + $u = r^2$ substitution + GR 3.471.9 (modified Bessel-K integral representation). **Corollary** (Friedberg–Hoffstein-shape closed form) presents $a_\chi(n;g)$ as a product of the unramified factors with placeholders at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ (to be filled by II.1.d.bis and II.4). **Five Remarks (R1)–(R5):** (R1) the simple "$a_\chi(n) = c\chi(\xi_n)|\xi_n|^{-1/2}G_n$" Friedberg–Hoffstein over-$\mathbb{Q}$ schematic does not directly apply to Bianchi: split-prime factor is a *generalized Hecke-like* $\sum\alpha^{2k}$, not $\chi(\xi_n)|\xi_n|^{1/2}$; (R2) Satake-parameter-$\alpha^2$ (not $\alpha$) Hecke-like factor at split $\mathfrak{p}$ is *expected* — $a_\chi$ is a theta-Fourier coefficient, not a Hecke eigenvalue of $\mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$, and the squared-parameter shift is consistent with the Bianchi-Waldspurger $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$ structure; (R3) symmetry under $\xi_n\to\bar\xi_n$ at each place — verified as place-by-place check on the II.2.a (R1) global symmetry, with local twist factor $\alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{2(b-a)}$ (resp. $(|z_2|/|z_1|)^{i\tau}$) at finite split (resp. $\infty$) primes, multiplying globally to $\chi(\eta_0) = 1$; (R4) $k = 0$ spectral support at $\infty$ matches the Maass-form (vs holomorphic discrete-series) character of $\mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ on $GL_2/F$; (R5) sphericality caveat at $\infty$ — Prop. (II.2.b)(c) is stated at $g_\infty = 1$ only; for general $g_\infty \in SU(2)$, $W_\infty$ involves the appropriate minimal-$K$-type matrix coefficient, deferred to II.3. Q4 updated to reflect II.2.b RESOLVED at unramified data. Outcome: PROGRESS. New "Atkin-Lehner translate $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$ and Casselman reversal (II.1.d.bis.2)" subsection inserted as a §-subsection of II.1.d.bis, directly between the II.1.d.bis "Done-criterion" and "## Open sub-questions". **REVERSAL of session-8 mis-identification:** the depth-0 $\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ IS the unique-up-to-scalar Friedberg–Hoffstein newvector at $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$. The session-8 "conjectured depth-$-2$ newvector $\phi^{\mathrm{FH}\,?}$" is *not* a separate newvector — it is $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}$, the Atkin-Lehner translate. **Casselman 1973 uniqueness:** the local component $\pi_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} = \mathrm{Ind}_B^{GL_2}(\chi_\mathfrak{p}, \chi^\sigma_\mathfrak{p})$ is a ramified principal series with both inducing characters of conductor $\mathfrak{p}^1$ over $F_\mathfrak{p}$ (Type-I); conductor of $\pi$ is $\mathfrak{p}^1$ and $\dim\pi^{K_1(\mathfrak{p})} = 1$. Restriction to $SL_2$ does not change the 1-dimensionality. A newvector at conductor $\mathfrak{p}^1$ in a ramified principal series is NOT generically an Atkin-Lehner eigenvector — it transforms into the $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant line under $w$, with a Gauss-sum prefactor. **Explicit computation $\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p} = \gamma_\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{G}(\chi,\psi)\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$** derived: $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}(x) := \chi^{-1}(\varpi x)\mathbf{1}_{\varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times}(x)$ (Atkin-Lehner-translated function, depth-$-2$ shell, $K_1^{op}(\mathfrak{p})$-invariant), $\mathcal{G}(\chi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p}) := q_F^{-1/2}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(D)G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}$ with $G_a^{\mathrm{raw}} = \int_{\mathcal{O}_F^\times}\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(a)\psi(2a/(D\varpi))da$, derived from the session-8 parity-of-$m$ Fourier-transform calculation at $m = -2$ + change of variable using $\chi(\bar y) = \chi^{-1}(y)$ (conjugate-self-duality) + $\chi(\varpi)^2 = 1$ (Type-I, order-2 quadratic). **Modulus calculation:** classical Plancherel on $\mathbb{F}_{q_F}^\times$ paired with non-trivial $\psi^{(D)}_\mathfrak{p}$ gives $|G_a^{\mathrm{raw}}| = q_F^{-1/2}$, hence $|\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1/2}\cdot q_F^{-1/2} = q_F^{-1}$. **Weil-isometry cross-check** confirms $|\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1}$ is *forced* by $\|\omega_\psi(w)\phi_\mathfrak{p}\| = \|\phi_\mathfrak{p}\|$ (independent verification — the modulus is determined two ways and they agree). **$K_1^{op}$-invariance of $\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$** verified via conjugation $w^{-1}K_1^{op}w = K_1$ + Weil-rep relation. **$\phi^{\mathrm{AL}}$ NOT $K_1$-invariant** confirmed by direct $n(b)$ check: for $x \in \varpi^{-1}\mathcal{O}_E^\times$, $b\mathrm{Nm}(x) \in \varpi^{-2}\mathcal{O}_F^\times \not\subset \mathcal{O}_F$, so $\psi(b\mathrm{Nm}(x)) \neq 1$. **$W_\mathfrak{p}$ confirmation:** $W_\mathfrak{p}(1;\xi_n) = \chi^{-1}_\mathfrak{p}(\xi_n)\mathbf{1}_{\xi_n\in\mathcal{O}_E^\times}$ (with vol $E^1 = 1$ normalization) is the correct ramified-prime $W$, with structural vanishing at $v_\mathfrak{p}(n) > 0$ being the *standard FH coprime-to-conductor feature* (not a deficiency). **Where Gauss sum enters Bianchi-Waldspurger:** $\mathcal{G}$ does NOT appear in $W_\mathfrak{p}$ or $a_\chi(1)$; it enters $c_\chi$ in the Bianchi-Waldspurger constant via the Atkin-Lehner-translated pairing in II.3. Global product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}|\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}|^{-1} = |q|_F^{1+o(1)}$, providing the dominant $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size in Phase IV. **Six remarks (R1)–(R6):** (R1) reversal disowning + correct interpretation; (R2) Casselman 1973 citation; (R3) $|\mathcal{G}| = q_F^{-1}$ explanation via volume-Jacobian + classical-Gauss; (R4) entry into $c_\chi$ in II.3; (R5) FH 1995 over $\mathbb{Q}$ analog (cusp-$\infty$ "$\chi(\sqrt{n})$" matches our $\chi^{-1}(\xi_n)$); (R6) $\xi_n$-shift invariance. New "Bianchi-Waldspurger pairing setup (II.3.a — framework, identification of $\Theta_\chi$ inside $\pi_\chi$, and statement)" subsection inserted between II.1.d.bis.2 Done-criterion and §Open sub-questions. **Framework setup:** auto-induced cuspidal representation $\pi_\chi := \mathrm{AI}_{E/F}(\chi)$ on $GL_2(\mathbb{A}_F)$ via Arthur–Clozel 1989, irreducible cuspidal under $\chi \neq \chi^{-1}$ (generic in cube-moment family); $L(s,\pi_\chi) = L(s,\chi)L(s,\bar\chi)$ factorization gives $L(\tfrac12,\pi_\chi) = |L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$ (II.3.a.1) — the foundational identity reformulating $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2$ as a single $GL_2/F$ central value. **Petersson pairing** on cuspidal $L^2([GL_2(F)])$ with trivial central character; $\widetilde\Theta_\chi(g) := \Theta_\chi(z_0^{-1}g)$ with no $\chi_{E/F}$ prefactor (R1: determinant of $\mathrm{Ind}_{W_E}^{W_F}\chi$ trivial under Type-I, so $\omega_{\pi_\chi} = \mathbf{1}$ — corrected from initial draft). Cuspidality + moderate growth (II.1.e) give finite $\langle\widetilde\Theta_\chi,\widetilde\Theta_\chi\rangle$. **Multiplicity-one identification:** $V_{\widetilde\Theta_\chi} = \pi_\chi$ via local Howe duality (Howe–Piatetski-Shapiro 1979 / Roberts–Schmidt 2007) + Jacquet–Langlands global multiplicity-one; hence $\widetilde\Theta_\chi = \lambda_\chi\cdot f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$ for unique $\lambda_\chi \in \mathbb{C}^\times$, with $f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}$ the $L^2$-normalized newvector of $\pi_\chi$. Yields $\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2 = |\lambda_\chi|^2$ and $a_\chi(1) = \lambda_\chi \cdot a_{f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}}(1)$, so $|a_\chi(1)|^2/\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2 = |a_{f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}}(1)|^2$. **Hoffstein–Lockhart first-coefficient formula** (II.3.a.6) gives $|a_{f_\chi^{\mathrm{new}}}(1)|^2 = 2/(L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi))$; auto-induced adjoint factorization $L(s,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = L(s,\chi^2)L(s,\chi_{E/F})$ (Gelbart–Jacquet 1978). **Statement (II.3):** $|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2 = c_\chi|a_\chi(1)|^2/\|\widetilde\Theta_\chi\|^2$ with $c_\chi = (1/2)\cdot L(1,\chi^2)\cdot L(1,\chi_{E/F})\cdot\prod_v J_v(\pi_\chi)$ (II.3.a.9) — derived by combining (II.3.a.1)+(II.3.a.6)+(II.3.a.7) and noting $L(\tfrac12,\pi_\chi)/|L(\tfrac12,\chi)|^2 = 1$. **Local factorization plan:** $c_\chi = \prod_v c_{\chi,v}$ with $c_{\chi,v} = L_v(1,\chi^2)L_v(1,\chi_{E/F})J_v(\pi_\chi)/2_v$ (factor of $1/2$ absorbed at $\infty$). Per-place sketch: at unramified $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$ explicit Euler factors + $J_\mathfrak{p}=1$ (II.3.b); at ramified $\mathfrak{p}\mid q$ trivial $L$-factors + $J_\mathfrak{p} = q_F^{-1}|\mathcal{G}_\mathfrak{p}|^{-2} = q_F^{-1}\cdot q_F^2 = q_F$ — global product $\prod_{\mathfrak{p}\mid q}c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}} = |q|_F$ providing dominant $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ size in Phase IV (II.3.c); archimedean $\Gamma$-factors + Bessel-function value $|K_{i\tau}(4\pi)|^{-2}$-like (II.3.d); dyadic deferred to II.4. **Six remarks (R1)–(R6):** (R1) determinant calc correcting central character extension; (R2) conductor reconciliation $\mathrm{cond}(\pi_\chi)_\mathfrak{p} = \mathfrak{p}^2$ via tame $d_{E_\mathfrak{p}/F_\mathfrak{p}} = 1$ (Serre VI Prop 13), confirming II.1.d.bis.2 R2; (R3) Phase-IV $|q|^{1+\epsilon}$ trace; (R4) reduction to Hoffstein–Lockhart; (R5) caveat on $a_\chi(1)$ definition; (R6) FH 1995 comparison — $\sqrt D$-factor matches our $|q|_F^{1/2}$. New "Local factor $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$ (II.3.b — explicit Euler factors)" subsection inserted between II.3.a Done-criterion and §Open sub-questions. **Two cases by splitting type of $\mathfrak{p}$ in $E$.** (i) **Split** $\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_E = w_1w_2$: with split Satake parameter $\alpha_\mathfrak{p} = \chi(\varpi_{w_1})$, Type-I gives $\chi(\varpi_{w_2}) = \alpha_\mathfrak{p}^{-1}$ (since $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}$ trivial at split unramified); $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{split}} = (1-\alpha^2/q_\mathfrak{p})^{-1}(1-\alpha^{-2}/q_\mathfrak{p})^{-1}(1-1/q_\mathfrak{p})^{-1}$ (II.3.b.3). (ii) **Inert** $\mathfrak{p}\mathcal{O}_E = \mathfrak{P}$: Type-I + unramified $\chi_{E/F,\mathfrak{p}}(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = -1$ forces $\chi(\varpi_\mathfrak{p}) = -1$ — **the inert-prime Satake parameter is fixed at $-1$ for every $\chi$ in the family** (no $\chi$-dependence); $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{inert}} = (1-1/q_\mathfrak{p}^2)^{-1}(1+1/q_\mathfrak{p})^{-1} = (1-1/q_\mathfrak{p})^{-1}(1+1/q_\mathfrak{p})^{-2}$ (II.3.b.5). **Unification (II.3.b.6):** $c_{\chi,\mathfrak{p}}^{\mathrm{ur}} = L_\mathfrak{p}(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)$ at every unramified $\mathfrak{p}\nmid q\mathfrak{p}_2$, derived by computing local adjoint Satake parameters $(\alpha^2, 1, \alpha^{-2})$ at split and $(-1, 1, -1)$ at inert from the auto-induced Satake $(\alpha,\alpha^{-1})$ (split) / $(i,-i)$ (inert), and matching explicitly against (II.3.b.3) / (II.3.b.5). Sanity check ✓ at both cases (numerical-verified $\alpha = e^{0.7i}, q_\mathfrak{p}=5$). **Global $\chi$-aspect bound (II.3.b.8–9):** $c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}} = L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)/(L_{\mathfrak{p}_2}\cdot L_\infty)$ at adjoint = $|q|^{o(1)}$ via unconditional log-power bound $(\log|q|)^{-O(1)} \ll L(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) \ll (\log|q|)^{O(1)}$ (Hoffstein–Lockhart 1994 lower bound + Goldfeld–Hoffstein–Lieman 1994 zero-free region). **Confirms structurally** all dominant $|q|$-size of $c_\chi$ comes from ramified primes — substance of II.3.c. **Six remarks (R1)–(R6):** (R1) (II.3.b.6) is the clean form promised in II.3.a; (R2) Satake parameter at inert primes is intrinsic to $E/F$, independent of $\chi$; (R3) II.2.b/II.3.b consistency on the $\alpha^2$ doubling at split primes; (R4) FH 1995 over-$\mathbb{Q}$ analog; (R5) conductor invariance of $J_\mathfrak{p}$ at unramified $\mathfrak{p}$; (R6) convergence of $c_\chi^{\mathrm{ur}}$ at $s = 1$ for $\chi^2 \neq 1$. New "Local factor $c_{\chi,\infty}$ at $v = \infty$ (II.3.d — archimedean Whittaker pairing for the spherical principal series of $GL_2(\mathbb{C})$)" subsection inserted between II.3.c Done-criterion and §Open sub-questions. **Local data:** $F = \mathbb{Q}(i)$, $\infty$ complex, $E_\infty = \mathbb{C}\oplus\mathbb{C}$ (split), $\chi_{w_1}(z) = |z|^{i\tau}_\mathbb{C}$, $\chi_{w_2}(z) = |z|^{-i\tau}_\mathbb{C}$ (Type-I + Maass spherical $k = 0$); $\pi_{\chi,\infty}$ unramified principal series (II.3.d.1)–(II.3.d.2). **Archimedean adjoint $L$-factor (II.3.d.3)–(II.3.d.4):** $L_\infty(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi) = \Gamma_\mathbb{C}(1+2i\tau)\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(1)\Gamma_\mathbb{C}(1-2i\tau) = 2\tau/(\pi^2\sinh(2\pi\tau))$ via Satake parameters $(|\cdot|^{2i\tau},\mathbf{1},|\cdot|^{-2i\tau})$ + $|\Gamma(1+iy)|^2 = \pi y/\sinh(\pi y)$. **Spherical Bianchi Whittaker (II.3.d.5)–(II.3.d.6):** $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(\mathrm{diag}(y,1)) = |y|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2}K_{i\tau}(4\pi|y|_\mathbb{C}^{1/2})$ (Bruggeman–Motohashi 2003 §5; Lokvenec-Guleska 2007), value $W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty(1) = K_{i\tau}(4\pi)$. **Local Whittaker pairing (II.3.d.7)–(II.3.d.11):** $\langle W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty, W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}} = \tau/(16\sinh(\pi\tau))$ via Gradshteyn–Ryzhik 6.576.4 Bessel-$K^2$ identity $\int_0^\infty K_{i\tau}(u)^2 u\,du = |\Gamma(1+i\tau)|^2/2 = \pi\tau/(2\sinh(\pi\tau))$ + polar coordinates; hence $\alpha_\infty(W^{\mathrm{HL}}_\infty) = 16\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2/\tau$ (II.3.d.11). **Archimedean Macdonald reference (II.3.d.12)–(II.3.d.13):** $\alpha_\infty^{\mathrm{ref,sph}} = \zeta_\infty(2)/L_\infty(1,\mathrm{Ad}) = \sinh(2\pi\tau)/(4\tau)$ via Jacquet–Shalika 1981. **Boxed per-place $J_\infty$ (II.3.d.14):** $J_\infty(\pi_\chi) = \cosh(\pi\tau)/(32K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2)$ via half-angle identity $\sinh(2\pi\tau) = 2\sinh(\pi\tau)\cosh(\pi\tau)$. Spectral asymptotic (II.3.d.15): $\overline{J_\infty} \sim |\tau|e^{2\pi|\tau|}/(64\pi)$ on average — exponentially large, dual to exponential decay of $L_\infty(1,\mathrm{Ad})$. **Boxed local factor $c_{\chi,\infty}$ (II.3.d.16)–(II.3.d.17):** $c_{\chi,\infty} = L_\infty(1,\mathrm{Ad}\,\pi_\chi)\cdot J_\infty(\pi_\chi)/c_F = \tau/(128\pi\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(4\pi)^2)$ with $c_F = 4/\pi$ absorbed (via $\mathrm{res}_{s=1}\zeta_F(s) = \pi/4$ class-number formula for $\mathbb{Q}(i)$). **Spectral-aspect average (II.3.d.18):** $\overline{c_{\chi,\infty}} \sim |\tau|^2/(64\pi^2)$ — clean polynomial growth, exponential $L_\infty/J_\infty$ factors cancel exactly. **Six remarks (R1)–(R6):** (R1) why $J_\infty\neq 1$ at archimedean spherical (Macdonald-analog convention-dependent); (R2) compatibility with global H–L identity, $\tau = 0$ degeneracy caveat; (R3) cancellation of exponential growth in $L_\infty\cdot J_\infty$ leaving polynomial $|\tau|^2$; (R4) FH 1995 Eq. (1.13) over-$\mathbb{Q}$ analog $\tau/(2\pi\sinh(\pi\tau)K_{i\tau}(2\pi)^2)$ matches structural form $\tau/(\sinh(\pi\tau)K^2)$ verbatim, constants differ by $|\cdot|_\mathbb{C}$ vs $|\cdot|_\mathbb{R}$ specialization; (R5) $c_F = 4/\pi$ as residue contribution naturally absorbed at $\infty$; (R6) chunk-chain location — penultimate Phase-II chunk, only II.4 dyadic remains. **Skeptic Round 1 raised 4 CORE issues** (C1 factor-of-4 in Bessel asymptotic; C2 Lapid–Mao $\alpha$ vs evaluation-at-1 ratio; C3 $c_F$ placement at $\infty$ is convention; C4 wrong Jacquet–Shalika citation for archimedean Macdonald). **All 4 CORE addressed in source:** C1 arithmetic corrected throughout ((II.3.d.15a)–(II.3.d.15)+(II.3.d.18); the average asymptotic shifted from $|\tau|^2/(16\pi^2)$ to $|\tau|^2/(64\pi^2)$); C2 documented as new caveat CV-d5 (Lapid–Mao normalizing constant deferred, global product invariant); C3 documented as new caveat CV-d6 ($c_F$ placement convention, global $c_\chi$ invariant); C4 citation corrected to Stade 2002 / Sakellaridis–Venkatesh 2017 in (II.3.d.12) prose. New "Local factor $c_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}_2}$ at the dyadic prime $\\mathfrak{p}_2 = (1+i)$ (II.4 — unramified spherical rep with dyadic measure normalization)" subsection inserted between II.3.d Done-criterion and \§Open sub-questions. **PHASE II CLOSED.** **Key structural observation:** the cube-moment family hypothesis $(q,\\mathfrak{p}_2) = 1$ forces $\\chi$ unramified at $\\mathfrak{p}_2$ (II.4.i), so $\\pi_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}_2}$ is unramified principal series — Pitale–Saha–Schmidt paramodular technology is NOT load-bearing here (PSS becomes load-bearing only in Phase V.1 with cube-free $q$ and $\\mathfrak{p}_2\\mid q$); the dyadic computation reduces to the II.3.b unification formula applied at $q_F = 2$. **Test function (II.4.ii):** $\\phi_{\\mathfrak{p}_2} = \\mathbf{1}_{\\mathcal{O}_{E_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}}}$ with explicit Weil-rep verifications tracking the dyadic additive-character conductor $\\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}$ (II.1.c C2): $n(b)$-invariance via $\\mathcal{O}_{F_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}} \\subset \\mathfrak{p}_2^{-2}$ trivially; $m(a)$-invariance via $\\chi_{V_2,\\mathfrak{p}_2}$ unramified; $w$-eigenvalue +1 via $\\gamma_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}(\\psi, V_2) = 1$ (with CV-2.2 caveat for the sign verification); Fourier non-self-dual $\\widehat{\\phi_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}} \\neq \\phi_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}$ but $\\widehat{\\widehat{\\phi_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}}} = \\phi_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}$ preserved (CV-2.3). **Boxed unification (II.4.3):** $c_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}_2} = L_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}(1, \\mathrm{Ad}\\,\\pi_\\chi)$ with $J_{\\mathfrak{p}_2} = 1$ via direct transfer of II.3.b unification — same structural class as at unramified odd primes. **Explicit Euler factors at $q_F = 2$:** split $c_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}_2}^{\\mathrm{split}} = 2/|1 - \\alpha^2/2|^2$ (II.4.4); inert $c_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}_2}^{\\mathrm{inert}} = 8/9$ exactly (II.4.5). **Boxed uniform bound (II.4.7):** $c_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}_2} \\in [8/9, 8]$ for every $\\chi$ in the cube-moment family — clean $O(1)$ contribution, no $|q|$ or $|\\tau|$ dependence. **Boxed global assembly (II.4.8)–(II.4.9):** $c_\\chi = c_{\\chi,\\infty}\\cdot c_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}_2}\\cdot\\prod_{\\mathfrak{p}\\mid q}c_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}}\\cdot\\prod_{\\mathfrak{p}\\nmid q\\mathfrak{p}_2,\\text{ finite}}c_{\\chi,\\mathfrak{p}}$, with place-by-place size table: $\\infty$ gives $\\sim |\\tau|^2/(64\\pi^2)$ (II.3.d.18 spectrally averaged); $\\mathfrak{p}_2$ gives $O(1)$; ramified $\\mathfrak{p}\\mid q$ gives $\\sim q_F$ per place, product $\\sim |q|^{1+o(1)}$ (II.3.c); unramified finite gives $|q|^{o(1)}$ (II.3.b). Global size: $|c_\\chi| \\asymp |q|^{1+o(1)}|\\tau|^2$ leading order — exactly the conjectured Phase-IV size. **Cubic-moment.md placeholder corrected (R2):** $\\mathrm{vol}(\\mathcal{O}_{F_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}}) = |\\mathfrak{d}_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}|^{1/2} = 1/2$, not 1/4 (the placeholder text in cubic-moment.md conflated $|\\mathfrak{d}|$ with its square root). **Caveats CV-2.1/2.2/2.3** document deferred items: Lapid–Mao normalizing constant at $\\mathfrak{p}_2$ (parallel to CV-d5); Weil-index sign at dyadic inert case (immaterial for II.4.7 via intrinsic-unification formula); Fourier non-self-duality of $\\phi_{\\mathfrak{p}_2}$ (load-bearing $\\widehat{\\widehat{\\,}} = \\mathrm{id}$ preserved).
